<li value="2"><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_b"><b><a href="#ref_b">^</a></b></span> <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Portugal" title="Constitution of Portugal">Portuguese Constitution adopted in 1976</a> with several subsequent minor revisions, between 1982 and 2005.</li>
<li value="3"><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_c"><b><a href="#ref_c">^</a></b></span> Before 2002, the <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_escudo" title="Portuguese escudo">escudo</a>.</li>

<p><b>Portugal</b> (<a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">Portuguese</a>: <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_Portuguese" title="Help:IPA for Portuguese">[pu…ætuÀà…£a…´]</a></span>), officially the <b>Portuguese Republic</b> (Portuguese: <span lang="pt"><i>Rep√∫blica Portuguesa</i></span>) (<a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">Portuguese</a>: <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_Portuguese" title="Help:IPA for Portuguese">[ Å…®'publik…ê pu…ætu'…£ez…ê]</a></span>), is a country on the <a href="/wiki/Iberian_Peninsula" title="Iberian Peninsula">Iberian Peninsula</a> in <a href="/wiki/Western_Europe" title="Western Europe">Southwestern Europe</a>. It is the westernmost country of <a href="/wiki/Mainland_Europe" class="mw-redirect" title="Mainland Europe">mainland Europe</a>. To the west and south it is bordered by the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">Atlantic Ocean</a> and to the east and north by <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Portugal%E2%80%93Spain_border" title="Portugal‚ÄìSpain border">Portugal‚ÄìSpain border</a> is 1,214 kilometres (754 <a href="/wiki/Mile" title="Mile">miles</a>) long and considered the longest uninterrupted border within the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>. The republic also includes the Atlantic <a href="/wiki/Archipelago" title="Archipelago">archipelagos</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Azores" title="Azores">Azores</a> and <a href="/wiki/Madeira" title="Madeira">Madeira</a>, both <a href="/wiki/Autonomous_regions_of_Portugal" class="mw-redirect" title="Autonomous regions of Portugal">autonomous regions</a> with their own <a href="/wiki/Regional_government" class="mw-redirect" title="Regional government">regional governments</a>.</p>
<p>The territory of modern Portugal has been continuously settled, invaded and fought over since <a href="/wiki/Prehistoric_Iberia" title="Prehistoric Iberia">prehistoric times</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Pre-Celtic" title="Pre-Celtic">Pre-Celts</a>, <a href="/wiki/Celts" title="Celts">Celts</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Carthage" title="Ancient Carthage">Carthaginians</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Republic" title="Roman Republic">Romans</a> were followed by the invasions of the <a href="/wiki/Visigoths" title="Visigoths">Visigothic</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Suebi" title="Suebi">Suebi</a> <a href="/wiki/Germanic_peoples" title="Germanic peoples">Germanic peoples</a>. In 711 the Iberian Peninsula was invaded by the <a href="/wiki/Moors" title="Moors">Moors</a>, making Portugal part of <a href="/wiki/Al_Andalus" class="mw-redirect" title="Al Andalus">Muslim Al Andalus</a>. Portugal was born as result of the Christian <i><a href="/wiki/Reconquista" title="Reconquista">Reconquista</a></i>, and in 1139, <a href="/wiki/Afonso_Henriques" class="mw-redirect" title="Afonso Henriques">Afonso Henriques</a> was proclaimed <a href="/wiki/King_of_Portugal" class="mw-redirect" title="King of Portugal">King of Portugal</a>, thus firmly establishing Portuguese independence.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">[9]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the 15th and 16th centuries, Portugal established the <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Empire" title="Portuguese Empire">first global empire</a>, becoming one of the world's major economic, political and military <a href="/wiki/Education_superpower" class="mw-redirect" title="Education superpower">powers</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">[10]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">[11]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">[12]</a></sup> During this time, Portuguese explorers pioneered maritime exploration in the <a href="/wiki/Age_of_Discovery" title="Age of Discovery">Age of Discovery</a>, notably under royal patronage of Prince <a href="/wiki/Henry_the_Navigator" class="mw-redirect" title="Henry the Navigator">Henry the Navigator</a> and King <a href="/wiki/John_II_of_Portugal" title="John II of Portugal">Jo√£o II</a>, with such notable discoveries as <a href="/wiki/Bartolomeu_Dias" title="Bartolomeu Dias">Bartolomeu Dias</a>'s reach of the <a href="/wiki/Cape_of_Good_Hope" title="Cape of Good Hope">Cape of Good Hope</a> (1488), the <a href="/wiki/Vasco_da_Gama" title="Vasco da Gama">Vasco da Gama</a>'s sea <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_India_Armadas" class="mw-redirect" title="Portuguese India Armadas">route to India</a> (1497‚Äì98) and the discovery of <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a> (1500). Portugal monopolized the <a href="/wiki/Spice_trade" title="Spice trade">spice trade</a> during this time, and the Portuguese Empire expanded with military campaigns led in Asia. But the destruction of <a href="/wiki/Lisbon" title="Lisbon">Lisbon</a> in a <a href="/wiki/Lisbon_Earthquake" class="mw-redirect" title="Lisbon Earthquake">1755 earthquake</a>, the country's occupation during the <a href="/wiki/Napoleonic_Wars" title="Napoleonic Wars">Napoleonic Wars</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Independence_of_Brazil" title="Independence of Brazil">independence of Brazil</a> (1822), and the <a href="/wiki/Liberal_Wars" title="Liberal Wars">Liberal Wars</a> (1828‚Äì34), all left Portugal crippled from war and diminished in its world power.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">[13]</a></sup></p>
<p>After the <a href="/wiki/5_October_1910_revolution" title="5 October 1910 revolution">1910 revolution</a> deposed the monarchy, the democratic but unstable <a href="/wiki/First_Portuguese_Republic" title="First Portuguese Republic">Portuguese First Republic</a> was established, later being superseded by the <i><a href="/wiki/Estado_Novo_(Portugal)" title="Estado Novo (Portugal)">Estado Novo</a></i> right-wing authoritarian regime. Democracy was restored after the <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Colonial_War" title="Portuguese Colonial War">Portuguese Colonial War</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Carnation_Revolution" title="Carnation Revolution">Carnation Revolution</a> in 1974. Shortly after, independence was granted to almost all <a href="/wiki/Portuguese-speaking_African_countries" title="Portuguese-speaking African countries">its overseas territories</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">[14]</a></sup> marking the end of the <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Empire" title="Portuguese Empire">longest-lived colonial empire</a>. Portugal has left a profound cultural and architectural influence <a href="/wiki/Evolution_of_the_Portuguese_Empire" title="Evolution of the Portuguese Empire">across the globe</a> and a legacy of over 250 million <a href="/wiki/Lusophone" title="Lusophone">Portuguese speakers today</a>.</p>
<p>Portugal is a <a href="/wiki/Developed_country" title="Developed country">developed country</a> with a high-income <a href="/wiki/Developed_country#IMF_advanced_economies" title="Developed country">advanced economy</a> and a high <a href="/wiki/Living_standard" class="mw-redirect" title="Living standard">living standard</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">[15]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">[16]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">[17]</a></sup> It is <a href="/wiki/Global_Peace_Index" title="Global Peace Index">the 5th most peaceful country in the world</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">[18]</a></sup> maintaining a <a href="/wiki/Unitary_state" title="Unitary state">unitary</a> <a href="/wiki/Semi-presidential_system" title="Semi-presidential system">semi-presidential</a> <a href="/wiki/Republic" title="Republic">republican</a> form of government.<sup id="cite_ref-constitution_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-constitution-20">[19]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">[20]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-e-book_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-e-book-22">[21]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">[22]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">[23]</a></sup> It has the 18th highest <a href="/wiki/Social_Progress_Index" class="mw-redirect" title="Social Progress Index">Social Progress</a> in the world, putting it ahead of other Western European countries like <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a>, <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a> and <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italy</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[24]</a></sup> A founding member of <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Community_of_Portuguese_Language_Countries" title="Community of Portuguese Language Countries">Community of Portuguese Language Countries</a>, it is also a member of numerous other international organizations, including the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a>, the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Eurozone" title="Eurozone">eurozone</a>, and <a href="/wiki/OECD" class="mw-redirect" title="OECD">OECD</a>.</p>
<p>Portugal is a pioneer when it comes to <a href="/wiki/Drug_policy_of_Portugal" title="Drug policy of Portugal">drug decriminalization</a>, as the nation decriminalized the possession of all drugs for personal use in 2001.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[25]</a></sup> Moreover, after years of investment and cooperation, Portugal marked a climax on <a href="/wiki/Renewable_energy_in_Portugal" title="Renewable energy in Portugal">renewable energy worldwide</a> in 2016, when it was powered for 107 consecutive hours exclusively by <a href="/wiki/Wind_power_in_Portugal" title="Wind power in Portugal">wind</a>, <a href="/wiki/Solar_power_in_Portugal" title="Solar power in Portugal">sun</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Renewable_energy_in_Portugal#Hydro_power" title="Renewable energy in Portugal">water</a>, which advocates say further shows fossil fuels are indeed replaceable.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[26]</a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-18"><a href="#Government_and_administration"><span class="tocnumber">3</span> <span class="toctext">Government and administration</span></a>
