<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portugal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Portugal" title="History of Portugal">History of Portugal</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_history:_Pre-Celts_and_Celts">Early history: Pre-Celts and Celts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portugal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Early history: Pre-Celts and Celts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Lusitania" title="Lusitania">Lusitania</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_the_Suebi" title="Kingdom of the Suebi">Kingdom of the Suebi</a></div>
<div class="thumb tmulti tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:204px;max-width:204px">
<div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Citania_briteiros_casa_2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Citania_briteiros_casa_2.jpg/200px-Citania_briteiros_casa_2.jpg" width="200" height="150" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Citania_briteiros_casa_2.jpg/300px-Citania_briteiros_casa_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Citania_briteiros_casa_2.jpg/400px-Citania_briteiros_casa_2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="480" /></a></div>
</div>
<div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Cit%C3%A2nia_de_Briteiros_-_conjunto_de_casas.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Cit%C3%A2nia_de_Briteiros_-_conjunto_de_casas.jpg/200px-Cit%C3%A2nia_de_Briteiros_-_conjunto_de_casas.jpg" width="200" height="150" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Cit%C3%A2nia_de_Briteiros_-_conjunto_de_casas.jpg/300px-Cit%C3%A2nia_de_Briteiros_-_conjunto_de_casas.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Cit%C3%A2nia_de_Briteiros_-_conjunto_de_casas.jpg/400px-Cit%C3%A2nia_de_Briteiros_-_conjunto_de_casas.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="768" /></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left"><a href="/wiki/Cit%C3%A2nia_de_Briteiros" title="Cit√¢nia de Briteiros">Cit√¢nia de Briteiros</a>, in the <a href="/wiki/Minho_Province" title="Minho Province">Minho</a>, is the best preserved <a href="/wiki/Iron_Age" title="Iron Age">Iron Age</a> and <a href="/wiki/Castro_culture" title="Castro culture">Castro culture</a> site in Portugal.</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The early history of Portugal is shared with the rest of the <a href="/wiki/Iberian_Peninsula" title="Iberian Peninsula">Iberian Peninsula</a> located in South Western Europe. <a href="/wiki/The_name_of_Portugal" class="mw-redirect" title="The name of Portugal">The name of Portugal</a> derives from the joined Romano-Celtic name <a href="/wiki/Portus_Cale" title="Portus Cale">Portus Cale</a>. The region was <a href="/wiki/Pre-Roman_peoples_of_the_Iberian_Peninsula" title="Pre-Roman peoples of the Iberian Peninsula">settled</a> by Pre-<a href="/wiki/Celts" title="Celts">Celts</a> and Celts, giving origin to peoples like the <a href="/wiki/Gallaeci" title="Gallaeci">Gallaeci</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lusitanians" title="Lusitanians">Lusitanians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Celtici" title="Celtici">Celtici</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cynetes" title="Cynetes">Cynetes</a>, visited by <a href="/wiki/Phoenicians" class="mw-redirect" title="Phoenicians">Phoenicians</a> and <a href="/wiki/Carthaginians" class="mw-redirect" title="Carthaginians">Carthaginians</a>, incorporated in the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Republic" title="Roman Republic">Roman Republic</a> dominions as <a href="/wiki/Lusitania" title="Lusitania">Lusitania</a> and part of <a href="/wiki/Gallaecia" title="Gallaecia">Gallaecia</a>, after 45 BC until 298 AD, settled again by <a href="/wiki/Suebi" title="Suebi">Suebi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Buri_(Germanic_tribe)" class="mw-redirect" title="Buri (Germanic tribe)">Buri</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Visigoths" title="Visigoths">Visigoths</a>, and conquered by <a href="/wiki/Moors" title="Moors">Moors</a>. Other influences include some 5th-century vestiges of <a href="/wiki/Alans" title="Alans">Alan</a> settlements, which were found in <a href="/wiki/Alenquer_Municipality,_Portugal" class="mw-redirect" title="Alenquer Municipality, Portugal">Alenquer (old Germanic <i>Alankerk</i>, from Alan+kerk; meaning <i>temple of the Alans</i>)</a>, <a href="/wiki/Coimbra" title="Coimbra">Coimbra</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lisbon" title="Lisbon">Lisbon</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">[27]</a></sup></p>
<p>The region of present-day Portugal was inhabited by <a href="/wiki/Neanderthal" title="Neanderthal">Neanderthals</a> and then by <a href="/wiki/Homo_sapiens" title="Homo sapiens">Homo sapiens</a>, who roamed the border-less region of the northern Iberian peninsula.<sup id="cite_ref-Birmp1_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Birmp1-29">[28]</a></sup> These were subsistence societies that, although they did not establish prosperous settlements, did establish organized societies. Neolithic Portugal experimented with domestication of herding animals, the raising of some cereal crops and fluvial or marine fishing.<sup id="cite_ref-Birmp1_29-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Birmp1-29">[28]</a></sup></p>
<p>It is believed by some scholars that early in the first millennium BC, several waves of <a href="/wiki/Celts" title="Celts">Celts</a> invaded Portugal from <a href="/wiki/Central_Europe" title="Central Europe">Central Europe</a> and inter-married with the local populations, forming <a href="/wiki/Pre-Roman_peoples_of_the_Iberian_Peninsula" title="Pre-Roman peoples of the Iberian Peninsula">different ethnic groups</a>, with many tribes.</p>
<p>Chief among these tribes were the <a href="/wiki/Gallaecia" title="Gallaecia">Calaicians or Gallaeci of Northern Portugal</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Lusitanians" title="Lusitanians">Lusitanians of central Portugal</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Celtici" title="Celtici">Celtici of Alentejo</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Cynetes" title="Cynetes">Cynetes or Conii of the Algarve</a>. Among the lesser tribes or sub-divisions were the <a href="/wiki/Bracari" title="Bracari">Bracari</a>, <a href="/wiki/Coelerni" title="Coelerni">Coelerni</a>, <a href="/wiki/Equaesi" title="Equaesi">Equaesi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Grovii" title="Grovii">Grovii</a>, <a href="/wiki/Interamici" title="Interamici">Interamici</a>, <a href="/wiki/Leuni" title="Leuni">Leuni</a>, <a href="/wiki/Luanqui" title="Luanqui">Luanqui</a>, <a href="/wiki/Limici" title="Limici">Limici</a>, <a href="/wiki/Narbasi" title="Narbasi">Narbasi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nemetati" title="Nemetati">Nemetati</a>, <a href="/wiki/Paesuri" title="Paesuri">Paesuri</a>, <a href="/wiki/Quaquerni" title="Quaquerni">Quaquerni</a>, <a href="/wiki/Seurbi" title="Seurbi">Seurbi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tamagani" title="Tamagani">Tamagani</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tapoli" title="Tapoli">Tapoli</a>, <a href="/wiki/Turduli" title="Turduli">Turduli</a>, <a href="/wiki/Turduli_Veteres" title="Turduli Veteres">Turduli Veteres</a>, <a href="/wiki/Turdulorum_Oppida" class="mw-redirect" title="Turdulorum Oppida">Turdulorum Oppida</a>, <a href="/wiki/Turodi" title="Turodi">Turodi</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Zoelae" title="Zoelae">Zoelae</a>. A few small, semi-permanent, commercial coastal settlements (such as <a href="/wiki/Tavira_Municipality" class="mw-redirect" title="Tavira Municipality">Tavira</a>) were also founded in the <a href="/wiki/Algarve" title="Algarve">Algarve</a> region by <a href="/wiki/Phoenicians" class="mw-redirect" title="Phoenicians">Phoenicians</a>-<a href="/wiki/Carthaginians" class="mw-redirect" title="Carthaginians">Carthaginians</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Roman_Lusitania_and_Gallaecia">Roman Lusitania and Gallaecia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portugal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Roman Lusitania and Gallaecia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Lusitania" title="Lusitania">Lusitania</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gallaecia" title="Gallaecia">Gallaecia</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Hispania" title="Hispania">Hispania</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Evora-RomanTemple_edit.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Evora-RomanTemple_edit.jpg/200px-Evora-RomanTemple_edit.jpg" width="200" height="148" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Evora-RomanTemple_edit.jpg/300px-Evora-RomanTemple_edit.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Evora-RomanTemple_edit.jpg/400px-Evora-RomanTemple_edit.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3676" data-file-height="2729" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Evora-RomanTemple_edit.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Roman_Temple_of_%C3%89vora" title="Roman Temple of √âvora">Roman Temple of √âvora</a> is one of the best preserved Roman-built structures in the country.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Romans first invaded the Iberian Peninsula in 219 BC. During the last days of <a href="/wiki/Julius_Caesar" title="Julius Caesar">Julius Caesar</a>, almost the entire peninsula had been annexed to the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Republic" title="Roman Republic">Roman Republic</a>. The Carthaginians, Rome's adversary in the <a href="/wiki/Punic_Wars" title="Punic Wars">Punic Wars</a>, were expelled from their coastal colonies.</p>
<p>The Roman conquest of what is now part of modern-day Portugal took almost two hundred years and took many lives of young soldiers and the lives of those who were sentenced to a certain death in the slavery mines when not sold as slaves to other parts of the empire. It suffered a severe setback in 150 BC, when a rebellion began in the north. The Lusitanians and other native tribes, under the leadership of <a href="/wiki/Viriathus" class="mw-redirect" title="Viriathus">Viriathus</a>, wrested control of all of western Iberia.</p>
<p>Rome sent numerous legions and its best generals to Lusitania to quell the rebellion, but to no avail‚Äîthe Lusitanians kept conquering territory. The Roman leaders decided to change their strategy. They bribed Viriathus's allies to kill him. In 139 BC, Viriathus was assassinated, and Tautalus became leader.</p>
<p>Rome installed a colonial regime. The complete Romanization of Lusitania only took place in the Visigothic era.</p>
<p>In 27 BC, Lusitania gained the status of <a href="/wiki/Roman_province" title="Roman province">Roman province</a>. Later, a northern province of Lusitania was formed, known as <a href="/wiki/Gallaecia" title="Gallaecia">Gallaecia</a>, with capital in Bracara Augusta, today's <a href="/wiki/Braga" title="Braga">Braga</a>. There are still many ruins of castros (<a href="/wiki/Hill_forts" class="mw-redirect" title="Hill forts">hill forts</a>) all over modern Portugal and remains of <a href="/wiki/Castro_culture" title="Castro culture">Castro culture</a>. Numerous Roman sites are scattered around present-day Portugal, some urban remains are quite large, like <a href="/wiki/Con%C3%ADmbriga" title="Con√≠mbriga">Con√≠mbriga</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mir%C3%B3briga" title="Mir√≥briga">Mirobriga</a>. The former, beyond being one of the largest <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">Roman</a> settlements in Portugal, is also classified as a <a href="/wiki/Monuments_of_Portugal" class="mw-redirect" title="Monuments of Portugal">National Monument</a>. Con√≠mbriga lies 16 kilometres (9.9 miles) from <a href="/wiki/Coimbra" title="Coimbra">Coimbra</a> which by its turn was the ancient <i><a href="/wiki/Aeminium" title="Aeminium">Aeminium</a></i>). The site also has a museum that displays objects found by archaeologists during their excavations.</p>
<p>Several works of engineering, such as baths, temples, bridges, roads, circus, theatres and layman's homes are preserved throughout the country. Coins, some of which coined in Lusitanian land, as well as numerous pieces of ceramics were also found. Contemporary historians include <a href="/wiki/Paulus_Orosius" class="mw-redirect" title="Paulus Orosius">Paulus Orosius</a> (c. 375‚Äì418)<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[29]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Hydatius" title="Hydatius">Hydatius</a> (c. 400‚Äì469), bishop of <a href="/wiki/Aquae_Flaviae" title="Aquae Flaviae">Aquae Flaviae</a>, who reported on the final years of the Roman rule and arrival of the <a href="/wiki/Germanic_peoples" title="Germanic peoples">Germanic tribes</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Germanic_kingdoms:_Suebi_and_Visigoths">Germanic kingdoms: Suebi and Visigoths</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portugal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Germanic kingdoms: Suebi and Visigoths">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Cvp-00791-109v.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Cvp-00791-109v.jpg/200px-Cvp-00791-109v.jpg" width="200" height="263" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Cvp-00791-109v.jpg/300px-Cvp-00791-109v.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/7/7c/Cvp-00791-109v.jpg 2x" data-file-width="390" data-file-height="512" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Cvp-00791-109v.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_the_Suebi" title="Kingdom of the Suebi">Suebic King</a> <a href="/wiki/Miro_(Suebian_king)" title="Miro (Suebian king)">Miro</a> and St. <a href="/wiki/Martin_of_Braga" title="Martin of Braga">Martin of Braga</a> from an 1145 manuscript of Martin's <i>De virtutibus quattuor</i>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In the early 5th century, <a href="/wiki/Germanic_peoples" title="Germanic peoples">Germanic tribes</a>, namely the <a href="/wiki/Suebi" title="Suebi">Suebi</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Vandals" title="Vandals">Vandals</a> (<a href="/wiki/Silingi" title="Silingi">Silingi</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hasdingi" title="Hasdingi">Hasdingi</a>) together with their allies, the <a href="/wiki/Sarmatian" class="mw-redirect" title="Sarmatian">Sarmatians</a> and <a href="/wiki/Alans" title="Alans">Alans</a> invaded the <a href="/wiki/Iberian_Peninsula" title="Iberian Peninsula">Iberian Peninsula</a> where they would form their kingdom. The <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_the_Suebi" title="Kingdom of the Suebi">Kingdom of the Suebi</a> was the Germanic post-Roman kingdom, established in the former Roman provinces of <a href="/wiki/Gallaecia" title="Gallaecia">Gallaecia</a>-<a href="/wiki/Lusitania" title="Lusitania">Lusitania</a>.</p>
<p>About 410 and during the 6th century it became a formally declared kingdom, where king <a href="/wiki/Hermeric" title="Hermeric">Hermeric</a> made a peace treaty with the Gallaecians before passing his domains to <a href="/wiki/Rechila" title="Rechila">Rechila</a>, his son. In 448 R√©chila died, leaving the state in expansion to <a href="/wiki/Rechiar" title="Rechiar">Rechiar</a>.</p>
<p>In the year 500, the <a href="/wiki/Visigothic_Kingdom" title="Visigothic Kingdom">Visigothic Kingdom</a> was installed in Iberia, centred on <a href="/wiki/Toledo,_Spain" title="Toledo, Spain">Toledo</a>. The Visigoths eventually conquered the Suebi and its capital city Bracara (modern day Portugal's <a href="/wiki/Braga" title="Braga">Braga</a>) in 584‚Äì585, following the consecutive defeats of the two last Suebi kings <a href="/wiki/Audeca" title="Audeca">Audeca</a> and <a href="/wiki/Malaric" title="Malaric">Malaric</a>. The former Kingdom of the Suebi then became the sixth province of the Visigothic Kingdom of Hispania.</p>
<p>For the next 300 years and by the year 700, the entire Iberian Peninsula was ruled by the Visigoths. This period lasted until 711, when King <a href="/wiki/Roderic" title="Roderic">Roderic</a> (Rodrigo) was killed while opposing a Moorish invasion from the south. From the various Germanic groups who settled in Western Iberia, the <a href="/wiki/Suebi" title="Suebi">Suebi</a> left the strongest lasting cultural legacy in what is today Portugal, Galicia and Asturias.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">[30]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[31]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[32]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Islamic_period_and_the_Reconquista">Islamic period and the Reconquista</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portugal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Islamic period and the Reconquista">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tmulti tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:204px;max-width:204px">
<div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Silves_castle_-_ancient_capital_of_Algarve_-_The_Algarve,_Portugal_(1387949771).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Silves_castle_-_ancient_capital_of_Algarve_-_The_Algarve%2C_Portugal_%281387949771%29.jpg/200px-Silves_castle_-_ancient_capital_of_Algarve_-_The_Algarve%2C_Portugal_%281387949771%29.jpg" width="200" height="150" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Silves_castle_-_ancient_capital_of_Algarve_-_The_Algarve%2C_Portugal_%281387949771%29.jpg/300px-Silves_castle_-_ancient_capital_of_Algarve_-_The_Algarve%2C_Portugal_%281387949771%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Silves_castle_-_ancient_capital_of_Algarve_-_The_Algarve%2C_Portugal_%281387949771%29.jpg/400px-Silves_castle_-_ancient_capital_of_Algarve_-_The_Algarve%2C_Portugal_%281387949771%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200" /></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left"><a href="/wiki/Castle_of_Silves" title="Castle of Silves">Silves Castle</a>, a Moorish-era fortification in the <a href="/wiki/Algarve" title="Algarve">Algarve</a>.</div>
</div>
<div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Al_Andalus_-_2.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Al_Andalus_-_2.png/200px-Al_Andalus_-_2.png" width="200" height="148" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Al_Andalus_-_2.png/300px-Al_Andalus_-_2.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Al_Andalus_-_2.png/400px-Al_Andalus_-_2.png 2x" data-file-width="670" data-file-height="497" /></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">The Caliphate of Cordoba c. 1000 at the apogee of <a href="/wiki/Al-Mansur_Ibn_Abi_Aamir" class="mw-redirect" title="Al-Mansur Ibn Abi Aamir">Al-Mansur</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Today's modern day continental Portugal, along with most of modern <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a>, was part of the Umayyad Caliphate between 711 AD ‚Äì 1249 AD, following the <a href="/wiki/Umayyad_Caliphate" title="Umayyad Caliphate">Umayyad Caliphate</a> conquest of the <a href="/wiki/Iberian_Peninsula" title="Iberian Peninsula">Iberian Peninsula</a> in 711 AD. This occupation lasted from some decades in the North to approximately five centuries in the South.</p>
<p>After defeating the <a href="/wiki/Visigoths" title="Visigoths">Visigoths</a> in only a few months, the Umayyad Caliphate started expanding rapidly in the peninsula. Beginning in 711, the land that is now Portugal became part of the vast Umayyad Caliphate's empire of <a href="/wiki/Damascus" title="Damascus">Damascus</a>, which stretched from the <a href="/wiki/Indus" class="mw-redirect" title="Indus">Indus</a> river in the Indian sub-continent (now <a href="/wiki/Pakistan" title="Pakistan">Pakistan</a>) up to the South of France, until its collapse in 750. That year the west of the empire gained its independence under <a href="/wiki/Abd-ar-Rahman_I" class="mw-redirect" title="Abd-ar-Rahman I">Abd-ar-Rahman I</a> with the establishment of the <a href="/wiki/Emirate_of_C%C3%B3rdoba" title="Emirate of C√≥rdoba">Emirate of C√≥rdoba</a>. After almost two centuries, the Emirate became the <a href="/wiki/Caliphate_of_C%C3%B3rdoba" title="Caliphate of C√≥rdoba">Caliphate of C√≥rdoba</a> in 929, until its dissolution a century later in 1031 into no less than 23 small kingdoms, called <a href="/wiki/Taifa" title="Taifa">Taifa</a> kingdoms.</p>
<p>The governors of the taifas each proclaimed themselves <a href="/wiki/Emir" title="Emir">Emir</a> of their provinces and established diplomatic relations with the Christian kingdoms of the north. Most of Portugal fell into the hands of the <a href="/wiki/Taifa_of_Badajoz" title="Taifa of Badajoz">Taifa of Badajoz</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Aftasid_Dynasty" class="mw-redirect" title="Aftasid Dynasty">Aftasid Dynasty</a>, and after a short spell of an ephemeral <a href="/wiki/Taifa_of_Lisbon" title="Taifa of Lisbon">Taifa of Lisbon</a> in 1022, fell under the dominion of the <a href="/wiki/Taifa_of_Seville" title="Taifa of Seville">Taifa of Seville</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Abbadids" class="mw-redirect" title="Abbadids">Abbadids</a> poets. The Taifa period ended with the conquest of the <a href="/wiki/Almoravids" class="mw-redirect" title="Almoravids">Almoravids</a> who came from <a href="/wiki/Morocco" title="Morocco">Morocco</a> in 1086 winning a decisive victory at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Sagrajas" title="Battle of Sagrajas">Battle of Sagrajas</a>, followed a century later in 1147, after the second period of Taifa, by the <a href="/wiki/Almohads" class="mw-redirect" title="Almohads">Almohads</a>, also from <a href="/wiki/Marrakesh" title="Marrakesh">Marrakesh</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">[33]</a></sup></p>
<p>Al-Andalus was divided into different districts called <i>Kura</i>. Gharb Al-Andalus at its largest was constituted of ten kuras,<sup id="cite_ref-A._R._Disney.2C_p.55_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-A._R._Disney.2C_p.55-35">[34]</a></sup> each with a distinct capital and governor. The main cities of the period in Portugal were <a href="/wiki/Beja_(Portugal)" class="mw-redirect" title="Beja (Portugal)">Beja</a>, <a href="/wiki/Silves_Municipality,_Portugal" class="mw-redirect" title="Silves Municipality, Portugal">Silves</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alc%C3%A1cer_do_Sal" title="Alc√°cer do Sal">Alc√°cer do Sal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Santar%C3%A9m,_Portugal" title="Santar√©m, Portugal">Santar√©m</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lisbon" title="Lisbon">Lisbon</a>.</p>
<p>The Muslim population of the region consisted mainly of native Iberian converts to <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a> (the so-called <i><a href="/wiki/Muwallad" class="mw-redirect" title="Muwallad">Muwallad</a></i> or <i>Muladi</i>) and berbers. The Arabs were principally noblemen from <a href="/wiki/Syria" title="Syria">Syria</a> and <a href="/wiki/Oman" title="Oman">Oman</a>; and though few in numbers, they constituted the elite of the population. The Berbers were originally from the <a href="/wiki/Atlas_mountains" class="mw-redirect" title="Atlas mountains">Atlas mountains</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rif" title="Rif">Rif</a> mountains of North Africa and were essentially nomads.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="County_of_Portucale">County of Portucale</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portugal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: County of Portucale">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Porto,_Portugal_(10552325653).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Porto%2C_Portugal_%2810552325653%29.jpg/200px-Porto%2C_Portugal_%2810552325653%29.jpg" width="200" height="300" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Porto%2C_Portugal_%2810552325653%29.jpg/300px-Porto%2C_Portugal_%2810552325653%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Porto%2C_Portugal_%2810552325653%29.jpg/400px-Porto%2C_Portugal_%2810552325653%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2592" data-file-height="3888" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Porto,_Portugal_(10552325653).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A statue of Count <a href="/wiki/V%C3%ADmara_Peres" title="V√≠mara Peres">V√≠mara Peres</a>, first <a href="/wiki/County_of_Portugal" title="County of Portugal">Count of Portugal</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/County_of_Portugal" title="County of Portugal">County of Portugal</a></div>
<p>An Asturian Visigothic noble named <a href="/wiki/Pelagius_of_Asturias" title="Pelagius of Asturias">Pelagius of Asturias</a> in 718 AD was elected leader by many of the ousted <a href="/wiki/Visigoth" class="mw-redirect" title="Visigoth">Visigoth</a> nobles. Pelagius called for the remnant of the Christian Visigothic armies to rebel against the Moors and regroup in the unconquered northern Asturian highlands, better known today as the <a href="/wiki/Cantabrian_Mountains" title="Cantabrian Mountains">Cantabrian Mountains</a>, in what is today the small mountain region in North-western <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a>, adjacent to the <a href="/wiki/Bay_of_Biscay" title="Bay of Biscay">Bay of Biscay</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-V._Livermore.2C_1969_pp._32-33_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-V._Livermore.2C_1969_pp._32-33-36">[35]</a></sup></p>
<p>Pelagius' plan was to use the Cantabrian mountains as a place of refuge and protection from the invading Moors. He then aimed to regroup the Iberian Peninsula's Christian armies and use the Cantabrian mountains as a springboard from which to regain their lands. In the process, after defeating the Moors in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Covadonga" title="Battle of Covadonga">Battle of Covadonga</a> in 722 AD, Pelagius was proclaimed king, thus founding the Christian <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Asturias" title="Kingdom of Asturias">Kingdom of Asturias</a> and starting the war of Christian reconquest known in <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">Portuguese</a> as the <i><a href="/wiki/Reconquista" title="Reconquista">Reconquista Crist√£</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-V._Livermore.2C_1969_pp._32-33_36-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-V._Livermore.2C_1969_pp._32-33-36">[35]</a></sup></p>
<p>At the end of the 9th century, the region of Portugal, between the rivers Minho and Douro, was freed or reconquered from the Moors by <a href="/wiki/V%C3%ADmara_Peres" title="V√≠mara Peres">V√≠mara Peres</a> on the orders of King <a href="/wiki/Alfonso_III_of_Asturias" title="Alfonso III of Asturias">Alfonso III of Asturias</a>. Finding that the region had previously had two major cities‚Äî<a href="/wiki/Portus_Cale" title="Portus Cale">Portus Cale</a> in the coast and <a href="/wiki/Braga" title="Braga">Braga</a> in the interior, with many towns that were now deserted‚Äîhe decided to repopulate and rebuild them with Portuguese and Galician refugees and other Christians.<sup id="cite_ref-QuidNovi_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-QuidNovi-37">[36]</a></sup></p>
<p>V√≠mara Peres organized the region he freed from the Moors, and elevated it to the status of <a href="/wiki/County" title="County">County</a>, naming it the <a href="/wiki/County_of_Portugal" title="County of Portugal">County of Portugal</a> after the region's major port city‚Äî<i>Portus Cale'</i> or modern <a href="/wiki/Porto" title="Porto">Porto</a>. One of the first cities Vimara Peres founded at this time is Vimaranes, known today as <a href="/wiki/Guimar%C3%A3es" title="Guimar√£es">Guimar√£es</a> ‚Äì the "birthplace of the Portuguese nation" or the "cradle city" (Cidade Ber√ßo in Portuguese).<sup id="cite_ref-QuidNovi_37-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-QuidNovi-37">[36]</a></sup></p>
<p>After annexing the County of Portugal into one of the several counties that made up the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Asturias" title="Kingdom of Asturias">Kingdom of Asturias</a>, King <a href="/wiki/Alfonso_III_of_Asturias" title="Alfonso III of Asturias">Alfonso III of Asturias</a> knighted V√≠mara Peres, in 868 AD, as the First Count of Portus Cale (Portugal). The region became known as <i>Portucale</i>, <i>Portugale</i>, and simultaneously <i>Portug√°lia</i> ‚Äî the <a href="/wiki/County_of_Portugal" title="County of Portugal">County of Portugal</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-QuidNovi_37-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-QuidNovi-37">[36]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Henri_de_Bourgogne_re%C3%A7oit_l%27investiture_du_comt%C3%A9_de_Portugal,_1094_(Claude_Jacquand,_dit_Claudius;_1841).png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Henri_de_Bourgogne_re%C3%A7oit_l%27investiture_du_comt%C3%A9_de_Portugal%2C_1094_%28Claude_Jacquand%2C_dit_Claudius%3B_1841%29.png/220px-Henri_de_Bourgogne_re%C3%A7oit_l%27investiture_du_comt%C3%A9_de_Portugal%2C_1094_%28Claude_Jacquand%2C_dit_Claudius%3B_1841%29.png" width="220" height="202" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Henri_de_Bourgogne_re%C3%A7oit_l%27investiture_du_comt%C3%A9_de_Portugal%2C_1094_%28Claude_Jacquand%2C_dit_Claudius%3B_1841%29.png/330px-Henri_de_Bourgogne_re%C3%A7oit_l%27investiture_du_comt%C3%A9_de_Portugal%2C_1094_%28Claude_Jacquand%2C_dit_Claudius%3B_1841%29.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Henri_de_Bourgogne_re%C3%A7oit_l%27investiture_du_comt%C3%A9_de_Portugal%2C_1094_%28Claude_Jacquand%2C_dit_Claudius%3B_1841%29.png/440px-Henri_de_Bourgogne_re%C3%A7oit_l%27investiture_du_comt%C3%A9_de_Portugal%2C_1094_%28Claude_Jacquand%2C_dit_Claudius%3B_1841%29.png 2x" data-file-width="1234" data-file-height="1135" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Henri_de_Bourgogne_re%C3%A7oit_l%27investiture_du_comt%C3%A9_de_Portugal,_1094_(Claude_Jacquand,_dit_Claudius;_1841).png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Alfonso_VI_of_Le%C3%B3n" class="mw-redirect" title="Alfonso VI of Le√≥n">Alfonso VI of Le√≥n</a> investing <a href="/wiki/Henry,_Count_of_Portugal" title="Henry, Count of Portugal">Henry, Count of Portugal</a>, in 1093.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Later the Kingdom of Asturias was divided into a number of Christian Kingdoms in Northern Iberia due to dynastic divisions of inheritance among the king's offspring. With the forced abdication of <a href="/wiki/Alfonso_III_of_Asturias" title="Alfonso III of Asturias">Alfonso III "the Great" of Asturias</a> by his sons in 910, the Kingdom of Asturias split into three separate kingdoms of <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Le%C3%B3n" title="Kingdom of Le√≥n">Le√≥n</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Galicia" title="Kingdom of Galicia">Galicia</a> and Asturias. The three kingdoms were eventually reunited in 924 (Le√≥n and Galicia in 914, Asturias later) under the crown of <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Le%C3%B3n" title="Kingdom of Le√≥n">Le√≥n</a>.</p>
<p>During the century of internecine struggles for dominance among the Northern Christians kingdoms, the County of Portugal formed the southern portion of the Kingdom of Galicia. At times the Kingdom of Galicia existed independently for short periods, but usually formed an important part of the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Le%C3%B3n" title="Kingdom of Le√≥n">Kingdom of Le√≥n</a>. Throughout this period, the people of County of Portugal as Galicians found themselves struggling to maintain the autonomy of Galicia with its distinct language and culture (<a href="/wiki/Galician-Portuguese" title="Galician-Portuguese">Galician-Portuguese</a>) from the Leonese culture, whenever the status of the Kingdom of Galicia changed in relation to the Kingdom of Le√≥n. As a result of political division, Galician-Portuguese lost its unity when the <a href="/wiki/County_of_Portugal" title="County of Portugal">County of Portugal</a> separated from the Kingdom of Galicia (a dependent kingdom of Le√≥n) to establish the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Portugal" title="Kingdom of Portugal">Kingdom of Portugal</a>.</p>
<p>In 1093, <a href="/wiki/Alfonso_VI_of_Le%C3%B3n_and_Castile" title="Alfonso VI of Le√≥n and Castile">Alfonso VI of Le√≥n and Castile</a> bestowed the county to <a href="/wiki/Henry,_Count_of_Portugal" title="Henry, Count of Portugal">Henry of Burgundy</a> and married him to his daughter, <a href="/wiki/Teresa_of_Le%C3%B3n,_Countess_of_Portugal" title="Teresa of Le√≥n, Countess of Portugal">Teresa of Le√≥n</a>, for his role in reconquering the land from Moors. Henry based his newly formed county in Bracara Augusta (modern <a href="/wiki/Braga" title="Braga">Braga</a>), capital city of the ancient Roman province, and also previous capital of several kingdoms over the first millennia.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Independence_and_Afonsine_era">Independence and Afonsine era</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portugal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Independence and Afonsine era">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Portugal_in_the_Middle_Ages" title="Portugal in the Middle Ages">Portugal in the Middle Ages</a> and <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_House_of_Burgundy" title="Portuguese House of Burgundy">Portuguese House of Burgundy</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Vis%C3%A3o_de_D._Afonso_Henriques_na_batalha_de_Ourique.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Vis%C3%A3o_de_D._Afonso_Henriques_na_batalha_de_Ourique.png/200px-Vis%C3%A3o_de_D._Afonso_Henriques_na_batalha_de_Ourique.png" width="200" height="226" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Vis%C3%A3o_de_D._Afonso_Henriques_na_batalha_de_Ourique.png/300px-Vis%C3%A3o_de_D._Afonso_Henriques_na_batalha_de_Ourique.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Vis%C3%A3o_de_D._Afonso_Henriques_na_batalha_de_Ourique.png/400px-Vis%C3%A3o_de_D._Afonso_Henriques_na_batalha_de_Ourique.png 2x" data-file-width="500" data-file-height="565" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Vis%C3%A3o_de_D._Afonso_Henriques_na_batalha_de_Ourique.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Afonso_Henriques" class="mw-redirect" title="Afonso Henriques">Afonso Henriques</a> receiving divine intervention at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Ourique" title="Battle of Ourique">Battle of Ourique</a> (1139), where he was acclaimed King of the Portuguese.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On 24 June 1128, the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_S%C3%A3o_Mamede" title="Battle of S√£o Mamede">Battle of S√£o Mamede</a> occurred near <a href="/wiki/Guimar%C3%A3es" title="Guimar√£es">Guimar√£es</a>. <a href="/wiki/Afonso_I_of_Portugal" title="Afonso I of Portugal">Afonso Henriques</a>, Count of Portugal, defeated his mother <a href="/wiki/Teresa,_Countess_of_Portugal" class="mw-redirect" title="Teresa, Countess of Portugal">Countess Teresa</a> and her lover <a href="/wiki/Fern%C3%A3o_Peres_de_Trava" class="mw-redirect" title="Fern√£o Peres de Trava">Fern√£o Peres de Trava</a>, thereby establishing himself as sole leader. Afonso then turned his arms against the Moors in the south.</p>
<p>Afonso's campaigns were successful and, on 25 July 1139, he obtained an overwhelming victory in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Ourique" title="Battle of Ourique">Battle of Ourique</a>, and straight after was unanimously proclaimed <a href="/wiki/King_of_Portugal" class="mw-redirect" title="King of Portugal">King of Portugal</a> by his soldiers. This is traditionally taken as the occasion when the County of Portugal, as a fief of the Kingdom of Le√≥n, was transformed into the independent <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Portugal" title="Kingdom of Portugal">Kingdom of Portugal</a>.</p>
<p>Afonso then established the first of the <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Cortes" title="Portuguese Cortes">Portuguese Cortes</a> at <a href="/wiki/Lamego" title="Lamego">Lamego</a>, where he was crowned by the Archbishop of Braga, though the validity of the Cortes of Lamego has been disputed and called a myth created during the <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Restoration_War" title="Portuguese Restoration War">Portuguese Restoration War</a>. Afonso was recognized in 1143 by King <a href="/wiki/Alfonso_VII_of_Le%C3%B3n" title="Alfonso VII of Le√≥n">Alfonso VII of Le√≥n</a>, and in 1179 by <a href="/wiki/Pope_Alexander_III" title="Pope Alexander III">Pope Alexander III</a>.</p>
<p>During the <a href="/wiki/Reconquista" title="Reconquista">Reconquista</a> period, Christians reconquered the Iberian Peninsula from <a href="/wiki/Moors" title="Moors">Moorish</a> domination. <a href="/wiki/Afonso_I_of_Portugal" title="Afonso I of Portugal">Afonso Henriques</a> and his successors, aided by military <a href="/wiki/Christian_monasticism" title="Christian monasticism">monastic orders</a>, pushed southward to drive out the Moors. At this time Portugal covered about half of its present area. In 1249, the Reconquista ended with the capture of the <a href="/wiki/Algarve" title="Algarve">Algarve</a> and complete expulsion of the last Moorish settlements on the southern coast, giving Portugal its present-day borders, with minor exceptions.</p>
<p>In one of these situations of conflict with the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Castile" title="Kingdom of Castile">kingdom of Castile</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dinis_I_of_Portugal" class="mw-redirect" title="Dinis I of Portugal">Dinis I of Portugal</a> signed with the king <a href="/wiki/Fernando_IV_of_Castile" class="mw-redirect" title="Fernando IV of Castile">Fernando IV of Castile</a> (which was represented, when being a minor, by his mother the queen <a href="/wiki/Maria_de_Molina" class="mw-redirect" title="Maria de Molina">Maria de Molina</a>) the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Alca%C3%B1ices_(1297)" title="Treaty of Alca√±ices (1297)">Treaty of Alca√±ices (1297)</a>, which stipulated that Portugal abolished agreed treaties against the kingdom of Castile for supporting the infant <a href="/wiki/Juan_de_Castilla" title="Juan de Castilla">Juan de Castilla</a>. This treaty established inter alia the border demarcation between the kingdom of Portugal and the kingdom of Leon, where the disputed town of <a href="/wiki/Olivenza" title="Olivenza">Olivenza</a> was included.</p>
<p>The reigns of <a href="/wiki/Denis_I_of_Portugal" class="mw-redirect" title="Denis I of Portugal">Dinis I</a> (Denis I), <a href="/wiki/Afonso_IV_of_Portugal" title="Afonso IV of Portugal">Afonso IV</a> (Alphons IV), and <a href="/wiki/Peter_I_of_Portugal" title="Peter I of Portugal">Pedro I</a> (Peter I) for the most part saw peace with the Christian kingdoms of Iberia.</p>
<p>In 1348 and 1349 Portugal, like the rest of Europe, was devastated by the <a href="/wiki/Black_Death" title="Black Death">Black Death</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[37]</a></sup> In 1373, Portugal made an <a href="/wiki/Anglo-Portuguese_Alliance" title="Anglo-Portuguese Alliance">alliance with England</a>, which is the longest-standing alliance in the world. Over time this went way beyond geo-political and military cooperation (protecting both nations' interests in Africa, the Americas and Asia against French, Spanish and Dutch rivals) and maintained strong trade and cultural ties between the two old European allies. Particularly in the Oporto region, there is visible <a href="/wiki/England" title="England">English</a> influence to this day.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Joanine_era_and_Age_of_Discoveries">Joanine era and Age of Discoveries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portugal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Joanine era and Age of Discoveries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Portugal_(1415%E2%80%931578)" title="History of Portugal (1415‚Äì1578)">History of Portugal (1415‚Äì1578)</a>, <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_discoveries" title="Portuguese discoveries">Portuguese discoveries</a>, and <a href="/wiki/House_of_Aviz" title="House of Aviz">House of Aviz</a></div>
<div class="thumb tmulti tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:204px;max-width:204px">
<div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Batalha_de_Aljubarrota_02.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Batalha_de_Aljubarrota_02.jpg/200px-Batalha_de_Aljubarrota_02.jpg" width="200" height="117" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Batalha_de_Aljubarrota_02.jpg/300px-Batalha_de_Aljubarrota_02.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Batalha_de_Aljubarrota_02.jpg/400px-Batalha_de_Aljubarrota_02.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5574" data-file-height="3250" /></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left"><a href="/wiki/John_I_of_Portugal" title="John I of Portugal">John I of Portugal</a>'s victory at <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Aljubarrota" title="Battle of Aljubarrota">Battle of Aljubarrota</a> secured the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Aviz" title="House of Aviz">House of Aviz</a>'s claim to the throne.</div>
</div>
<div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Batalha_009_(4617766169).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Batalha_009_%284617766169%29.jpg/200px-Batalha_009_%284617766169%29.jpg" width="200" height="134" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Batalha_009_%284617766169%29.jpg/300px-Batalha_009_%284617766169%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Batalha_009_%284617766169%29.jpg/400px-Batalha_009_%284617766169%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="671" /></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left"><a href="/wiki/Batalha_Monastery" title="Batalha Monastery">Batalha Monastery</a> was erected by King John I to commemorate his victory in the <a href="/wiki/1383%E2%80%9385_Portuguese_interregnum" class="mw-redirect" title="1383‚Äì85 Portuguese interregnum">1383‚Äì85 Crisis</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 1383, <a href="/wiki/John_I_of_Castile" title="John I of Castile">John I of Castile</a>, husband of <a href="/wiki/Beatrice_of_Portugal" title="Beatrice of Portugal">Beatrice of Portugal</a> and son-in-law of <a href="/wiki/Ferdinand_I_of_Portugal" title="Ferdinand I of Portugal">Ferdinand I of Portugal</a>, claimed the throne of Portugal. A faction of petty noblemen and commoners, led by <a href="/wiki/John_I_of_Portugal" title="John I of Portugal">John of Aviz</a> (later King John I of Portugal) and commanded by General <a href="/wiki/Nuno_%C3%81lvares_Pereira" title="Nuno √Ålvares Pereira">Nuno √Ålvares Pereira</a> defeated the Castilians in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Aljubarrota" title="Battle of Aljubarrota">Battle of Aljubarrota</a>. With this battle, the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Aviz" title="House of Aviz">House of Aviz</a> became the ruling house of Portugal.</p>
<p>Portugal spearheaded European exploration of the world and the <a href="/wiki/Age_of_Discovery" title="Age of Discovery">Age of Discovery</a>. Prince <a href="/wiki/Henry_the_Navigator" class="mw-redirect" title="Henry the Navigator">Henry the Navigator</a>, son of <a href="/wiki/John_I_of_Portugal" title="John I of Portugal">King Jo√£o I</a>, became the main sponsor and patron of this endeavour. During this period, Portugal explored the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">Atlantic Ocean</a>, discovering several Atlantic archipelagos like the <a href="/wiki/Azores" title="Azores">Azores</a>, <a href="/wiki/Madeira" title="Madeira">Madeira</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Cape_Verde" title="Portuguese Cape Verde">Cape Verde</a>, explored the African coast, colonized selected areas of <a href="/wiki/Africa" title="Africa">Africa</a>, discovered an eastern <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_India_Armadas" class="mw-redirect" title="Portuguese India Armadas">route to India</a> via the <a href="/wiki/Cape_of_Good_Hope" title="Cape of Good Hope">Cape of Good Hope</a>, <a href="/wiki/Colonial_Brazil#Discovery_and_early_exploitation" title="Colonial Brazil">discovered Brazil</a>, explored the <a href="/wiki/Indian_Ocean" title="Indian Ocean">Indian Ocean</a>, established trading routes throughout most of <a href="/wiki/Southern_Asia" class="mw-redirect" title="Southern Asia">southern Asia</a>, and sent the first direct European maritime trade and diplomatic missions to <a href="/wiki/Fern%C3%A3o_Pires_de_Andrade" title="Fern√£o Pires de Andrade">China</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nanban_trade" title="Nanban trade">Japan</a>.</p>
<p>In 1415, Portugal acquired the first of its overseas colonies by conquering <a href="/wiki/Ceuta" title="Ceuta">Ceuta</a>, the first prosperous Islamic trade centre in <a href="/wiki/North_Africa" title="North Africa">North Africa</a>. There followed the first discoveries in the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic" class="mw-redirect" title="Atlantic">Atlantic</a>: <a href="/wiki/Madeira" title="Madeira">Madeira</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Azores" title="Azores">Azores</a>, which led to the first <a href="/wiki/Colonialism" title="Colonialism">colonization</a> movements.</p>
<p>Throughout the 15th century, <a href="/wiki/European_exploration_of_Africa#Portuguese" class="mw-redirect" title="European exploration of Africa">Portuguese explorers</a> sailed the coast of Africa, establishing trading posts for <a href="/wiki/Economic_history_of_Portugal#Expansion_of_the_Portuguese_empire_.2815th_and_16th_centuries.29" title="Economic history of Portugal">several common types of tradable commodities at the time</a>, ranging from <a href="/wiki/Gold" title="Gold">gold</a> to <a href="/wiki/Slavery" title="Slavery">slaves</a>, as they looked for a route to India and its <a href="/wiki/Spice" title="Spice">spices</a>, which were coveted in Europe.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Tordesillas" title="Treaty of Tordesillas">Treaty of Tordesillas</a>, intended to resolve the dispute that had been created following the return of <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Columbus" title="Christopher Columbus">Christopher Columbus</a>, which was made by <a href="/wiki/Pope_Alexander_VI" title="Pope Alexander VI">Pope Alexander VI</a>, the mediator between Portugal and Spain. It was signed on 7 June 1494, and divided the newly discovered lands outside Europe between the two countries along a meridian 370 leagues west of the <a href="/wiki/Cape_Verde" title="Cape Verde">Cape Verde</a> islands (off the west coast of Africa).</p>
<p>In 1498, <a href="/wiki/Vasco_da_Gama" title="Vasco da Gama">Vasco da Gama</a> reached <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a> and brought <a href="/wiki/Economic_history_of_Portugal" title="Economic history of Portugal">economic prosperity to Portugal</a> and its population of 1.7&#160;million residents, helping to start the <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Renaissance" title="Portuguese Renaissance">Portuguese Renaissance</a>. In 1500, the Portuguese explorer <a href="/wiki/Gaspar_Corte-Real" title="Gaspar Corte-Real">Gaspar Corte-Real</a> reached what is now <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a> and founded the town of <a href="/wiki/Portugal_Cove-St._Philip%27s" title="Portugal Cove-St. Philip's">Portugal Cove-St. Philip's</a>, <a href="/wiki/Newfoundland_and_Labrador" title="Newfoundland and Labrador">Newfoundland and Labrador</a>, long before the French and English in the 17th century, and being just one of many <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_colonization_of_the_Americas" title="Portuguese colonization of the Americas">Portuguese Colonizations of the Americas</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[38]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[39]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">[40]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tmulti tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:292px;max-width:292px">
<div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:129px;max-width:129px">
<div class="thumbimage" style="height:178px;overflow:hidden"><a href="/wiki/File:Lisboa-Museu_Nacional_de_Arte_Antiga-Retrato_dito_de_Vasco_da_Gama-20140917.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Lisboa-Museu_Nacional_de_Arte_Antiga-Retrato_dito_de_Vasco_da_Gama-20140917.jpg/127px-Lisboa-Museu_Nacional_de_Arte_Antiga-Retrato_dito_de_Vasco_da_Gama-20140917.jpg" width="127" height="178" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Lisboa-Museu_Nacional_de_Arte_Antiga-Retrato_dito_de_Vasco_da_Gama-20140917.jpg/191px-Lisboa-Museu_Nacional_de_Arte_Antiga-Retrato_dito_de_Vasco_da_Gama-20140917.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Lisboa-Museu_Nacional_de_Arte_Antiga-Retrato_dito_de_Vasco_da_Gama-20140917.jpg/254px-Lisboa-Museu_Nacional_de_Arte_Antiga-Retrato_dito_de_Vasco_da_Gama-20140917.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1250" data-file-height="1750" /></a></div>
</div>
<div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:159px;max-width:159px">
<div class="thumbimage" style="height:178px;overflow:hidden"><a href="/wiki/File:Henry_the_Navigator1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Henry_the_Navigator1.jpg/157px-Henry_the_Navigator1.jpg" width="157" height="179" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Henry_the_Navigator1.jpg/236px-Henry_the_Navigator1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Henry_the_Navigator1.jpg/314px-Henry_the_Navigator1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="329" data-file-height="375" /></a></div>
</div>
<div style="clear:left"></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:left;background-color:transparent"><a href="/wiki/Vasco_da_Gama" title="Vasco da Gama">Vasco da Gama</a> (left), Prince <a href="/wiki/Henry_the_Navigator" class="mw-redirect" title="Henry the Navigator">Henry the Navigator</a> (right): figures of the <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_discoveries" title="Portuguese discoveries">Portuguese discoveries</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 1500, <a href="/wiki/Pedro_%C3%81lvares_Cabral" title="Pedro √Ålvares Cabral">Pedro √Ålvares Cabral</a> discovered <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a> and claimed it for Portugal.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">[41]</a></sup> Ten years later, <a href="/wiki/Afonso_de_Albuquerque" title="Afonso de Albuquerque">Afonso de Albuquerque</a> conquered <a href="/wiki/Goa" title="Goa">Goa</a> in <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a>, <a href="/wiki/Muscat,_Oman" title="Muscat, Oman">Muscat</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ormuz" class="mw-redirect" title="Ormuz">Ormuz</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Persian_Strait" class="mw-redirect" title="Persian Strait">Persian Strait</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Malacca" title="Malacca">Malacca</a>, now a <a href="/wiki/States_of_Malaysia" class="mw-redirect" title="States of Malaysia">state</a> in <a href="/wiki/Malaysia" title="Malaysia">Malaysia</a>. Thus, the Portuguese empire held dominion over commerce in the <a href="/wiki/Indian_Ocean" title="Indian Ocean">Indian Ocean</a> and South Atlantic. Portuguese sailors set out to reach Eastern Asia by sailing eastward from Europe, landing in such places as <a href="/wiki/Taiwan" title="Taiwan">Taiwan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Japan" title="Japan">Japan</a>, the island of <a href="/wiki/Timor" title="Timor">Timor</a>, and in the <a href="/wiki/Moluccas" class="mw-redirect" title="Moluccas">Moluccas</a>.</p>
<p>Although for a long period it was believed the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">Dutch</a> were the first <a href="/wiki/Europeans" class="mw-redirect" title="Europeans">Europeans</a> to arrive in Australia, there is also some evidence that the <a href="/wiki/Theory_of_the_Portuguese_discovery_of_Australia" title="Theory of the Portuguese discovery of Australia">Portuguese may have discovered Australia</a> in 1521.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[42]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[43]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">[44]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Zaragoza" title="Treaty of Zaragoza">Treaty of Zaragoza</a>, signed on 22 April 1529 between Portugal and Spain, specified the anti-meridian to the line of demarcation specified in the Treaty of Tordesillas.</p>
<p>All these factors made Portugal one of the world's major economic, military, and political powers from the 15th century until the late 16th century.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Iberian_Union.2C_Restoration_and_early_Brigantine_era">Iberian Union, Restoration and early Brigantine era</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portugal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Iberian Union, Restoration and early Brigantine era">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Iberian_Union" title="Iberian Union">Iberian Union</a>, <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Restoration_War" title="Portuguese Restoration War">Portuguese Restoration War</a>, and <a href="/wiki/House_of_Braganza" title="House of Braganza">House of Braganza</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Dona_Filipa_de_Vilhena.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Dona_Filipa_de_Vilhena.jpg/200px-Dona_Filipa_de_Vilhena.jpg" width="200" height="144" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Dona_Filipa_de_Vilhena.jpg/300px-Dona_Filipa_de_Vilhena.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Dona_Filipa_de_Vilhena.jpg/400px-Dona_Filipa_de_Vilhena.jpg 2x" data-file-width="624" data-file-height="450" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Dona_Filipa_de_Vilhena.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<i>D. Filipa de Vilhena Arming Her Sons</i> (<a href="/wiki/Vieira_Portuense" title="Vieira Portuense">Vieira Portuense</a>, 1801), a legend of the <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Restoration_War" title="Portuguese Restoration War">Restoration War</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Portugal's sovereignty was interrupted between 1580 and 1640. This occurred because the last two kings of the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Aviz" title="House of Aviz">House of Aviz</a>&#160;‚Äì King <a href="/wiki/Sebastian_of_Portugal" title="Sebastian of Portugal">Sebastian</a>, who died in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Alc%C3%A1cer_Quibir" title="Battle of Alc√°cer Quibir">battle of Alc√°cer Quibir</a> in <a href="/wiki/Morocco" title="Morocco">Morocco</a>, and his great-uncle and successor, King <a href="/wiki/Henry_I_of_Portugal" class="mw-redirect" title="Henry I of Portugal">Henry of Portugal</a>&#160;‚Äì both died without heirs, resulting in the <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_succession_crisis_of_1580" title="Portuguese succession crisis of 1580">Portuguese succession crisis of 1580</a>.</p>
<p>Subsequently, <a href="/wiki/Philip_II_of_Spain" title="Philip II of Spain">Philip II of Spain</a> claimed the throne and so became Philip I of Portugal. Although Portugal did not lose its formal independence, it was governed by the same monarch who governed the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Empire" title="Spanish Empire">Spanish Empire</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">[45]</a></sup> briefly forming a <a href="/wiki/Iberian_Union" title="Iberian Union">union</a> of kingdoms. At this time Spain was a <a href="/wiki/Geographic_region" class="mw-redirect" title="Geographic region">geographic territory</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">[46]</a></sup> The joining of the two crowns deprived Portugal of an independent foreign policy and led to its involvement in the <a href="/wiki/Eighty_Years%27_War" title="Eighty Years' War">Eighty Years' War</a> between <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">Netherlands</a>.</p>
<p>War led to a deterioration of the relations with <a href="/wiki/Anglo-Portuguese_Alliance" title="Anglo-Portuguese Alliance">Portugal's oldest ally, England</a>, and the loss of <a href="/wiki/Ormus" title="Ormus">Hormuz</a>, a strategic trading post located between <a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">Iran</a> and <a href="/wiki/Oman" title="Oman">Oman</a>. From 1595 to 1663 the <a href="/wiki/Dutch-Portuguese_War" class="mw-redirect" title="Dutch-Portuguese War">Dutch-Portuguese War</a> primarily involved the Dutch companies invading many Portuguese <a href="/wiki/Colonies" class="mw-redirect" title="Colonies">colonies</a> and commercial interests in Brazil, Africa, India and the Far East, resulting in the loss of the Portuguese Indian sea trade monopoly.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:John_V_of_Portugal_Pompeo_Batoni.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/John_V_of_Portugal_Pompeo_Batoni.jpg/170px-John_V_of_Portugal_Pompeo_Batoni.jpg" width="170" height="217" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/John_V_of_Portugal_Pompeo_Batoni.jpg/255px-John_V_of_Portugal_Pompeo_Batoni.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/John_V_of_Portugal_Pompeo_Batoni.jpg/340px-John_V_of_Portugal_Pompeo_Batoni.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1465" data-file-height="1867" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:John_V_of_Portugal_Pompeo_Batoni.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
King <a href="/wiki/John_V_of_Portugal" title="John V of Portugal">John V</a> patronized numerous artistic works, earning him the epithet of the <i>Portuguese Sun King</i>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 1640, <a href="/wiki/John_IV_of_Portugal" title="John IV of Portugal">John IV</a> spearheaded an uprising backed by disgruntled nobles and was proclaimed king. The <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Restoration_War" title="Portuguese Restoration War">Portuguese Restoration War</a> between Portugal and the Spanish Empire, in the aftermath of the 1640 revolt, ended the sixty-year period of the <a href="/wiki/Iberian_Union" title="Iberian Union">Iberian Union</a> under the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Habsburg" title="House of Habsburg">House of Habsburg</a>. This was the beginning of the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Braganza" title="House of Braganza">House of Braganza</a>, which reigned in Portugal until 1910.</p>
<p>King John IV's eldest son came to reign as <a href="/wiki/Afonso_VI_of_Portugal" title="Afonso VI of Portugal">Afonso VI</a>, however his physical and mental disabilities left him overpowered by <a href="/wiki/Lu%C3%ADs_de_Vasconcelos_e_Sousa,_3rd_Count_of_Castelo_Melhor" title="Lu√≠s de Vasconcelos e Sousa, 3rd Count of Castelo Melhor">Lu√≠s de Vasconcelos e Sousa, 3rd Count of Castelo Melhor</a>. In a palace coup organized by the King's wife, <a href="/wiki/Maria_Francisca_of_Savoy" title="Maria Francisca of Savoy">Maria Francisca of Savoy</a>, and his brother, <a href="/wiki/Peter_II_of_Portugal" title="Peter II of Portugal">Pedro, Duke of Beja</a>, King Afonso VI was declared mentally incompetent and exiled first to the Azores and then to the <a href="/wiki/Sintra_National_Palace" class="mw-redirect" title="Sintra National Palace">Royal Palace of Sintra</a>, outside Lisbon. After Afonso's death, Pedro came to the throne as King Pedro II. Pedro's reign saw the consolidation of national independence, imperial expansion, and investment in domestic production.</p>
<p>Pedro II's son, <a href="/wiki/John_V_of_Portugal" title="John V of Portugal">John V</a>, saw a reign characterized by the influx of gold into the coffers of the royal treasury, supplied largely by the <a href="/wiki/Royal_fifth" title="Royal fifth">royal fifth</a> (a tax on precious metals) that was received from the <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_empire" class="mw-redirect" title="Portuguese empire">Portuguese colonies</a> of <a href="/wiki/State_of_Brazil" title="State of Brazil">Brazil</a> and <a href="/wiki/State_of_Maranh%C3%A3o_(colonial)" title="State of Maranh√£o (colonial)">Maranh√£o</a>. Acting as an absolute monarch, John nearly depleted his country's tax revenues on ambitious architectural works, most notably <a href="/wiki/Mafra_National_Palace" class="mw-redirect" title="Mafra National Palace">Mafra Palace</a>, and on commissions and additions for his sizable art and literary collections.</p>
<p>Official estimates&#160;‚Äì and most estimates made so far&#160;‚Äì place the number of Portuguese migrants to <a href="/wiki/Colonial_Brazil" title="Colonial Brazil">Colonial Brazil</a> during the gold rush of the 18th century at 600,000.<sup id="cite_ref-ibge_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ibge-48">[47]</a></sup> This represented one of the largest movements of European populations to their colonies in the Americas during colonial times.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Pombaline_era_and_Enlightenment">Pombaline era and Enlightenment</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portugal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Pombaline era and Enlightenment">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Portugal_(1640%E2%80%931777)" title="History of Portugal (1640‚Äì1777)">History of Portugal (1640‚Äì1777)</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:O_marques_de_pombal,_conde_de_Oeiras.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/O_marques_de_pombal%2C_conde_de_Oeiras.jpg/200px-O_marques_de_pombal%2C_conde_de_Oeiras.jpg" width="200" height="248" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/O_marques_de_pombal%2C_conde_de_Oeiras.jpg/300px-O_marques_de_pombal%2C_conde_de_Oeiras.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/O_marques_de_pombal%2C_conde_de_Oeiras.jpg/400px-O_marques_de_pombal%2C_conde_de_Oeiras.jpg 2x" data-file-width="851" data-file-height="1054" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:O_marques_de_pombal,_conde_de_Oeiras.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Sebasti%C3%A3o_Jos%C3%A9_de_Carvalho_e_Melo,_1st_Marquis_of_Pombal" title="Sebasti√£o Jos√© de Carvalho e Melo, 1st Marquis of Pombal">1st Marquis of Pombal</a> effectively ruled Portugal during the reign of King <a href="/wiki/Joseph_I_of_Portugal" title="Joseph I of Portugal">Jos√© I</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 1738, <a href="/wiki/Sebasti%C3%A3o_Jos%C3%A9_de_Carvalho_e_Melo,_1st_Marquis_of_Pombal" title="Sebasti√£o Jos√© de Carvalho e Melo, 1st Marquis of Pombal">Sebasti√£o Jos√© de Carvalho e Melo, 1st Marquis of Pombal</a>, began a diplomatic career as the Portuguese <a href="/wiki/Ambassador" title="Ambassador">Ambassador</a> in <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a> and later in <a href="/wiki/Vienna" title="Vienna">Vienna</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Queen_consort" title="Queen consort">Queen consort</a> of Portugal, <a href="/wiki/Mary_Anne_of_Austria" class="mw-redirect" title="Mary Anne of Austria">Archduchess Maria Anne Josefa of Austria</a>, was fond of Melo; and after his first wife died, she arranged the widowed de Melo's second marriage to the daughter of the Austrian Field Marshal <a href="/wiki/Leopold_Josef,_Count_von_Daun" class="mw-redirect" title="Leopold Josef, Count von Daun">Leopold Josef, Count von Daun</a>. King <a href="/wiki/John_V_of_Portugal" title="John V of Portugal">John V of Portugal</a>, however, was not pleased and recalled Melo to Portugal in 1749. John V died the following year and his son, Joseph I of Portugal, was crowned. In contrast to his father, Joseph I was fond of de Melo, and with the <a href="/wiki/Queen_Mother" class="mw-redirect" title="Queen Mother">Queen Mother</a>'s approval, he appointed Melo as <a href="/wiki/Political_minister" class="mw-redirect" title="Political minister">Minister</a> of Foreign Affairs.</p>
<p>As the King's confidence in de Melo increased, the King entrusted him with more control of the state. By 1755, Sebasti√£o de Melo was made Prime Minister. Impressed by British economic success that he had witnessed from the Ambassador, he successfully implemented similar <a href="/wiki/Economic_system" title="Economic system">economic</a> policies in Portugal. He abolished slavery in Portugal and in the Portuguese colonies in India; reorganized the army and the navy; restructured the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Coimbra" title="University of Coimbra">University of Coimbra</a>, and ended discrimination against different <a href="/wiki/Christian" title="Christian">Christian</a> sects in Portugal.</p>
<p>But Sebasti√£o de Melo's greatest reforms were economic and financial, with the creation of several companies and guilds to regulate every commercial activity. He demarcated the region for production of <a href="/wiki/Port_wine" title="Port wine">Port</a> to ensure the wine's quality, and this was the first attempt to control wine quality and production in Europe. He ruled with a strong hand by imposing strict law upon all classes of Portuguese society from the high nobility to the poorest working class, along with a widespread review of the country's tax system. These reforms gained him enemies in the upper classes, especially among the high nobility, who despised him as a social upstart.</p>
<p>Disaster fell upon Portugal in the morning of 1 November 1755, when <a href="/wiki/Lisbon" title="Lisbon">Lisbon</a> was struck by <a href="/wiki/1755_Lisbon_earthquake" title="1755 Lisbon earthquake">a violent earthquake</a> with an estimated <a href="/wiki/Moment_magnitude_scale" title="Moment magnitude scale">moment magnitude</a> of 8.5‚Äì9. The city was razed to the ground by the earthquake and the subsequent tsunami and ensuing fires.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">[48]</a></sup> Sebasti√£o de Melo survived by a stroke of luck and then immediately embarked on rebuilding the city, with his famous quote: "What now? We bury the dead and take care of the living."</p>
<p>Despite the calamity and huge <a href="/wiki/Death_toll" class="mw-redirect" title="Death toll">death toll</a>, Lisbon suffered no epidemics and within less than one year was already being rebuilt. The new city centre of Lisbon was designed to resist subsequent earthquakes. Architectural models were built for tests, and the effects of an earthquake were simulated by marching troops around the models. The buildings and big squares of the Pombaline City Centre still remain as one of Lisbon's tourist attractions. Sebasti√£o de Melo also made an important contribution to the study of <a href="/wiki/Seismology" title="Seismology">seismology</a> by designing an inquiry that was sent to every parish in the country.</p>
<div class="thumb tmulti tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:292px;max-width:292px">

</div>
