</div>
<div style="clear:left"></div>
<div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:144px;max-width:144px">
<div class="thumbimage" style="height:100px;overflow:hidden"><a href="/wiki/File:Ruinas_da_Igreja_de_S._Paulo_ap%C3%B3s_o_Terramoto_de_1755_-_Jacques_Philippe_Le_Bas,_1757.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Ruinas_da_Igreja_de_S._Paulo_ap%C3%B3s_o_Terramoto_de_1755_-_Jacques_Philippe_Le_Bas%2C_1757.png/142px-Ruinas_da_Igreja_de_S._Paulo_ap%C3%B3s_o_Terramoto_de_1755_-_Jacques_Philippe_Le_Bas%2C_1757.png" width="142" height="101" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Ruinas_da_Igreja_de_S._Paulo_ap%C3%B3s_o_Terramoto_de_1755_-_Jacques_Philippe_Le_Bas%2C_1757.png/213px-Ruinas_da_Igreja_de_S._Paulo_ap%C3%B3s_o_Terramoto_de_1755_-_Jacques_Philippe_Le_Bas%2C_1757.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Ruinas_da_Igreja_de_S._Paulo_ap%C3%B3s_o_Terramoto_de_1755_-_Jacques_Philippe_Le_Bas%2C_1757.png/284px-Ruinas_da_Igreja_de_S._Paulo_ap%C3%B3s_o_Terramoto_de_1755_-_Jacques_Philippe_Le_Bas%2C_1757.png 2x" data-file-width="1029" data-file-height="731" /></a></div>
</div>
<div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:144px;max-width:144px">
<div class="thumbimage" style="height:100px;overflow:hidden"><a href="/wiki/File:Ruinas_da_S%C3%A9_de_Lisboa_ap%C3%B3s_o_Terramoto_de_1755_-_Jacques_Philippe_Le_Bas,_1757.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Ruinas_da_S%C3%A9_de_Lisboa_ap%C3%B3s_o_Terramoto_de_1755_-_Jacques_Philippe_Le_Bas%2C_1757.png/142px-Ruinas_da_S%C3%A9_de_Lisboa_ap%C3%B3s_o_Terramoto_de_1755_-_Jacques_Philippe_Le_Bas%2C_1757.png" width="142" height="101" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Ruinas_da_S%C3%A9_de_Lisboa_ap%C3%B3s_o_Terramoto_de_1755_-_Jacques_Philippe_Le_Bas%2C_1757.png/213px-Ruinas_da_S%C3%A9_de_Lisboa_ap%C3%B3s_o_Terramoto_de_1755_-_Jacques_Philippe_Le_Bas%2C_1757.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Ruinas_da_S%C3%A9_de_Lisboa_ap%C3%B3s_o_Terramoto_de_1755_-_Jacques_Philippe_Le_Bas%2C_1757.png/284px-Ruinas_da_S%C3%A9_de_Lisboa_ap%C3%B3s_o_Terramoto_de_1755_-_Jacques_Philippe_Le_Bas%2C_1757.png 2x" data-file-width="1016" data-file-height="725" /></a></div>
</div>
<div style="clear:left"></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:left;background-color:transparent">The <a href="/wiki/1755_Lisbon_earthquake" title="1755 Lisbon earthquake">1755 Lisbon earthquake</a> devastated Portugal with an estimated magnitude between 8.5‚Äì9.0.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Following the earthquake, <a href="/wiki/Joseph_I_of_Portugal" title="Joseph I of Portugal">Joseph I</a> gave his Prime Minister even more power, and Sebasti√£o de Melo became a powerful, progressive dictator. As his power grew, his enemies increased in number, and bitter disputes with the high nobility became frequent. In 1758 Joseph I was wounded in an attempted assassination. The <a href="/wiki/T%C3%A1vora_affair" title="T√°vora affair">T√°vora family</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Dukes_of_Aveiro" class="mw-redirect" title="Dukes of Aveiro">Duke of Aveiro</a> were implicated and executed after a quick trial. The <a href="/wiki/Society_of_Jesus" title="Society of Jesus">Jesuits</a> were expelled from the country and their assets confiscated by the crown. Sebasti√£o de Melo prosecuted every person involved, even women and children. This was the final stroke that broke the power of the aristocracy. Joseph I made his loyal minister Count of <a href="/wiki/Oeiras_Municipality,_Portugal" class="mw-redirect" title="Oeiras Municipality, Portugal">Oeiras</a> in 1759.</p>
<p>In 1762, <a href="/wiki/Spanish%E2%80%93Portuguese_War,_1761%E2%80%931763" class="mw-redirect" title="Spanish‚ÄìPortuguese War, 1761‚Äì1763">Spain invaded Portuguese territory</a> as part of the <a href="/wiki/Seven_Years%27_War" title="Seven Years' War">Seven Years' War</a>, but by 1763 the <i>status quo</i> between Spain and Portugal before the war had been restored.</p>
<p>Following the T√°vora affair, the new Count of Oeiras knew no opposition. Made "Marquis of Pombal" in 1770, he effectively ruled Portugal until Joseph I's death in 1779. However, historians also argue that Pombal‚Äôs "enlightenment," while far-reaching, was primarily a mechanism for enhancing autocracy at the expense of individual liberty and especially an apparatus for crushing opposition, suppressing criticism, and furthering colonial economic exploitation as well as intensifying book censorship and consolidating personal control and profit.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">[49]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Napoleonic_era">Napoleonic era</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portugal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Napoleonic era">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Portugal_(1777%E2%80%931834)" title="History of Portugal (1777‚Äì1834)">History of Portugal (1777‚Äì1834)</a> and <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_of_Portugal,_Brazil_and_the_Algarves" title="United Kingdom of Portugal, Brazil and the Algarves">United Kingdom of Portugal, Brazil and the Algarves</a></div>
<div class="thumb tmulti tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:204px;max-width:204px">
<div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Autor_n%C3%A3o_identificado_-_Embarque_da_Fam%C3%ADlia_Real_Portuguesa.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Autor_n%C3%A3o_identificado_-_Embarque_da_Fam%C3%ADlia_Real_Portuguesa.jpg/200px-Autor_n%C3%A3o_identificado_-_Embarque_da_Fam%C3%ADlia_Real_Portuguesa.jpg" width="200" height="153" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Autor_n%C3%A3o_identificado_-_Embarque_da_Fam%C3%ADlia_Real_Portuguesa.jpg/300px-Autor_n%C3%A3o_identificado_-_Embarque_da_Fam%C3%ADlia_Real_Portuguesa.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Autor_n%C3%A3o_identificado_-_Embarque_da_Fam%C3%ADlia_Real_Portuguesa.jpg/400px-Autor_n%C3%A3o_identificado_-_Embarque_da_Fam%C3%ADlia_Real_Portuguesa.jpg 2x" data-file-width="729" data-file-height="558" /></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">The <a href="/wiki/Transfer_of_the_Portuguese_Court_to_Brazil" title="Transfer of the Portuguese Court to Brazil">Departure of the Portuguese Royal Court to Brazil</a> in 1808.</div>
</div>
<div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Alegoria_%C3%A0s_virtudes_do_Pr%C3%ADncipe_Regente_D._Jo%C3%A3o_-_Domingos_Sequeira,_1810.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Alegoria_%C3%A0s_virtudes_do_Pr%C3%ADncipe_Regente_D._Jo%C3%A3o_-_Domingos_Sequeira%2C_1810.png/200px-Alegoria_%C3%A0s_virtudes_do_Pr%C3%ADncipe_Regente_D._Jo%C3%A3o_-_Domingos_Sequeira%2C_1810.png" width="200" height="147" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Alegoria_%C3%A0s_virtudes_do_Pr%C3%ADncipe_Regente_D._Jo%C3%A3o_-_Domingos_Sequeira%2C_1810.png/300px-Alegoria_%C3%A0s_virtudes_do_Pr%C3%ADncipe_Regente_D._Jo%C3%A3o_-_Domingos_Sequeira%2C_1810.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Alegoria_%C3%A0s_virtudes_do_Pr%C3%ADncipe_Regente_D._Jo%C3%A3o_-_Domingos_Sequeira%2C_1810.png/400px-Alegoria_%C3%A0s_virtudes_do_Pr%C3%ADncipe_Regente_D._Jo%C3%A3o_-_Domingos_Sequeira%2C_1810.png 2x" data-file-width="3543" data-file-height="2608" /></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left"><i>Allegory of the Virtues of <a href="/wiki/John_VI_of_Portugal" title="John VI of Portugal">Prince Regent John</a></i>; <a href="/wiki/Domingos_Sequeira" title="Domingos Sequeira">D. Sequeira</a>, 1810.</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The new ruler, Queen <a href="/wiki/Maria_I_of_Portugal" title="Maria I of Portugal">Maria I of Portugal</a>, disliked the Marquis because of the power he amassed, and never forgave him for the ruthlessness with which he dispatched the T√°vora family, and upon her accession to the throne, she withdrew all his political offices. Pombal died on his estate at <a href="/wiki/Pombal,_Portugal" title="Pombal, Portugal">Pombal</a> in 1782.</p>
<p>In the autumn of 1807, <a href="/wiki/Napoleon" title="Napoleon">Napoleon</a> moved French troops through Spain to invade Portugal. From 1807 to 1811, British-Portuguese forces would successfully fight against the <a href="/wiki/Peninsular_War" title="Peninsular War">French invasion of Portugal</a>, while the royal family and the Portuguese <a href="/wiki/Nobility" title="Nobility">nobility</a>, including Maria I, relocated to the <a href="/wiki/Colonial_Brazil" title="Colonial Brazil">Portuguese territory of Brazil</a>, at that time a colony of the <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Empire" title="Portuguese Empire">Portuguese Empire</a>, in South America. This episode is known as the <a href="/wiki/Transfer_of_the_Portuguese_Court_to_Brazil" title="Transfer of the Portuguese Court to Brazil">Transfer of the Portuguese Court to Brazil</a>.</p>
<p>With the occupation by Napoleon, Portugal began a slow but inexorable decline that lasted until the 20th century. This decline was hastened by the independence in 1822 of the country's largest colonial possession, Brazil. In 1807, as Napoleon's army closed in on Lisbon, the <a href="/wiki/Prince_Regent" class="mw-redirect" title="Prince Regent">Prince Regent</a> <a href="/wiki/Jo%C3%A3o_VI_of_Portugal" class="mw-redirect" title="Jo√£o VI of Portugal">Jo√£o VI of Portugal</a> <a href="/wiki/Transfer_of_the_Portuguese_Court_to_Brazil" title="Transfer of the Portuguese Court to Brazil">transferred his court</a> to Brazil and established <a href="/wiki/Rio_de_Janeiro" title="Rio de Janeiro">Rio de Janeiro</a> as the capital of the Portuguese Empire. In 1815, Brazil was declared a Kingdom and the Kingdom of Portugal was united with it, forming a pluricontinental State, the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_of_Portugal,_Brazil_and_the_Algarves" title="United Kingdom of Portugal, Brazil and the Algarves">United Kingdom of Portugal, Brazil and the Algarves</a>.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Portuguese_Constitution_of_1826.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Portuguese_Constitution_of_1826.jpg/200px-Portuguese_Constitution_of_1826.jpg" width="200" height="252" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Portuguese_Constitution_of_1826.jpg/300px-Portuguese_Constitution_of_1826.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Portuguese_Constitution_of_1826.jpg/400px-Portuguese_Constitution_of_1826.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1243" data-file-height="1564" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Portuguese_Constitution_of_1826.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The frontispiece of the 1826 Portuguese Constitution featuring King-Emperor <a href="/wiki/Pedro_I_of_Brazil" title="Pedro I of Brazil">Pedro IV</a> and his daughter Queen <a href="/wiki/Maria_II_of_Portugal" title="Maria II of Portugal">Maria II</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>As a result of the change in its status and the arrival of the Portuguese royal family, Brazilian administrative, civic, <a href="/wiki/Economic_history_of_Brazil#The_economy_at_independence.2C_1822" title="Economic history of Brazil">economical</a>, military, <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Brazil#History" title="Education in Brazil">educational</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_science_and_technology#History" title="Brazilian science and technology">scientific</a> apparatus were expanded and highly modernized. Portuguese and their allied British troops fought against the <a href="/wiki/French_Invasion_of_Portugal" class="mw-redirect" title="French Invasion of Portugal">French Invasion of Portugal</a> and by 1815 the situation in Europe had cooled down sufficiently that Jo√£o VI would have been able to return safely to Lisbon. However, the King of Portugal remained in Brazil until the <a href="/wiki/Liberal_Revolution_of_1820" title="Liberal Revolution of 1820">Liberal Revolution of 1820</a>, which started in <a href="/wiki/Porto" title="Porto">Porto</a>, demanded his return to Lisbon in 1821.</p>
<p>Thus he returned to Portugal but left his son <a href="/wiki/Pedro_I_of_Brazil" title="Pedro I of Brazil">Pedro</a> in charge of Brazil. When the Portuguese Government attempted the following year to return the Kingdom of Brazil to subordinate status, his son Pedro, with the overwhelming support of the Brazilian elites, declared <a href="/wiki/War_of_Independence_of_Brazil" title="War of Independence of Brazil">Brazil's independence</a> from Portugal. <a href="/wiki/Cisplatina" title="Cisplatina">Cisplatina</a> (today's sovereign state of Uruguay), in the south, was one of the last additions to the territory of Brazil under Portuguese rule.</p>
<p>Brazilian independence was recognized in 1825, whereby Emperor Pedro I granted unto his father the titular honour of <i>Emperor of Brazil</i>. John VI's death in 1826 caused serious questions in his succession. Though Pedro was his heir, and reigned briefly as Pedro IV, his status as a Brazilian monarch was seen as an impediment to holding the Portuguese throne by both nations. Pedro abdicated in favour of his daughter, <a href="/wiki/Maria_II_of_Portugal" title="Maria II of Portugal">Maria II</a>. However, Pedro's brother, <a href="/wiki/Miguel_I_of_Portugal" title="Miguel I of Portugal">Infante Miguel</a>, claimed the throne in protest. After a proposal for Miguel and Maria to marry failed, Miguel seized power as King Miguel I, in 1828. In order to defend his daughter's rights to the throne, Pedro launched the <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Civil_War" class="mw-redirect" title="Portuguese Civil War">Liberal Wars</a> to reinstall his daughter and establish a constitutional monarchy in Portugal. The war ended in 1834, with Miguel's defeat, the promulgation of a constitution, and the reinstatement of Queen Maria II.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Constitutional_monarchy">Constitutional monarchy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portugal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Constitutional monarchy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Portugal_(1834%E2%80%931910)" title="History of Portugal (1834‚Äì1910)">History of Portugal (1834‚Äì1910)</a></div>
<div class="thumb tmulti tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:204px;max-width:204px">
<div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:O_Regic%C3%ADdio_por_Haenen_(2).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/O_Regic%C3%ADdio_por_Haenen_%282%29.jpg/200px-O_Regic%C3%ADdio_por_Haenen_%282%29.jpg" width="200" height="118" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/O_Regic%C3%ADdio_por_Haenen_%282%29.jpg/300px-O_Regic%C3%ADdio_por_Haenen_%282%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/O_Regic%C3%ADdio_por_Haenen_%282%29.jpg/400px-O_Regic%C3%ADdio_por_Haenen_%282%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="669" data-file-height="395" /></a></div>
</div>
<div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Aclama%C3%A7%C3%A3o_de_Dom_Manuel_II.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Aclama%C3%A7%C3%A3o_de_Dom_Manuel_II.jpg/200px-Aclama%C3%A7%C3%A3o_de_Dom_Manuel_II.jpg" width="200" height="123" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Aclama%C3%A7%C3%A3o_de_Dom_Manuel_II.jpg/300px-Aclama%C3%A7%C3%A3o_de_Dom_Manuel_II.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Aclama%C3%A7%C3%A3o_de_Dom_Manuel_II.jpg/400px-Aclama%C3%A7%C3%A3o_de_Dom_Manuel_II.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1045" data-file-height="644" /></a></div>
</div>
<div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Proclama%C3%A7%C3%A3o_Rep%C3%BAblica_Portuguesa.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Proclama%C3%A7%C3%A3o_Rep%C3%BAblica_Portuguesa.jpg/200px-Proclama%C3%A7%C3%A3o_Rep%C3%BAblica_Portuguesa.jpg" width="200" height="139" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Proclama%C3%A7%C3%A3o_Rep%C3%BAblica_Portuguesa.jpg/300px-Proclama%C3%A7%C3%A3o_Rep%C3%BAblica_Portuguesa.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Proclama%C3%A7%C3%A3o_Rep%C3%BAblica_Portuguesa.jpg/400px-Proclama%C3%A7%C3%A3o_Rep%C3%BAblica_Portuguesa.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1422" /></a></div>
</div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:left;background-color:transparent">Top to bottom: The <a href="/wiki/Lisbon_Regicide" title="Lisbon Regicide">Lisbon Regicide</a> (1908), <a href="/wiki/Manuel_II_of_Portugal" title="Manuel II of Portugal">Manuel II</a>'s acclamation as King (1908) and the <a href="/wiki/5_October_1910_revolution" title="5 October 1910 revolution">Proclamation of the Republic</a> (1910).</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Queen Maria II and King <a href="/wiki/Ferdinand_II_of_Portugal" title="Ferdinand II of Portugal">Ferdinand II</a>'s son, King <a href="/wiki/Pedro_V" class="mw-redirect" title="Pedro V">Pedro V</a> modernized the country during his short reign (1853‚Äì1861). Under his reign, roads, telegraphs, and railways were constructed and improvements in public health advanced. His popularity increased when, during the <a href="/wiki/Cholera" title="Cholera">cholera</a> outbreak of 1853‚Äì1856, he visited hospitals handing out gifts and comforting the sick. Pedro's reign was short, as he died of cholera in 1861, after a series of deaths in the royal family, including his two brothers <a href="/wiki/Infante_Fernando_of_Portugal" title="Infante Fernando of Portugal">Infante Fernando</a> and <a href="/wiki/Infante_Jo%C3%A3o,_Duke_of_Beja" title="Infante Jo√£o, Duke of Beja">Infante Jo√£o, Duke of Beja</a>, and his wife, <a href="/wiki/Stephanie_of_Hohenzollern-Sigmaringen" title="Stephanie of Hohenzollern-Sigmaringen">Stephanie of Hohenzollern-Sigmaringen</a>. Not having children, his brother, <a href="/wiki/Lu%C3%ADs_I_of_Portugal" title="Lu√≠s I of Portugal">Lu√≠s I of Portugal</a> ascended the throne and continued his modernization.</p>
<p>At the height of European colonialism in the 19th century, Portugal had already lost its territory in South America and all but a few bases in Asia. <a href="/wiki/Luanda" title="Luanda">Luanda</a>, <a href="/wiki/Benguela" title="Benguela">Benguela</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bissau" title="Bissau">Bissau</a>, <a href="/wiki/Maputo" title="Maputo">Louren√ßo Marques</a>, <a href="/wiki/Porto_Amboim" title="Porto Amboim">Porto Amboim</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Island_of_Mozambique" title="Island of Mozambique">Island of Mozambique</a> were among the oldest Portuguese-founded port cities in its African territories. During this phase, Portuguese colonialism focused on expanding its outposts in Africa into nation-sized territories to compete with other European powers there.</p>
<p>With the <a href="/wiki/Berlin_Conference_(1884)" class="mw-redirect" title="Berlin Conference (1884)">Conference of Berlin</a> of 1884, Portuguese Africa territories had their borders formally established on request of Portugal in order to protect the centuries-long Portuguese interests in the continent from rivalries enticed by the <a href="/wiki/Scramble_for_Africa" title="Scramble for Africa">Scramble for Africa</a>. Portuguese Africa's cities and towns like <a href="/wiki/Nova_Lisboa" class="mw-redirect" title="Nova Lisboa">Nova Lisboa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lubango" title="Lubango">S√° da Bandeira</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kuito" title="Kuito">Silva Porto</a>, <a href="/wiki/Malanje" title="Malanje">Malanje</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tete" class="mw-redirect" title="Tete">Tete</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vila_Junqueiro" class="mw-redirect" title="Vila Junqueiro">Vila Junqueiro</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vila_Pery" class="mw-redirect" title="Vila Pery">Vila Pery</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vila_Cabral" class="mw-redirect" title="Vila Cabral">Vila Cabral</a> were founded or redeveloped inland during this period and beyond. New coastal towns like <a href="/wiki/Beira,_Mozambique" title="Beira, Mozambique">Beira</a>, <a href="/wiki/Namibe" title="Namibe">Mo√ß√¢medes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lobito" title="Lobito">Lobito</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jo%C3%A3o_Belo" class="mw-redirect" title="Jo√£o Belo">Jo√£o Belo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nacala" title="Nacala">Nacala</a> and <a href="/wiki/Porto_Am%C3%A9lia" class="mw-redirect" title="Porto Am√©lia">Porto Am√©lia</a> were also founded. Even before the turn of the 20th century, railway tracks as the <a href="/wiki/Benguela_railway" title="Benguela railway">Benguela railway</a> in Angola, and the <a href="/wiki/Beira_railway" class="mw-redirect" title="Beira railway">Beira railway</a> in Mozambique, started to be built to link coastal areas and selected inland regions.</p>
<p>Other episodes during this period of the Portuguese presence in Africa include the <a href="/wiki/1890_British_Ultimatum" title="1890 British Ultimatum">1890 British Ultimatum</a>. This forced the Portuguese military to retreat from the land between the Portuguese colonies of <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Mozambique" title="Portuguese Mozambique">Mozambique</a> and <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Angola" title="Portuguese Angola">Angola</a> (most of present-day <a href="/wiki/Zimbabwe" title="Zimbabwe">Zimbabwe</a> and <a href="/wiki/Zambia" title="Zambia">Zambia</a>), which had been claimed by Portugal and included in its "<a href="/wiki/Pink_Map" title="Pink Map">Pink Map</a>", which clashed with British aspirations to create a <a href="/wiki/Cape_to_Cairo_Railway" title="Cape to Cairo Railway">Cape to Cairo Railway</a>.</p>
<p>The Portuguese territories in Africa were <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Cape_Verde" title="Portuguese Cape Verde">Cape Verde</a>, <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_S%C3%A3o_Tom%C3%A9_and_Pr%C3%ADncipe" title="Portuguese S√£o Tom√© and Pr√≠ncipe">S√£o Tom√© and Pr√≠ncipe</a>, <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Guinea" title="Portuguese Guinea">Portuguese Guinea</a>, <a href="/wiki/Angola_(Portugal)" class="mw-redirect" title="Angola (Portugal)">Angola</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Mozambique_(Portugal)" class="mw-redirect" title="Mozambique (Portugal)">Mozambique</a>. The tiny fortress of <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Jo%C3%A3o_Baptista_de_Ajud%C3%A1" class="mw-redirect" title="S√£o Jo√£o Baptista de Ajud√°">S√£o Jo√£o Baptista de Ajud√°</a> on the coast of <a href="/wiki/Dahomey" title="Dahomey">Dahomey</a>, was also under Portuguese rule. In addition, Portugal still ruled the Asian territories of <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_India" title="Portuguese India">Portuguese India</a>, <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Timor" title="Portuguese Timor">Portuguese Timor</a> and <a href="/wiki/Macau" title="Macau">Macau</a>.</p>
<p>On 1 February 1908, the king Dom <a href="/wiki/Carlos_I_of_Portugal" title="Carlos I of Portugal">Carlos I of Portugal</a> and his <a href="/wiki/Heir_apparent" title="Heir apparent">heir apparent</a>, <a href="/wiki/Luis_Filipe,_Prince_Royal_of_Portugal" class="mw-redirect" title="Luis Filipe, Prince Royal of Portugal">Prince Royal Dom Lu√≠s Filipe</a>, <a href="/wiki/Duke_of_Braganza" title="Duke of Braganza">Duke of Braganza</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lisbon_Regicide" title="Lisbon Regicide">were murdered in Lisbon</a>. Under his rule, Portugal had twice been declared <a href="/wiki/Bankrupt" class="mw-redirect" title="Bankrupt">bankrupt</a>&#160;‚Äì on 14 June 1892, and again on 10 May 1902&#160;‚Äì causing social turmoil, economic disturbances, protests, revolts and criticism of the monarchy. <a href="/wiki/Manuel_II_of_Portugal" title="Manuel II of Portugal">Manuel II of Portugal</a> became the new king, but was eventually overthrown by the <a href="/wiki/5_October_1910_revolution" title="5 October 1910 revolution">5 October 1910 revolution</a>, which abolished the regime and instated <a href="/wiki/Republicanism" title="Republicanism">republicanism</a> in Portugal.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="First_Republic_and_Estado_Novo">First Republic and Estado Novo</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portugal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: First Republic and Estado Novo">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bernardino_Machado,_Te%C3%B3filo_Braga,_Ant%C3%B3nio_Jos%C3%A9_de_Almeida_e_Afonso_Costa,_ap%C3%B3s_uma_sess%C3%A3o_solene_do_Parlamento_em_homenagem_aos_mortos_da_revolu%C3%A7%C3%A3o_republicana,_1911.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Bernardino_Machado%2C_Te%C3%B3filo_Braga%2C_Ant%C3%B3nio_Jos%C3%A9_de_Almeida_e_Afonso_Costa%2C_ap%C3%B3s_uma_sess%C3%A3o_solene_do_Parlamento_em_homenagem_aos_mortos_da_revolu%C3%A7%C3%A3o_republicana%2C_1911.png/200px-thumbnail.png" width="200" height="141" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Bernardino_Machado%2C_Te%C3%B3filo_Braga%2C_Ant%C3%B3nio_Jos%C3%A9_de_Almeida_e_Afonso_Costa%2C_ap%C3%B3s_uma_sess%C3%A3o_solene_do_Parlamento_em_homenagem_aos_mortos_da_revolu%C3%A7%C3%A3o_republicana%2C_1911.png/300px-thumbnail.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Bernardino_Machado%2C_Te%C3%B3filo_Braga%2C_Ant%C3%B3nio_Jos%C3%A9_de_Almeida_e_Afonso_Costa%2C_ap%C3%B3s_uma_sess%C3%A3o_solene_do_Parlamento_em_homenagem_aos_mortos_da_revolu%C3%A7%C3%A3o_republicana%2C_1911.png/400px-thumbnail.png 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1445" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bernardino_Machado,_Te%C3%B3filo_Braga,_Ant%C3%B3nio_Jos%C3%A9_de_Almeida_e_Afonso_Costa,_ap%C3%B3s_uma_sess%C3%A3o_solene_do_Parlamento_em_homenagem_aos_mortos_da_revolu%C3%A7%C3%A3o_republicana,_1911.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Left to right: <a href="/wiki/Bernardino_Machado" title="Bernardino Machado">Bernardino Machado</a> (3rd &amp; 8th President), <a href="/wiki/Te%C3%B3filo_Braga" title="Te√≥filo Braga">Te√≥filo Braga</a> (2nd President), <a href="/wiki/Ant%C3%B3nio_Jos%C3%A9_de_Almeida" title="Ant√≥nio Jos√© de Almeida">Ant√≥nio Jos√© de Almeida</a> (6th President), and <a href="/wiki/Afonso_Costa" title="Afonso Costa">Afonso Costa</a> (58th Prime Minister); 1911.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_First_Republic" class="mw-redirect" title="Portuguese First Republic">Portuguese First Republic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Estado_Novo_(Portugal)" title="Estado Novo (Portugal)">Estado Novo (Portugal)</a></div>
<p>Political instability and economic weaknesses were fertile ground for chaos and unrest during the <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_First_Republic" class="mw-redirect" title="Portuguese First Republic">Portuguese First Republic</a>. These conditions would lead to the failed <a href="/wiki/Monarchy_of_the_North" title="Monarchy of the North">Monarchy of the North</a>, <a href="/wiki/28_May_1926_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat" title="28 May 1926 coup d'√©tat">28 May 1926 coup d'√©tat</a>, and the creation of the National Dictatorship (<i><a href="/wiki/Ditadura_Nacional" title="Ditadura Nacional">Ditadura Nacional</a></i>). This in turn led to the establishment of the right-wing dictatorship of the <a href="/wiki/Estado_Novo_(Portugal)" title="Estado Novo (Portugal)">Estado Novo</a> under <a href="/wiki/Ant%C3%B3nio_de_Oliveira_Salazar" title="Ant√≥nio de Oliveira Salazar">Ant√≥nio de Oliveira Salazar</a> in 1933.</p>
<p>Portugal was one of only five European countries to remain neutral in <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>. From the 1940s to the 1960s, Portugal was a founding member of <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a>, <a href="/wiki/OECD" class="mw-redirect" title="OECD">OECD</a> and the <a href="/wiki/European_Free_Trade_Association" title="European Free Trade Association">European Free Trade Association</a> (EFTA). Gradually, new economic development projects and relocation of mainland Portuguese citizens into the overseas provinces in Africa were initiated, with <a href="/wiki/Angola_(Portugal)" class="mw-redirect" title="Angola (Portugal)">Angola</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mozambique_(Portugal)" class="mw-redirect" title="Mozambique (Portugal)">Mozambique</a>, as the largest and richest overseas territories, being the main targets of those initiatives. These actions were used to affirm Portugal's status as a <a href="/wiki/List_of_transcontinental_countries" title="List of transcontinental countries">transcontinental</a> nation and not as a colonial empire.</p>
<p>After India attained independence in 1947, pro-Indian residents of <a href="/wiki/Dadra_and_Nagar_Haveli" title="Dadra and Nagar Haveli">Dadra and Nagar Haveli</a>, with the support of the Indian government and the help of pro-independence organisations, separated the territories of Dadra and Nagar Haveli from Portuguese rule in 1954.<sup id="cite_ref-lele_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lele-51">[50]</a></sup> In 1961, <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Jo%C3%A3o_Baptista_de_Ajud%C3%A1" class="mw-redirect" title="S√£o Jo√£o Baptista de Ajud√°">S√£o Jo√£o Baptista de Ajud√°</a>'s annexation by the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Dahomey" title="Republic of Dahomey">Republic of Dahomey</a> was the start of a process that led to the final dissolution of the centuries-old Portuguese Empire.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Antonio_Salazar-1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Antonio_Salazar-1.jpg/200px-Antonio_Salazar-1.jpg" width="200" height="268" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Antonio_Salazar-1.jpg/300px-Antonio_Salazar-1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Antonio_Salazar-1.jpg/400px-Antonio_Salazar-1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1195" data-file-height="1600" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Antonio_Salazar-1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Ant%C3%B3nio_de_Oliveira_Salazar" title="Ant√≥nio de Oliveira Salazar">Ant√≥nio de Oliveira Salazar</a> ruled Portugal from 1932 to 1968, within the <a href="/wiki/Estado_Novo_(Portugal)" title="Estado Novo (Portugal)">Estado Novo</a> regime.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>According to the census of 1921 S√£o Jo√£o Baptista de Ajud√° had 5 inhabitants and, at the moment of the ultimatum by the Dahomey Government, it had only 2 inhabitants representing Portuguese Sovereignty.</p>
<p>Another forcible retreat from overseas territories occurred in December 1961 when Portugal refused to relinquish the territories of <a href="/wiki/Goa" title="Goa">Goa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Daman_and_Diu" title="Daman and Diu">Daman and Diu</a>. As a result, the Portuguese army and navy were involved in armed conflict in its colony of <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_India" title="Portuguese India">Portuguese India</a> against the <a href="/wiki/Indian_Armed_Forces" title="Indian Armed Forces">Indian Armed Forces</a>.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Operation_Vijay_(1961)" class="mw-redirect" title="Operation Vijay (1961)">operations resulted in the defeat</a> and surrender of the limited Portuguese defensive garrison, which was forced to surrender to a much larger military force. The outcome was the loss of the remaining Portuguese territories in the <a href="/wiki/Indian_subcontinent" title="Indian subcontinent">Indian subcontinent</a>. The Portuguese regime refused to recognize Indian sovereignty over the annexed territories, which continued to be represented in Portugal's National Assembly until the military coup of 1974.</p>
<p>Also in the early 1960s, independence movements in the Portuguese overseas provinces of <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Angola" title="Portuguese Angola">Angola</a>, <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Mozambique" title="Portuguese Mozambique">Mozambique</a> and <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Guinea" title="Portuguese Guinea">Guinea</a> in Africa, resulted in the <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Colonial_War" title="Portuguese Colonial War">Portuguese Colonial War</a> (1961‚Äì1974).</p>
<p>Throughout the colonial war period Portugal had to deal with increasing dissent, arms embargoes and other punitive sanctions imposed by most of the international community. However, the authoritarian and conservative <a href="/wiki/Estado_Novo_(Portugal)" title="Estado Novo (Portugal)">Estado Novo</a> regime, first installed and governed by <a href="/wiki/Ant%C3%B3nio_de_Oliveira_Salazar" title="Ant√≥nio de Oliveira Salazar">Ant√≥nio de Oliveira Salazar</a> and from 1968 onwards led by <a href="/wiki/Marcelo_Caetano" title="Marcelo Caetano">Marcelo Caetano</a>, tried to preserve a vast centuries-long intercontinental empire with a total area of 2,168,071&#160;km<sup>2</sup>.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[51]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Carnation_Revolution_and_European_integration">Carnation Revolution and European integration</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portugal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Carnation Revolution and European integration">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Carnation_Revolution" title="Carnation Revolution">Carnation Revolution</a> and <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_transition_to_democracy" title="Portuguese transition to democracy">Portuguese transition to democracy</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Portuguese_colonial_war_map1.PNG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Portuguese_colonial_war_map1.PNG/200px-Portuguese_colonial_war_map1.PNG" width="200" height="218" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Portuguese_colonial_war_map1.PNG/300px-Portuguese_colonial_war_map1.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/7/77/Portuguese_colonial_war_map1.PNG 2x" data-file-width="360" data-file-height="392" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Portuguese_colonial_war_map1.PNG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Africa" title="Portuguese Africa">Portuguese Africa</a> before independence in 1975.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Portuguese government and army resisted the <a href="/wiki/Decolonization" title="Decolonization">decolonization</a> of its overseas territories until April 1974, when a bloodless left-wing military <a href="/wiki/Coup" class="mw-redirect" title="Coup">coup</a> in <a href="/wiki/Lisbon" title="Lisbon">Lisbon</a>, known as the <a href="/wiki/Carnation_Revolution" title="Carnation Revolution">Carnation Revolution</a>, led the way for the independence of the overseas territories in Africa and Asia, as well as for the restoration of democracy after two years of a transitional period known as PREC (<i><a href="/wiki/Processo_Revolucion%C3%A1rio_Em_Curso" title="Processo Revolucion√°rio Em Curso">Processo Revolucion√°rio Em Curso</a></i>). This period was characterized by social turmoil and power disputes between left- and right-wing political forces. The retreat from the overseas territories and the acceptance of its independence terms by Portuguese head representatives for overseas negotiations, which would create independent states in 1975, prompted a mass exodus of Portuguese citizens from Portugal's African territories (mostly from Portuguese <a href="/wiki/Overseas_Province_of_Angola" class="mw-redirect" title="Overseas Province of Angola">Angola</a> and <a href="/wiki/Overseas_Province_of_Mozambique" class="mw-redirect" title="Overseas Province of Mozambique">Mozambique</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[52]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[53]</a></sup></p>
<p>Over one million <a href="/wiki/White_African#Portuguese_in_Africa" class="mw-redirect" title="White African">Portuguese refugees</a> fled the former Portuguese provinces as white settlers were usually not considered part of the new identities of the former Portuguese colonies in Africa and Asia. <a href="/wiki/M%C3%A1rio_Soares" title="M√°rio Soares">M√°rio Soares</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ant%C3%B3nio_de_Almeida_Santos" title="Ant√≥nio de Almeida Santos">Ant√≥nio de Almeida Santos</a> were charged with organising the independence of Portugal's overseas territories. By 1975, all the Portuguese African territories were independent and Portugal held <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Constituent_Assembly_election,_1975" title="Portuguese Constituent Assembly election, 1975">its first democratic elections</a> in 50 years.</p>
<p>Portugal continued to be governed by a <a href="/wiki/Junta_de_Salva%C3%A7%C3%A3o_Nacional" class="mw-redirect" title="Junta de Salva√ß√£o Nacional">Junta de Salva√ß√£o Nacional</a> until the <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_legislative_election,_1976" title="Portuguese legislative election, 1976">Portuguese legislative election of 1976</a>. It was won by the <a href="/wiki/Socialist_Party_(Portugal)" title="Socialist Party (Portugal)">Portuguese Socialist Party</a> (PS) and M√°rio Soares, its leader, became Prime Minister of the 1st Constitutional Government on 23 July. M√°rio Soares would be Prime Minister from 1976 to 1978 and again from 1983 to 1985. In this capacity Soares tried to resume the economic growth and development record that had been achieved before the Carnation Revolution, during the last decade of the previous regime. He initiated the process of accession to the <a href="/wiki/European_Economic_Community" title="European Economic Community">European Economic Community</a> (EEC) by starting accession negotiations as early as 1977.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Portugese_minister_Soares_(1975).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Portugese_minister_Soares_%281975%29.jpg/200px-Portugese_minister_Soares_%281975%29.jpg" width="200" height="131" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Portugese_minister_Soares_%281975%29.jpg/300px-Portugese_minister_Soares_%281975%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Portugese_minister_Soares_%281975%29.jpg/400px-Portugese_minister_Soares_%281975%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1280" data-file-height="840" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Portugese_minister_Soares_(1975).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/M%C3%A1rio_Soares" title="M√°rio Soares">M√°rio Soares</a> became Portugal's first democratically elected Prime-Minister in 1976.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Portugal bounced between <a href="/wiki/Socialism" title="Socialism">socialism</a> and adherence to the <a href="/wiki/Neoliberal" class="mw-redirect" title="Neoliberal">neoliberal</a> model. <a href="/wiki/Land_reform" title="Land reform">Land reform</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nationalization" title="Nationalization">nationalizations</a> were enforced; the <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Constitution" class="mw-redirect" title="Portuguese Constitution">Portuguese Constitution</a> (approved in 1976) was rewritten in order to accommodate socialist and communist principles. Until the constitutional revisions of 1982 and 1989, the constitution was a highly charged ideological document with numerous references to socialism, the rights of workers, and the desirability of a <a href="/wiki/Socialist_economy" class="mw-redirect" title="Socialist economy">socialist economy</a>. Portugal's economic situation after its transition to democracy, obliged the government to pursue <a href="/wiki/International_Monetary_Fund" title="International Monetary Fund">International Monetary Fund</a> (IMF)-monitored stabilization programs in 1977‚Äì78 and 1983‚Äì85.</p>
<p>In 1986, Portugal joined the <a href="/wiki/European_Economic_Community" title="European Economic Community">European Economic Community</a> (EEC) that later became the European Union (EU). In the following years Portugal's economy progressed considerably as a result of EEC/EU <a href="/wiki/Structural_and_cohesion_funds" class="mw-redirect" title="Structural and cohesion funds">structural and cohesion funds</a> and Portuguese companies' easier access to foreign markets.</p>
<p>Portugal's last overseas territory, <a href="/wiki/Macau" title="Macau">Macau</a>, was peacefully handed over to the People's Republic of China (PRC) in 1999, under the 1987 joint declaration that set the terms for Macau's handover from Portugal to the PRC. In 2002, the independence of <a href="/wiki/East_Timor" title="East Timor">East Timor</a> (Asia) was formally recognized by Portugal, after an incomplete decolonization process that was started in 1975 because of the Carnation Revolution, but interrupted by an <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">Indonesian</a> armed invasion and <a href="/wiki/Indonesian_occupation_of_East_Timor" title="Indonesian occupation of East Timor">occupation</a>.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Tratado_de_Lisboa_13_12_2007_(081).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Tratado_de_Lisboa_13_12_2007_%28081%29.jpg/220px-Tratado_de_Lisboa_13_12_2007_%28081%29.jpg" width="220" height="131" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Tratado_de_Lisboa_13_12_2007_%28081%29.jpg/330px-Tratado_de_Lisboa_13_12_2007_%28081%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Tratado_de_Lisboa_13_12_2007_%28081%29.jpg/440px-Tratado_de_Lisboa_13_12_2007_%28081%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="521" data-file-height="310" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Tratado_de_Lisboa_13_12_2007_(081).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Lisbon" title="Treaty of Lisbon">Treaty of Lisbon</a> was signed in 2007, when Portugal held the presidency for the <a href="/wiki/European_Council" title="European Council">European Council</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On 26 March 1995, Portugal started to implement <a href="/wiki/Schengen_Area" title="Schengen Area">Schengen Area</a> rules, eliminating border controls with other Schengen members while simultaneously strengthening border controls with non-member states. In 1996 the country was a co-founder of the <a href="/wiki/Community_of_Portuguese_Language_Countries" title="Community of Portuguese Language Countries">Community of Portuguese Language Countries</a> (CPLP) headquartered in Lisbon. <a href="/wiki/Expo_%2798" title="Expo '98">Expo '98</a> took place in Portugal and in 1999 it was one of the founding countries of the <a href="/wiki/Euro" title="Euro">euro</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Eurozone" title="Eurozone">eurozone</a>.</p>
<p>On 5 July 2004, <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Manuel_Barroso" title="Jos√© Manuel Barroso">Jos√© Manuel Barroso</a>, then <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Portugal" title="Prime Minister of Portugal">Prime Minister of Portugal</a>, was nominated <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_European_Commission" title="President of the European Commission">President of the European Commission</a>, the most powerful office in the European Union. On 1 December 2009, the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Lisbon" title="Treaty of Lisbon">Treaty of Lisbon</a> entered into force, after it had been signed by the European Union member states on 13 December 2007 in the <a href="/wiki/Jer%C3%B3nimos_Monastery" title="Jer√≥nimos Monastery">Jer√≥nimos Monastery</a>, in Lisbon, enhancing the efficiency and democratic legitimacy of the Union and improving the coherence of its action. The <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Ireland" title="Republic of Ireland">Republic of Ireland</a> was the only EU state to hold a democratic referendum on the Lisbon Treaty; it was initially rejected by voters in 2008.</p>
<p>Economic disruption and an unsustainable growth in <a href="/wiki/Government_debt" title="Government debt">borrowing costs</a> in the wake of the <a href="/wiki/Late-2000s_financial_crisis" class="mw-redirect" title="Late-2000s financial crisis">late-2000s financial crisis</a> led the country to negotiate in 2011 with the IMF and the European Union, through the <a href="/wiki/European_Financial_Stability_Mechanism" class="mw-redirect" title="European Financial Stability Mechanism">European Financial Stability Mechanism</a> (EFSM) and the <a href="/wiki/European_Financial_Stability_Facility" title="European Financial Stability Facility">European Financial Stability Facility</a> (EFSF), a loan to help the country stabilise its finances.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portugal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Portugal" title="Geography of Portugal">Geography of Portugal</a></div>
<div class="thumb tmulti tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:204px;max-width:204px">
<div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Portugal_topographic_map-pt.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Portugal_topographic_map-pt.png/200px-Portugal_topographic_map-pt.png" width="200" height="353" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Portugal_topographic_map-pt.png/300px-Portugal_topographic_map-pt.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Portugal_topographic_map-pt.png/400px-Portugal_topographic_map-pt.png 2x" data-file-width="1738" data-file-height="3070" /></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">Topography and administration.</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The territory of Portugal includes an area in the <a href="/wiki/Iberian_Peninsula" title="Iberian Peninsula">Iberian Peninsula</a> (referred to as <i>the continent</i> by most Portuguese) and two archipelagos in the Atlantic Ocean: the archipelagos of Madeira and the Azores. It lies between latitudes <a href="/wiki/32nd_parallel_north" title="32nd parallel north">32¬∞</a> and <a href="/wiki/43rd_parallel_north" title="43rd parallel north">43¬∞ N</a>, and longitudes <a href="/wiki/32nd_meridian_west" title="32nd meridian west">32¬∞</a> and <a href="/wiki/6th_meridian_west" title="6th meridian west">6¬∞ W</a>.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Continental_Portugal" title="Continental Portugal">Mainland Portugal</a> is split by its main river, the <a href="/wiki/Tagus" title="Tagus">Tagus</a> that flows from Spain and disgorges in Tagus Estuary, in Lisbon, before escaping into the Atlantic. The northern landscape is mountainous towards the interior with several plateaus indented by river valleys, whereas the south, that includes the <a href="/wiki/Algarve" title="Algarve">Algarve</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Alentejo" title="Alentejo">Alentejo</a> regions, is characterized by rolling plains.</p>
<p>Portugal's highest peak is the similarly named <a href="/wiki/Mount_Pico" title="Mount Pico">Mount Pico</a> on the island of <a href="/wiki/Pico_Island" title="Pico Island">Pico</a> in the Azores. This ancient volcano, which measures 2,351&#160;m (7,713&#160;ft) is an iconic symbol of the Azores, while the <a href="/wiki/Serra_da_Estrela" title="Serra da Estrela">Serra da Estrela</a> on the mainland (the summit being 1,991&#160;m (6,532&#160;ft) above sea level) is an important seasonal attraction for skiers and winter sports enthusiasts.</p>
<p>The archipelagos of Madeira and the Azores are scattered within the Atlantic Ocean: the Azores straddling the <a href="/wiki/Mid-Atlantic_Ridge" title="Mid-Atlantic Ridge">Mid-Atlantic Ridge</a> on a tectonic triple junction, and Madeira along a range formed by <a href="/wiki/Plate_tectonics" title="Plate tectonics">in-plate</a> <a href="/wiki/Hotspot_(geology)" title="Hotspot (geology)">hotspot</a> geology. Geologically, these islands were formed by volcanic and seismic events. The last terrestrial volcanic eruption occurred in 1957‚Äì58 (<a href="/wiki/Capelinhos" title="Capelinhos">Capelinhos</a>) and minor earthquakes occur sporadically, usually of low intensity.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Exclusive_economic_zone_of_Portugal" title="Exclusive economic zone of Portugal">Portugal's exclusive economic zone</a>, a sea zone over which the Portuguese have special rights over the exploration and use of marine resources, has 1,727,408&#160;km<sup>2</sup>. This is the 3rd largest <a href="/wiki/Exclusive_economic_zone" title="Exclusive economic zone">exclusive economic zone</a> of the European Union and the 11th largest in the world.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portugal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Climate_of_Portugal" class="mw-redirect" title="Climate of Portugal">Climate of Portugal</a></div>
<p>Portugal is defined as a <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_climate" title="Mediterranean climate">Mediterranean climate</a> (<i>Csa</i> in the South, interior, and Douro region; <i>Csb</i> in the North, Central Portugal and coastal Alentejo; mixed <a href="/wiki/Oceanic_climate" title="Oceanic climate">oceanic climate</a> along the northern half of the coastline<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">[54]</a></sup> and also <a href="/wiki/Semi-arid_climate" title="Semi-arid climate">Semi-arid climate</a> or <a href="/wiki/Steppe_climate" class="mw-redirect" title="Steppe climate">Steppe climate</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/Cold_semi-arid_climate" class="mw-redirect" title="Cold semi-arid climate">BSk</a></i> in certain parts of Beja district far South) according to the <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="K√∂ppen climate classification">K√∂ppen-Geiger Climate Classification</a>), and is one of the warmest European countries: the annual average temperature in <a href="/wiki/Mainland_Portugal" class="mw-redirect" title="Mainland Portugal">mainland Portugal</a> varies from 8‚Äì12&#160;¬∞C (46.4‚Äì53.6&#160;¬∞F) in the mountainous interior north to 16‚Äì20&#160;¬∞C (60.8‚Äì68.0&#160;¬∞F) in the south and on the <a href="/wiki/Guadiana" title="Guadiana">Guadiana</a> <a href="/wiki/River_basin" class="mw-redirect" title="River basin">river basin</a>. There are however, variations from the highlands to the lowlands: Rivas Martinez, presents several different bioclimatic zones for Portugal. <sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">[55]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Algarve" title="Algarve">Algarve</a>, separated from the <a href="/wiki/Alentejo" title="Alentejo">Alentejo</a> region by mountains reaching up to 900 metres (3,000&#160;ft) in Alto de F√≥ia, has a climate similar to that of the southern coastal areas of Spain or Southwest Australia.</p>
<p>Annual average rainfall in the mainland varies from just over 3,200&#160;mm (126.0&#160;in) in the northern mountains to less than 300&#160;mm (11.8&#160;in) in the area of the Massueime River, near C√¥a, along the <a href="/wiki/Douro" title="Douro">Douro</a> river. <a href="/wiki/Mount_Pico" title="Mount Pico">Mount Pico</a> is recognized as receiving the largest annual rainfall (over 6,250&#160;mm (246.1&#160;in) per year) in Portugal, according to <i><a href="/wiki/Instituto_Portugu%C3%AAs_do_Mar_e_da_Atmosfera" title="Instituto Portugu√™s do Mar e da Atmosfera">Instituto Portugu√™s do Mar e da Atmosfera</a></i> (English: Portuguese Institute of the Sea and the Atmosphere).</p>
<p>In some areas, such as the Guadiana basin, annual average temperatures can be as high as 28&#160;¬∞C (82&#160;¬∞F), and summer highest temperatures routinely are over 40&#160;¬∞C (104&#160;¬∞F). The record high of 47.4&#160;¬∞C (117.3&#160;¬∞F) was recorded in <a href="/wiki/Amareleja" title="Amareleja">Amareleja</a>, although this might not be the hottest spot in summer, according to satellite readings.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">[56]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">[57]</a></sup></p>
<p>Snowfalls occur regularly in the winter in the interior North and Centre of the country in districts such as <a href="/wiki/Guarda_District" title="Guarda District">Guarda</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bragan%C3%A7a_District" title="Bragan√ßa District">Bragan√ßa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Viseu" title="Viseu">Viseu</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vila_Real_District" title="Vila Real District">Vila Real</a>, particularly on the mountains. In winter temperatures may drop below ‚àí10.0&#160;¬∞C (14.0&#160;¬∞F) in particular in <a href="/wiki/Serra_da_Estrela" title="Serra da Estrela">Serra da Estrela</a>, <a href="/wiki/Serra_do_Ger%C3%AAs" class="mw-redirect" title="Serra do Ger√™s">Serra do Ger√™s</a>, <a href="/wiki/Serra_do_Mar%C3%A3o" title="Serra do Mar√£o">Serra do Mar√£o</a> and <a href="/wiki/Montesinho_Natural_Park" title="Montesinho Natural Park">Serra de Montesinho</a>. In these places snow can fall any time from October to May. In the South of the country snowfalls are rare but still occur in the highest elevations. While the official absolute minimum by <a href="/wiki/Instituto_Portugu%C3%AAs_do_Mar_e_da_Atmosfera" title="Instituto Portugu√™s do Mar e da Atmosfera">IPMA</a> is ‚àí16.0&#160;¬∞C (3.2&#160;¬∞F) in <a href="/wiki/Penhas_da_Sa%C3%BAde" title="Penhas da Sa√∫de">Penhas da Sa√∫de</a> and <a href="/wiki/Miranda_do_Douro" title="Miranda do Douro">Miranda do Douro</a>, lower temperatures have been recorded, such as ‚àí17.5&#160;¬∞C (0.5&#160;¬∞F) by <a href="/wiki/Bragan%C3%A7a,_Portugal" title="Bragan√ßa, Portugal">Bragan√ßa</a> Polytechnic Institute in the outskirts of the city in 1983, and bellow ‚àí20.0&#160;¬∞C (‚àí4.0&#160;¬∞F) in Serra da Estrela.</p>
<p>Portugal has around 2500 to 3200 hours of sunshine a year, an average of 4‚Äì6&#160;h in winter and 10‚Äì12&#160;h in the summer, with higher values in the south-east and lower in the north-west.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Sea_surface_temperature" title="Sea surface temperature">sea surface temperature</a> on the west coast of mainland Portugal varies from 13‚Äì15&#160;¬∞C (55.4‚Äì59.0&#160;¬∞F) in winter to 18‚Äì22&#160;¬∞C (64.4‚Äì71.6&#160;¬∞F) in the summer while on the south coast it ranges from 15&#160;¬∞C (59.0&#160;¬∞F) in winter and rises in the summer to about 23&#160;¬∞C (73.4&#160;¬∞F) occasionally reaching 27&#160;¬∞C (80.6&#160;¬∞F).</p>
<p>Both the archipelagos of the Azores and Madeira have a subtropical climate, although variations between islands exist, making weather predictions very difficult (owing to rough topography). The Madeira and Azorean archipelagos have a narrower temperature range, with annual average temperatures exceeding 20&#160;¬∞C (68&#160;¬∞F) along the coast (according to the Portuguese Meteorological Institute). Some islands in Azores do have drier months in the summer. Consequently, the island of the Azores have been identified as having a <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean" class="mw-redirect" title="Mediterranean">Mediterranean</a> climate (both <i>Csa</i> and <i>Csb</i> types), while some islands (such as <a href="/wiki/Flores_Island_(Azores)" title="Flores Island (Azores)">Flores</a> or <a href="/wiki/Corvo_Island" title="Corvo Island">Corvo</a>) are classified as Maritime Temperate (<i>Cfb</i>) and Humid subtropical (<i>Cfa</i>), respectively, according to K√∂ppen-Geiger classification.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Porto_Santo" class="mw-redirect" title="Porto Santo">Porto Santo</a> island in Madeira has a semi-arid steppe climate (<i>BSh</i>). The <a href="/wiki/Savage_Islands" title="Savage Islands">Savage Islands</a>, which are part of the regional territory of Madeira and a nature reserve are unique in being classified as a desert climate (<i>BWh</i>) with an annual average rainfall of approximately 150&#160;mm (5.9&#160;in). The sea surface temperature in the archipelagos varies from 17‚Äì18&#160;¬∞C (62.6‚Äì64.4&#160;¬∞F) in winter to 24‚Äì25&#160;¬∞C (75.2‚Äì77.0&#160;¬∞F) in the summer occasionally reaching 26&#160;¬∞C (78.8&#160;¬∞F).</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Biodiversity">Biodiversity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portugal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Biodiversity">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Geres1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Geres1.jpg/200px-Geres1.jpg" width="200" height="200" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Geres1.jpg/300px-Geres1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Geres1.jpg/400px-Geres1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="1024" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Geres1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Peneda-Ger%C3%AAs_National_Park" title="Peneda-Ger√™s National Park">Peneda-Ger√™s National Park</a> is the only national park in Portugal.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Despite the fact that humans have occupied the territory of Portugal for thousands of years, something still remains of the original vegetation. In Ger√™s both mature deciduous and coniferous forests can be found, an extremely rare worldwide mature Mediterranean forest remain in some parts of the Arr√°bida mountain and a subtropical laurissilva forest, dating back to the Tertiary period, covers its largest continuous area in the world in the Madeira main island. Due to the human population decrease and rural exodus, Pyrenean oak and other local native trees are colonizing many abandoned areas.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Boar" class="mw-redirect" title="Boar">Boar</a>, Iberian red deer, roe deer, and the Iberian wild goat, are reported to have expanded greatly during recent decades. Boars were found recently roaming at night inside large urban areas, like in Setubal. <a href="/wiki/Protected_areas_of_Portugal" title="Protected areas of Portugal">Protected areas of Portugal</a> include one national park (<a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">Portuguese</a>: <span lang="pt"><i>Parque Nacional</i></span>), 12 natural parks (<a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">Portuguese</a>: <span lang="pt"><i>Parque Natural</i></span>), nine natural reserves (<a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">Portuguese</a>: <span lang="pt"><i>Reserva Natural</i></span>), five natural monuments (<a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">Portuguese</a>: <span lang="pt"><i>Monumento Natural</i></span>), and seven protected landscapes (<a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">Portuguese</a>: <span lang="pt"><i>Paisagem Protegida</i></span>), which include the <a href="/wiki/Parque_Nacional_da_Peneda-Ger%C3%AAs" class="mw-redirect" title="Parque Nacional da Peneda-Ger√™s">Parque Nacional da Peneda-Ger√™s</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Parque_Natural_da_Serra_da_Estrela" class="mw-redirect" title="Parque Natural da Serra da Estrela">Parque Natural da Serra da Estrela</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Paul_de_Arzila" title="Paul de Arzila">Paul d'Arzila</a>.</p>
<p>These natural environments are shaped by diverse flora, and include widespread species of pine (especially the <i><a href="/wiki/Pinus_pinaster" title="Pinus pinaster">Pinus pinaster</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Pinus_pinea" class="mw-redirect" title="Pinus pinea">Pinus pinea</a></i> species), the English oak (<i><a href="/wiki/Quercus_robur" title="Quercus robur">Quercus robur</a></i>), the Pyrenean oak (<i><a href="/wiki/Quercus_pyrenaica" title="Quercus pyrenaica">Quercus pyrenaica</a></i>) the chestnut (<i><a href="/wiki/Castanea_sativa" title="Castanea sativa">Castanea sativa</a></i>), the cork-oak (<i><a href="/wiki/Quercus_suber" title="Quercus suber">Quercus suber</a></i>), the holm oak (<i><a href="/wiki/Quercus_ilex" title="Quercus ilex">Quercus ilex</a></i>) or the Portuguese oak (<i><a href="/wiki/Quercus_faginea" title="Quercus faginea">Quercus faginea</a></i>). Due to their economic value, some species of the <i>Eucalyptus</i> genus were introduced and are now common, despite their environmental impact.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Laurisilva" class="mw-redirect" title="Laurisilva">Laurisilva</a> is a unique type of subtropical rainforest found in few areas of Europe and the world: in the Azores, and in particular on the island of Madeira, there are large forests of endemic <i>Laurisilva</i> forests (the latter protected as a natural heritage preserve). There are several species of diverse <a href="/wiki/Mammal" title="Mammal">mammalian</a> fauna, including the <a href="/wiki/Fox" title="Fox">fox</a>, <a href="/wiki/Badger" title="Badger">badger</a>, <a href="/wiki/Iberian_lynx" title="Iberian lynx">iberian lynx</a>, <a href="/wiki/Iberian_wolf" title="Iberian wolf">iberian wolf</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wild_goat" title="Wild goat">wild goat</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/Capra_pyrenaica" class="mw-redirect" title="Capra pyrenaica">Capra pyrenaica</a></i>), wild cat (<i><a href="/wiki/Felis_silvestris" class="mw-redirect" title="Felis silvestris">Felis silvestris</a></i>), <a href="/wiki/Hare" title="Hare">hare</a>, <a href="/wiki/Weasel" title="Weasel">weasel</a>, <a href="/wiki/European_polecat" title="European polecat">polecat</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chameleon" title="Chameleon">chameleon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mongoose" title="Mongoose">mongoose</a>, <a href="/wiki/Civet" title="Civet">civet</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brown_bear" title="Brown bear">brown bear</a><sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> (spotted near Rio Minho, close to Peneda-Ger√™s) and many others. Portugal is an important stopover for migratory birds, in places such as <a href="/wiki/Cape_St._Vincent" title="Cape St. Vincent">Cape St. Vincent</a> or the <a href="/wiki/Serra_de_Monchique" title="Serra de Monchique">Monchique</a> mountains, where thousands of birds cross from Europe to Africa during the autumn or in the spring (return migration).</p>
<div class="thumb tmulti tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:312px;max-width:312px">
<div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:146px;max-width:146px">
<div class="thumbimage" style="height:105px;overflow:hidden"><a href="/wiki/File:Estrela_Mountain_Dog_6_month_old_male.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Estrela_Mountain_Dog_6_month_old_male.jpg/144px-Estrela_Mountain_Dog_6_month_old_male.jpg" width="144" height="106" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Estrela_Mountain_Dog_6_month_old_male.jpg/216px-Estrela_Mountain_Dog_6_month_old_male.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Estrela_Mountain_Dog_6_month_old_male.jpg/288px-Estrela_Mountain_Dog_6_month_old_male.jpg 2x" data-file-width="736" data-file-height="541" /></a></div>
</div>
<div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:162px;max-width:162px">
<div class="thumbimage" style="height:105px;overflow:hidden"><a href="/wiki/File:Loutre_des_pyrenees_baronnies_2004.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Loutre_des_pyrenees_baronnies_2004.jpg/160px-Loutre_des_pyrenees_baronnies_2004.jpg" width="160" height="106" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Loutre_des_pyrenees_baronnies_2004.jpg/240px-Loutre_des_pyrenees_baronnies_2004.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Loutre_des_pyrenees_baronnies_2004.jpg/320px-Loutre_des_pyrenees_baronnies_2004.jpg 2x" data-file-width="594" data-file-height="394" /></a></div>
</div>
<div style="clear:left"></div>
<div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:148px;max-width:148px">
<div class="thumbimage" style="height:109px;overflow:hidden"><a href="/wiki/File:Abejaruco.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Abejaruco.jpg/146px-Abejaruco.jpg" width="146" height="177" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Abejaruco.jpg/219px-Abejaruco.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Abejaruco.jpg/292px-Abejaruco.jpg 2x" data-file-width="648" data-file-height="784" /></a></div>
</div>
<div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:160px;max-width:160px">
<div class="thumbimage" style="height:109px;overflow:hidden"><a href="/wiki/File:Estrela_Mar%C3%A7o_2010-40.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Estrela_Mar%C3%A7o_2010-40.jpg/158px-Estrela_Mar%C3%A7o_2010-40.jpg" width="158" height="110" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Estrela_Mar%C3%A7o_2010-40.jpg/237px-Estrela_Mar%C3%A7o_2010-40.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Estrela_Mar%C3%A7o_2010-40.jpg/316px-Estrela_Mar%C3%A7o_2010-40.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3872" data-file-height="2700" /></a></div>
</div>
<div style="clear:left"></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:left;background-color:transparent">Left-to-right: an <a href="/wiki/Estrela_Mountain_Dog" title="Estrela Mountain Dog">Estrela Mountain Dog</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Eurasian_otter" title="Eurasian otter">Eurasian otter</a>, a <a href="/wiki/European_bee-eater" title="European bee-eater">European bee-eater</a>, and a <a href="/wiki/Lusitano" title="Lusitano">Lusitano</a> horse.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Most of the avian species congregate along the <a href="/wiki/Iberian_Peninsula" title="Iberian Peninsula">Iberian Peninsula</a> since it is the closest stopover between Northern Europe and Africa. Six hundred bird species occur in Portugal (either for nesting or during the course of migration), and annually there are new registries of nesting species. The archipelagos of the Azores and Madeira are transient stopover for American, European, and African birds, while continental Portugal mostly encounters European and African bird species.</p>
<p>There are more than 100 freshwater fish species, varying from the giant European catfish (in the Tagus International Natural Park) to some small and endemic species that live only in small lakes (along the western portion of country, for example). Some of these rare and specific species are highly endangered because of habitat loss, pollution and drought. Up-welling along the west coast of Portugal makes the sea extremely rich in nutrients and diverse species of marine fish; the Portuguese marine waters are one of the richest in the world. <a href="/wiki/Marine_fish" class="mw-redirect" title="Marine fish">Marine fish</a> species are more common, and include thousands of species, such as the <a href="/wiki/Sardine" title="Sardine">sardine</a> (<i>Sardina pilchardus</i>), <a href="/wiki/Tuna" title="Tuna">tuna</a> and <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_mackerel" title="Atlantic mackerel">Atlantic mackerel</a>. Bioluminescent species are also well represented (including species in different colour spectrum and forms), like the glowing plankton that are possible to observe in some beaches.</p>
<p>There are many endemic insect species, most only found in certain parts of Portugal, while other species are more widespread like the <a href="/wiki/Stag_beetle" title="Stag beetle">stag beetle</a> (<i>Lucanus cervus</i>) and the <a href="/wiki/Cicada" title="Cicada">cicada</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Macaronesia" title="Macaronesia">Macaronesian</a> islands (Azores and Madeira) have many endemic species (like birds, reptiles, bats, insects, snails and slugs) that evolved independently from other regions of Portugal. In Madeira, for example, it is possible to observe more than 250 species of land <a href="/wiki/Gastropods" class="mw-redirect" title="Gastropods">gastropods</a>.</p>
