</div>
<div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:153px;max-width:153px">
<div class="thumbimage" style="height:213px;overflow:hidden"><a href="/wiki/File:MarceloRebeloDeSousa_10Jun2016.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/MarceloRebeloDeSousa_10Jun2016.png/151px-MarceloRebeloDeSousa_10Jun2016.png" width="151" height="214" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/MarceloRebeloDeSousa_10Jun2016.png/227px-MarceloRebeloDeSousa_10Jun2016.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/MarceloRebeloDeSousa_10Jun2016.png/302px-MarceloRebeloDeSousa_10Jun2016.png 2x" data-file-width="514" data-file-height="728" /></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">
<center><a href="/wiki/Marcelo_Rebelo_de_Sousa" title="Marcelo Rebelo de Sousa">Marcelo Rebelo de Sousa</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_Presidents_of_Portugal" title="List of Presidents of Portugal">20th</a> <a href="/wiki/President_of_Portugal" title="President of Portugal">President of Portugal</a>.</center>
</div>
</div>
<div style="clear:left"></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Portugal has been a <a href="/wiki/Semi-presidential_system" title="Semi-presidential system">semi-presidential</a> <a href="/wiki/Representative_democracy" title="Representative democracy">representative democratic</a> <a href="/wiki/Republic" title="Republic">republic</a> since the ratification of the <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Constitution_of_1976" class="mw-redirect" title="Portuguese Constitution of 1976">Constitution of 1976</a>, with <a href="/wiki/Lisbon" title="Lisbon">Lisbon</a>, the nation's largest city, as its capital. The Constitution grants the division or separation of powers among four bodies referred as "organs of Sovereignty": the <a href="/wiki/President_of_Portugal" title="President of Portugal">President of the Republic</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Portugal" title="Government of Portugal">Government</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_parliament" class="mw-redirect" title="Portuguese parliament">Assembly of the Republic</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Judiciary_of_Portugal" title="Judiciary of Portugal">Courts</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-constitution_20-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-constitution-20">[19]</a></sup></p>
<p>The President, who is elected to a five-year term, has an executive role: the current President is <a href="/wiki/Marcelo_Rebelo_de_Sousa" title="Marcelo Rebelo de Sousa">Marcelo Rebelo de Sousa</a>. The Assembly of the Republic is a single chamber parliament composed of 230 deputies elected for a four-year term. The Government is headed by the <a href="/wiki/List_of_Prime_Ministers_of_Portugal" title="List of Prime Ministers of Portugal">Prime Minister</a> (currently <a href="/wiki/Ant%C3%B3nio_Costa" title="Ant√≥nio Costa">Ant√≥nio Costa</a>) and includes Ministers and Secretaries of State. The <a href="/wiki/Courts" class="mw-redirect" title="Courts">Courts</a> are organized into several levels, among the judicial, administrative and fiscal branches. The <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Supreme_Court" class="mw-redirect" title="Portuguese Supreme Court">Supreme Courts</a> are institutions of last resort/appeal. A thirteen-member <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Constitutional_Court" class="mw-redirect" title="Portuguese Constitutional Court">Constitutional Court</a> oversees the constitutionality of the laws.</p>
<p>Portugal operates a multi-party system of competitive legislatures/local administrative governments at the national, regional and local levels. The Assembly of the Republic, Regional Assemblies and local municipalities and parishes, are dominated by two political parties, the <a href="/wiki/Socialist_Party_(Portugal)" title="Socialist Party (Portugal)">Socialist Party</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Social_Democratic_Party_(Portugal)" title="Social Democratic Party (Portugal)">Social Democratic Party</a>, in addition to the <a href="/wiki/Unitary_Democratic_Coalition" title="Unitary Democratic Coalition">Unitary Democratic Coalition</a> (<a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Communist_Party" title="Portuguese Communist Party">Portuguese Communist Party</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ecologist_Party_%22The_Greens%22" title="Ecologist Party &quot;The Greens&quot;">Ecologist Party "The Greens"</a>), the <a href="/wiki/Left_Bloc" title="Left Bloc">Left Bloc</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Democratic_and_Social_Centre_%E2%80%93_People%27s_Party" class="mw-redirect" title="Democratic and Social Centre ‚Äì People's Party">Democratic and Social Centre&#160;‚Äì People's Party</a>, which garner between 5 and 15% of the vote regularly.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Presidency_of_the_Republic">Presidency of the Republic</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portugal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Presidency of the Republic">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Portugal_(17135381862).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Portugal_%2817135381862%29.jpg/200px-Portugal_%2817135381862%29.jpg" width="200" height="150" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Portugal_%2817135381862%29.jpg/300px-Portugal_%2817135381862%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Portugal_%2817135381862%29.jpg/400px-Portugal_%2817135381862%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1536" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Portugal_(17135381862).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Bel%C3%A9m_Palace" title="Bel√©m Palace">Bel√©m Palace</a> serves as the official residence and workplace of the <a href="/wiki/President_of_Portugal" title="President of Portugal">President of the Republic</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/President_of_Portugal" title="President of Portugal">President of Portugal</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_Presidents_of_Portugal" title="List of Presidents of Portugal">List of Presidents of Portugal</a></div>
<p>The Head of State of Portugal is the <a href="/wiki/President_of_Portugal" title="President of Portugal">President of the Republic</a>, elected to a five-year term by direct, <a href="/wiki/Universal_suffrage" title="Universal suffrage">universal suffrage</a>. He or she has also supervision and <a href="/wiki/Reserve_power" title="Reserve power">reserve powers</a>. Presidential powers include the appointment of the Prime Minister and the other members of the Government (where the President takes into account the results of legislative elections); dismissing the Prime Minister; dissolving the Assembly of the Republic (to call early elections); <a href="/wiki/Veto" title="Veto">vetoing</a> legislation (which may be overridden by the Assembly); and declaring a state of war or siege. The President is also the <i><a href="/wiki/Ex_officio" class="mw-redirect" title="Ex officio">ex officio</a></i> Commander-in-Chief of the Armed Forces.</p>
<p>The President is advised on issues of importance by the <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Council_of_State" class="mw-redirect" title="Portuguese Council of State">Council of State</a>, which is composed of six senior civilian officers, any former Presidents elected under the 1976 Constitution, five-members chosen by the Assembly, and five selected by the president.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Government">Government</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portugal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Government">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Portugal" title="Government of Portugal">Government of Portugal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Portugal" title="Prime Minister of Portugal">Prime Minister of Portugal</a>, and <a href="/wiki/List_of_Prime_Ministers_of_Portugal" title="List of Prime Ministers of Portugal">List of Prime Ministers of Portugal</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Lisbon_holiday_(18607400288).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/Lisbon_holiday_%2818607400288%29.jpg/200px-Lisbon_holiday_%2818607400288%29.jpg" width="200" height="150" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/Lisbon_holiday_%2818607400288%29.jpg/300px-Lisbon_holiday_%2818607400288%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/Lisbon_holiday_%2818607400288%29.jpg/400px-Lisbon_holiday_%2818607400288%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2560" data-file-height="1920" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Lisbon_holiday_(18607400288).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Pra%C3%A7a_do_Com%C3%A9rcio" title="Pra√ßa do Com√©rcio">Pra√ßa do Com√©rcio</a> houses multiple ministries of the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Portugal" title="Government of Portugal">Government of Portugal</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Government is headed by the presidentially appointed <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Portugal" title="Prime Minister of Portugal">Prime Minister</a>, also including one or more Deputy Prime Ministers, Ministers, Secretaries of State and Under-Secretaries of State.</p>
<p>The Government is both the organ of sovereignty that conducts the general politics of the country and the superior body of the public administration.</p>
<p>It has essentially Executive powers, but has also limited Legislative powers. The Government can legislate about its own organization, about areas covered by legislative authorizations conceded by the Assembly of the Republic and about the specific regulation of generalist laws issued by the Assembly.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Council_of_Ministers_(Portugal)" title="Council of Ministers (Portugal)">Council of Ministers</a> ‚Äì under the presidency of the Prime Minister (or the President of Portugal at the latter's request) and the Ministers (may also include one or more Deputy Prime Ministers) ‚Äì acts as the <a href="/wiki/Cabinet_(government)" title="Cabinet (government)">cabinet</a>. Each government is required to define the broad outline of its policies in a programme, and present it to the Assembly for a mandatory period of debate. The failure of the Assembly to reject the government programme by an absolute majority of deputies confirms the cabinet in office.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Parliament">Parliament</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portugal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Parliament">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Lisbon_Portugal_116_The_Pal%C3%A1cio_de_S%C3%A3o_Bento_(5107570895).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Lisbon_Portugal_116_The_Pal%C3%A1cio_de_S%C3%A3o_Bento_%285107570895%29.jpg/200px-Lisbon_Portugal_116_The_Pal%C3%A1cio_de_S%C3%A3o_Bento_%285107570895%29.jpg" width="200" height="150" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Lisbon_Portugal_116_The_Pal%C3%A1cio_de_S%C3%A3o_Bento_%285107570895%29.jpg/300px-Lisbon_Portugal_116_The_Pal%C3%A1cio_de_S%C3%A3o_Bento_%285107570895%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Lisbon_Portugal_116_The_Pal%C3%A1cio_de_S%C3%A3o_Bento_%285107570895%29.jpg/400px-Lisbon_Portugal_116_The_Pal%C3%A1cio_de_S%C3%A3o_Bento_%285107570895%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="2448" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Lisbon_Portugal_116_The_Pal%C3%A1cio_de_S%C3%A3o_Bento_(5107570895).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Bento_Palace" title="S√£o Bento Palace">S√£o Bento Palace</a> is the seat of the <a href="/wiki/Assembly_of_the_Republic_(Portugal)" title="Assembly of the Republic (Portugal)">Portuguese Legislature</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Assembly_of_the_Republic_(Portugal)" title="Assembly of the Republic (Portugal)">Assembly of the Republic (Portugal)</a></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Assembly_of_the_Republic_(Portugal)" title="Assembly of the Republic (Portugal)">Assembly of the Republic</a> is the national <a href="/wiki/Parliament" title="Parliament">parliament</a> of Portugal. It is the main Legislative body, although the Government also has limited legislative powers.</p>
<p>The Assembly of the Republic is a unicameral body composed of up to 230 deputies. Elected by universal suffrage according to a system of proportional representation, deputies serve four-year terms of office, unless the President dissolves the Assembly and calls for new elections.</p>
<p>Currently the Government (PS) and its unofficial coalition (BE, PCP, PEV) controls parliament with the most seats. The PSD and CDS-PP form the opposition to the government alongside a single seat held by the PAN.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Law_and_criminal_justice">Law and criminal justice</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portugal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Law and criminal justice">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Pal%C3%A1cio_da_Justi%C3%A7a_(Lisbon),_Metro_Centric,_2015,_24025730286.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Pal%C3%A1cio_da_Justi%C3%A7a_%28Lisbon%29%2C_Metro_Centric%2C_2015%2C_24025730286.jpg/200px-Pal%C3%A1cio_da_Justi%C3%A7a_%28Lisbon%29%2C_Metro_Centric%2C_2015%2C_24025730286.jpg" width="200" height="133" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Pal%C3%A1cio_da_Justi%C3%A7a_%28Lisbon%29%2C_Metro_Centric%2C_2015%2C_24025730286.jpg/300px-Pal%C3%A1cio_da_Justi%C3%A7a_%28Lisbon%29%2C_Metro_Centric%2C_2015%2C_24025730286.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Pal%C3%A1cio_da_Justi%C3%A7a_%28Lisbon%29%2C_Metro_Centric%2C_2015%2C_24025730286.jpg/400px-Pal%C3%A1cio_da_Justi%C3%A7a_%28Lisbon%29%2C_Metro_Centric%2C_2015%2C_24025730286.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5184" data-file-height="3456" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Pal%C3%A1cio_da_Justi%C3%A7a_(Lisbon),_Metro_Centric,_2015,_24025730286.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Palace of Justice in Lisbon houses the courts for the judicial <i><a href="/wiki/Comarca" title="Comarca">Comarca</a></i> of <a href="/wiki/District_of_Lisbon" class="mw-redirect" title="District of Lisbon">District of Lisbon</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Judiciary_of_Portugal" title="Judiciary of Portugal">Judiciary of Portugal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Law_of_Portugal" title="Law of Portugal">Law of Portugal</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Drug_policy_of_Portugal" title="Drug policy of Portugal">Drug policy of Portugal</a></div>
<p>The Portuguese legal system is part of the civil law legal system, also called the continental family legal system. The main laws include the Constitution (1976, as amended), the <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Civil_Code" title="Portuguese Civil Code">Portuguese Civil Code</a> (1966, as amended) and the <a href="/wiki/Penal_Code_of_Portugal" title="Penal Code of Portugal">Penal Code of Portugal</a> (1982, as amended). Other relevant laws are the <i>Commercial Code</i> (1888, as amended) and the <i>Civil Procedure Code</i> (1961, as amended).</p>
<p>The supreme national courts are the <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_Justice_(Portugal)" title="Supreme Court of Justice (Portugal)">Supreme Court of Justice</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Constitutional_Court_of_Portugal" class="mw-redirect" title="Constitutional Court of Portugal">Constitutional Court</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Public_Ministry_(Portugal)" title="Public Ministry (Portugal)">Public Ministry</a>, headed by the Attorney General of the Republic, constitutes the independent body of public prosecutors.</p>
<p>Portuguese law applied in the former <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_colonies" class="mw-redirect" title="Portuguese colonies">colonies and territories</a> and continues to be the major influence for those countries.</p>
<p>Portugal was one of the first countries in the world to abolish the death penalty. Maximum jail sentences are limited to 25 years.</p>
<p>Portugal is also known for having decriminalized the usage of all common drugs in 2001, the first country in the world to do so. Portugal decriminalized possession of effectively all drugs that are still illegal in other developed nations including <a href="/wiki/Cannabis" title="Cannabis">cannabis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cocaine" title="Cocaine">cocaine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Heroin" title="Heroin">heroin</a>, and <a href="/wiki/LSD" class="mw-redirect" title="LSD">LSD</a>. While possession is legal, trafficking and possession of more than "10 days worth of personal use" are still punishable by jail time and fines. People caught with small amounts of any drug are given the choice to go to a rehab facility, and may refuse treatment without consequences. Despite criticism from other European nations, who stated Portugal's drug consumption would tremendously increase, overall drug use has declined along with the number of <a href="/wiki/HIV" title="HIV">HIV</a> infection cases, which had dropped 50 percent by 2009. Drug use among 16- to 18-year-olds also declined, however the use of marijuana rose only slightly among that age group.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">[58]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">[59]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[60]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 31 May 2010, Portugal became the sixth country in Europe and the eighth country in the world to legally recognize <a href="/wiki/Same-sex_marriage_in_Portugal" title="Same-sex marriage in Portugal">same-sex marriage</a> on the national level. The law came into force on 5 June 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated2_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2-62">[61]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Law_enforcement">Law enforcement</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portugal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Law enforcement">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Render_da_Guarda_no_Palacio_de_Belem_22.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Render_da_Guarda_no_Palacio_de_Belem_22.JPG/200px-Render_da_Guarda_no_Palacio_de_Belem_22.JPG" width="200" height="301" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Render_da_Guarda_no_Palacio_de_Belem_22.JPG/300px-Render_da_Guarda_no_Palacio_de_Belem_22.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Render_da_Guarda_no_Palacio_de_Belem_22.JPG/400px-Render_da_Guarda_no_Palacio_de_Belem_22.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2848" data-file-height="4288" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Render_da_Guarda_no_Palacio_de_Belem_22.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A cavalryman of the <a href="/wiki/National_Republican_Guard_(Portugal)" title="National Republican Guard (Portugal)">National Republican Guard</a>'s honor guard.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Law_enforcement_in_Portugal" title="Law enforcement in Portugal">Law enforcement in Portugal</a></div>
<p>Portugal's main police organizations are the <i><a href="/wiki/Guarda_Nacional_Republicana" class="mw-redirect" title="Guarda Nacional Republicana">Guarda Nacional Republicana</a>&#160;‚Äì GNR</i> (<a href="/wiki/National_Republican_Guard_(Portugal)" title="National Republican Guard (Portugal)">National Republican Guard</a>), a <a href="/wiki/Gendarmerie" title="Gendarmerie">gendarmerie</a>; the <i><a href="/wiki/Pol%C3%ADcia_de_Seguran%C3%A7a_P%C3%BAblica" title="Pol√≠cia de Seguran√ßa P√∫blica">Pol√≠cia de Seguran√ßa P√∫blica</a>&#160;‚Äì PSP</i> (Public Security Police), a civilian police force who work in urban areas; and the <i><a href="/wiki/Pol%C3%ADcia_Judici%C3%A1ria" title="Pol√≠cia Judici√°ria">Pol√≠cia Judici√°ria</a>&#160;‚Äì PJ</i> (Judicial Police), a highly specialized criminal investigation police that is overseen by the <a href="/wiki/Public_Ministry_(Portugal)" title="Public Ministry (Portugal)">Public Ministry</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">Administrative divisions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portugal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Administrative divisions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Administrative_divisions_of_Portugal" title="Administrative divisions of Portugal">Administrative divisions of Portugal</a></div>
<p>Administratively, Portugal is divided into 308 <a href="/wiki/Municipalities_of_Portugal" title="Municipalities of Portugal">municipalities</a> (<a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">Portuguese</a>: <span lang="pt"><i>munic√≠pios or <a href="/wiki/Concelhos" class="mw-redirect" title="Concelhos">concelhos</a></i></span>), which after a reform in <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_local_election,_2013" class="mw-redirect" title="Portuguese local election, 2013">2013</a> are subdivided into 3,092 civil parishes (<a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">Portuguese</a>: <span lang="pt"><i><a href="/wiki/Freguesia" title="Freguesia">freguesia</a></i></span>). Operationally, the municipality and civil parish, along with the national government, are the only legally identifiable <a href="/wiki/Local_administrative_unit" title="Local administrative unit">local administrative units</a> identified by the government of Portugal (for example, cities, towns or villages have no standing in law, although may be used as catchment for the defining services). For statistical purposes the Portuguese government also identifies <a href="/wiki/Nomenclature_of_Territorial_Units_for_Statistics" title="Nomenclature of Territorial Units for Statistics">NUTS</a>, inter-municipal communities and informally, the district system, used until European integration (and being phased-out by the national government).<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:No_original_research" title="Wikipedia:No original research"><span title="The material near this tag possibly contains original research. (February 2016)">original research?</span></a></i>]</sup> Continental Portugal is agglomerated into 18 districts, while the archipelagos of the Azores and Madeira are governed as <a href="/wiki/Autonomous_area" class="mw-redirect" title="Autonomous area">autonomous regions</a>; the largest units, established since 1976, are either <a href="/wiki/Mainland_Portugal" class="mw-redirect" title="Mainland Portugal">mainland Portugal</a> (<a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">Portuguese</a>: <span lang="pt"><i>Portugal Continental</i></span>) and the <a href="/wiki/Autonomous_regions_of_Portugal" class="mw-redirect" title="Autonomous regions of Portugal">autonomous regions of Portugal</a> (<a href="/wiki/Azores" title="Azores">Azores</a> and <a href="/wiki/Madeira" title="Madeira">Madeira</a>).</p>
<p>The 18 districts of mainland Portugal are: <a href="/wiki/Aveiro_District" title="Aveiro District">Aveiro</a>, <a href="/wiki/Beja_District" title="Beja District">Beja</a>, <a href="/wiki/Braga_District" title="Braga District">Braga</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bragan%C3%A7a_District" title="Bragan√ßa District">Bragan√ßa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Castelo_Branco_District" title="Castelo Branco District">Castelo Branco</a>, <a href="/wiki/Coimbra_District" title="Coimbra District">Coimbra</a>, <a href="/wiki/%C3%89vora_District" title="√âvora District">√âvora</a>, <a href="/wiki/Faro_District" title="Faro District">Faro</a>, <a href="/wiki/Guarda_District" title="Guarda District">Guarda</a>, <a href="/wiki/Leiria_District" title="Leiria District">Leiria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lisbon_District" title="Lisbon District">Lisbon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Portalegre_District" title="Portalegre District">Portalegre</a>, <a href="/wiki/Porto_District" title="Porto District">Porto</a>, <a href="/wiki/Santar%C3%A9m_District" title="Santar√©m District">Santar√©m</a>, <a href="/wiki/Set%C3%BAbal_District" title="Set√∫bal District">Set√∫bal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Viana_do_Castelo_District" title="Viana do Castelo District">Viana do Castelo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vila_Real_District" title="Vila Real District">Vila Real</a> and <a href="/wiki/Viseu_District" title="Viseu District">Viseu</a>&#160;‚Äì each district takes the name of the district capital.</p>
<p>Within the European Union NUTS (<a href="/wiki/Nomenclature_of_Territorial_Units_for_Statistics" title="Nomenclature of Territorial Units for Statistics">Nomenclature of Territorial Units for Statistics</a>) system, Portugal is divided into seven regions: the <a href="/wiki/Azores" title="Azores">Azores</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alentejo" title="Alentejo">Alentejo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Algarve" title="Algarve">Algarve</a>, <a href="/wiki/Centro,_Portugal" class="mw-redirect" title="Centro, Portugal">Centro</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lisboa_Region" title="Lisboa Region">Lisboa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Madeira" title="Madeira">Madeira</a> and <a href="/wiki/Norte,_Portugal" class="mw-redirect" title="Norte, Portugal">Norte</a>, and with the exception of the Azores and Madeira, these NUTS areas are subdivided into 28 subregions.</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_relations">Foreign relations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portugal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Foreign relations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Pal%C3%A1cio_das_Necessidades_1997.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Pal%C3%A1cio_das_Necessidades_1997.JPG/200px-Pal%C3%A1cio_das_Necessidades_1997.JPG" width="200" height="150" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Pal%C3%A1cio_das_Necessidades_1997.JPG/300px-Pal%C3%A1cio_das_Necessidades_1997.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Pal%C3%A1cio_das_Necessidades_1997.JPG/400px-Pal%C3%A1cio_das_Necessidades_1997.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2608" data-file-height="1952" /></a>

<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Flickr_-_Minist%C3%A9rio_da_Cultura_-_VII_Reuni%C3%A3o_de_Ministros_da_Cultura_da_CPLP_(1).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Community_of_Portuguese_Language_Countries" title="Community of Portuguese Language Countries">Community of Portuguese Language Countries</a> (CPLP) is headquartered in Lisbon.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Portugal" title="Foreign relations of Portugal">Foreign relations of Portugal</a></div>
<p>A member state of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> since 1955, Portugal is also a founding member of <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a> (1949), <a href="/wiki/OECD" class="mw-redirect" title="OECD">OECD</a> (1961) and <a href="/wiki/European_Free_Trade_Association" title="European Free Trade Association">EFTA</a> (1960); it left the latter in 1986 to join the <a href="/wiki/European_Economic_Community" title="European Economic Community">European Economic Community</a>, which became the European Union in 1993. In 1996 it co-founded the <a href="/wiki/Community_of_Portuguese_Language_Countries" title="Community of Portuguese Language Countries">Community of Portuguese Language Countries</a> (CPLP), which seeks to foster closer economic and cultural ties between the world's <a href="/wiki/Lusophone" title="Lusophone">Lusophone</a> nations.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Ant%C3%B3nio_Guterres" title="Ant√≥nio Guterres">Ant√≥nio Guterres</a>, who has served as Prime Minister of Portugal from 1995 to 2002 and <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_High_Commissioner_for_Refugees" title="United Nations High Commissioner for Refugees">UN High Commissioner for Refugees</a> from 2005 to 2015, assumed the post of <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Secretary-General" class="mw-redirect" title="United Nations Secretary-General">UN Secretary-General</a>; making him the first Secretary-General from Western Europe since Kurt Waldheim of Austria (1972‚Äì1981), the first former head of government to become Secretary-General and the first Secretary-General born after the establishment of the United Nations on June 26, 1945.</p>
<p>In addition, Portugal is a full member of the <a href="/wiki/Latin_Union" title="Latin Union">Latin Union</a> (1983) and the <a href="/wiki/Organization_of_Ibero-American_States" title="Organization of Ibero-American States">Organization of Ibero-American States</a> (1949). It has a friendship alliance and <a href="/wiki/Multiple_citizenship" title="Multiple citizenship">dual citizenship</a> treaty with its former colony, Brazil. Portugal and England (subsequently, the United Kingdom of Great Britain and Northern Ireland) share the world's oldest active military accord through their <a href="/wiki/Anglo-Portuguese_Alliance" title="Anglo-Portuguese Alliance">Anglo-Portuguese Alliance</a> (<a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Windsor_(1386)" title="Treaty of Windsor (1386)">Treaty of Windsor</a>), which was signed in 1373.</p>
<p>There are two international territorial disputes, both with Spain:</p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Olivenza" title="Olivenza">Olivenza</a>. Under Portuguese sovereignty since 1297, the municipality of Olivenza was ceded to Spain under the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Badajoz_(1801)" title="Treaty of Badajoz (1801)">Treaty of Badajoz</a> in 1801, after the <a href="/wiki/War_of_the_Oranges" title="War of the Oranges">War of the Oranges</a>. Portugal claimed it back in 1815 under the <a href="/wiki/Congress_of_Vienna" title="Congress of Vienna">Treaty of Vienna</a>. However, since the 19th century, it has been continuously ruled by Spain which considers the territory theirs not only <i>de facto</i> but also <i>de jure</i>.</li>
<li>The Ilhas Selvagens (<a href="/wiki/Savage_Islands" title="Savage Islands">Savage Islands</a>). The archipelago is under Portuguese domination but is geographically closer to the <a href="/wiki/Canary_Islands" title="Canary Islands">Canary Islands</a> (165&#160;km) than to <a href="/wiki/Madeira" title="Madeira">Madeira</a> (280&#160;km). Found in 1364 by Italian navigators, the islands belonged to private owners until 1971, when the Portuguese government bought them and established a natural reserve area covering the whole archipelago. The islands have been claimed by Spain since 1911 and the dispute has caused some periods of political tension between the two countries. The main problem is not so much their intrinsic value but the fact that they expand considerably to the south the <a href="/wiki/Exclusive_Economic_Zone" class="mw-redirect" title="Exclusive Economic Zone">Exclusive Economic Zone</a> of Portugal.</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Military">Military</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portugal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Military">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Armed_Forces" title="Portuguese Armed Forces">Portuguese Armed Forces</a></div>
<p>The armed forces have three branches: <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Navy" title="Portuguese Navy">Navy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Army" title="Portuguese Army">Army</a> and <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Air_Force" title="Portuguese Air Force">Air Force</a>. They serve primarily as a self-defense force whose mission is to protect the territorial integrity of the country and provide humanitarian assistance and security at home and abroad. As of 2008<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Portugal&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, the three branches numbered 39,200 active personnel including 7,500 women. <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_military_expenditures" title="List of countries by military expenditures">Portuguese military expenditure</a> in 2009 was $5.2 billion, representing 2.1 percent of GDP. Military conscription was abolished in 2004. The minimum age for voluntary recruitment is 18 years.</p>
<p>The Army (21,000 personnel) comprises three brigades and other small units. An <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Intervention_Brigade" class="mw-redirect" title="Portuguese Intervention Brigade">infantry brigade</a> (mainly equipped with <a href="/wiki/Pandur_II" title="Pandur II">Pandur II</a> <a href="/wiki/Armoured_personnel_carrier" title="Armoured personnel carrier">APC</a>), a <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Mechanized_Brigade" title="Portuguese Mechanized Brigade">mechanized brigade</a> (mainly equipped with <a href="/wiki/Leopard_2" title="Leopard 2">Leopard 2 A6</a> tanks and <a href="/wiki/M113" class="mw-redirect" title="M113">M113</a> APC) and a <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Rapid_Reaction_Brigade" class="mw-redirect" title="Portuguese Rapid Reaction Brigade">Rapid Reaction Brigade</a> (consisting of paratroopers, <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Army_Commandos" title="Portuguese Army Commandos">commandos</a> and rangers). The Navy (10,700 personnel, of which 1,580 are <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Marines" class="mw-redirect" title="Portuguese Marines">marines</a>) has five frigates, seven corvettes, two submarines, and 28 patrol and auxiliary vessels. The Air Force (7,500 personnel) has the <a href="/wiki/Lockheed_F-16_Fighting_Falcon" class="mw-redirect" title="Lockheed F-16 Fighting Falcon">Lockheed F-16 Fighting Falcon</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Dassault/Dornier_Alpha_Jet" title="Dassault/Dornier Alpha Jet">Dassault/Dornier Alpha Jet</a> as the main combat aircraft.</p>
<table class="toccolours" style="float:right; margin:0 0 1em 1em; border:1px #ddd solid;">
<caption><b>Branches of the Portuguese Armed Forces</b></caption>
<tr style="text-align:center;">

<a href="/wiki/MEKO_200" title="MEKO 200">MEKO-200 PN</a></small></td>

<small><a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Air_Force" title="Portuguese Air Force">Portuguese Air Force</a><br />
<a href="/wiki/General_Dynamics_F-16_Fighting_Falcon" title="General Dynamics F-16 Fighting Falcon">F-16 Fighting Falcon</a></small></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>In addition to the three branches of the armed forces, there is the <a href="/wiki/National_Republican_Guard_(Portugal)" title="National Republican Guard (Portugal)">National Republican Guard</a>, a security force subject to military law and organization (<a href="/wiki/Gendarmerie" title="Gendarmerie">gendarmerie</a>) comprising 25,000 personnel. This force is under the authority of both the Defense and the Interior Ministry. It has provided detachments for participation in international operations in Iraq and East Timor.</p>
<p>The United States maintains a military presence with 770 troops in the <a href="/wiki/Lajes_Air_Base" class="mw-redirect" title="Lajes Air Base">Lajes Air Base</a> at <a href="/wiki/Terceira_Island" title="Terceira Island">Terceira Island</a>, in the Azores. The <a href="/wiki/Allied_Joint_Force_Command_Lisbon" title="Allied Joint Force Command Lisbon">Allied Joint Force Command Lisbon</a> (JFC Lisbon)&#160;‚Äì one of the three main subdivisions of <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Allied_Command_Operations" class="mw-redirect" title="Allied Command Operations">Allied Command Operations</a>&#160;‚Äì it is based in <a href="/wiki/Oeiras_Municipality,_Portugal" class="mw-redirect" title="Oeiras Municipality, Portugal">Oeiras</a>, near Lisbon.</p>
<p>In the 20th century, Portugal engaged in two major conflicts: <a href="/wiki/Portugal_in_the_Great_War" class="mw-redirect" title="Portugal in the Great War">World War I</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Colonial_War" title="Portuguese Colonial War">Portuguese Colonial War</a> (1961‚Äì1974). After the end of the <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Empire" title="Portuguese Empire">Portuguese Empire</a> in 1975, the Portuguese Armed Forces have participated in peacekeeping missions in East Timor, Bosnia, Kosovo, Afghanistan, Somalia, Iraq (<a href="/wiki/Nasiriyah" title="Nasiriyah">Nasiriyah</a>) and Lebanon. Portugal also conducted several independent unilateral military operations abroad, as were the cases of the interventions of the Portuguese Armed Forces in Angola in 1992 and in Guinea-Bissau in 1998 with the main objectives of protecting and withdrawing of Portuguese and foreign citizens threatened by local civil conflicts.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Government_finance">Government finance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portugal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Government finance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Further information: <a href="/wiki/2010%E2%80%9314_Portuguese_financial_crisis" title="2010‚Äì14 Portuguese financial crisis">2010‚Äì14 Portuguese financial crisis</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Portuguese_debt_and_EU_average.png" class="image"><img alt="Portuguese debt compared to Eurozone average" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Portuguese_debt_and_EU_average.png/200px-Portuguese_debt_and_EU_average.png" width="200" height="194" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Portuguese_debt_and_EU_average.png/300px-Portuguese_debt_and_EU_average.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Portuguese_debt_and_EU_average.png/400px-Portuguese_debt_and_EU_average.png 2x" data-file-width="703" data-file-height="681" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Portuguese_debt_and_EU_average.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Debt as a percentage of the <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Portugal" title="Economy of Portugal">economy of Portugal</a>, compared to eurozone average.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Portuguese government is heavily indebted, and received a 78 billion euro bailout from the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> and the <a href="/wiki/International_Monetary_Fund" title="International Monetary Fund">International Monetary Fund</a> in May 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-nytimes_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nytimes-64">[63]</a></sup> The ratio of Portugal‚Äôs debt to its overall economy, was 107 percent when it received the bailout.<sup id="cite_ref-nytimes_64-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nytimes-64">[63]</a></sup> As part of the deal, the country agreed to cut its budget deficit from 9.8 percent of GDP in 2010 to 5.9 percent in 2011, 4.5 percent in 2012 and 3 percent in 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-reuters1_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-reuters1-65">[64]</a></sup></p>
<p>After the bailout was announced, the Portuguese government headed by <a href="/wiki/Pedro_Passos_Coelho" title="Pedro Passos Coelho">Pedro Passos Coelho</a> managed to implement measures with the intention of improving the state's financial situation, including tax hikes, a freeze of civil service-related lower-wages and cuts of higher-wages by 14.3%, on top of the government's spending cuts. The Portuguese government also agreed to eliminate its <a href="/wiki/Golden_share" title="Golden share">golden share</a> in <a href="/wiki/Portugal_Telecom" title="Portugal Telecom">Portugal Telecom</a> which gave it veto power over vital decisions.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">[65]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[66]</a></sup> In 2012, all public servants had already seen an average wage cut of 20% relative to their 2010 baseline, with cuts reaching 25% for those earning more than 1,500 euro per month.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">[67]</a></sup></p>
<p>The IMF, the <a href="/wiki/European_Commission" title="European Commission">European Commission</a> (EC) and the <a href="/wiki/European_Central_Bank" title="European Central Bank">European Central Bank</a> (ECB) said in September 2012 that Portugal‚Äôs debt would peak at 124 percent of gross domestic product in 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-October_2012_status_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-October_2012_status-69">[68]</a></sup> The IMF previously said in July 2012 that Portugal‚Äôs debt would peak at about 118.5 percent of GDP in 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-October_2012_status_69-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-October_2012_status-69">[68]</a></sup> In September 2013, the Portuguese Government reviewed again the public debt of Portugal for 2013 to 127.8 percent, after a peak of 130.9 percent in that month.<sup id="cite_ref-September_2013_status_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-September_2013_status-70">[69]</a></sup></p>
<p>A report released in January 2011 by the <a href="/wiki/Di%C3%A1rio_de_Not%C3%ADcias" title="Di√°rio de Not√≠cias">Di√°rio de Not√≠cias</a><sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">[70]</a></sup> and published in Portugal by <a href="/wiki/Gradiva" title="Gradiva">Gradiva</a>, had demonstrated that in the period between the <a href="/wiki/Carnation_Revolution" title="Carnation Revolution">Carnation Revolution</a> in 1974 and 2010, the democratic <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Portugal" title="Government of Portugal">Portuguese Republic governments</a> encouraged over-expenditure and investment bubbles through unclear <a href="/wiki/Public%E2%80%93private_partnership" title="Public‚Äìprivate partnership">Public‚Äìprivate partnerships</a> and funding of numerous ineffective and unnecessary external consultancy and advisory of committees and firms. This allowed considerable <a href="/wiki/Slippage_(finance)" title="Slippage (finance)">slippage</a> in state-managed <a href="/wiki/Public_works" title="Public works">public works</a> and inflated top management and head officer bonuses and wages. Persistent and lasting recruitment policies boosted the number of redundant public servants. Risky <a href="/wiki/Credit_(finance)" title="Credit (finance)">credit</a>, <a href="/wiki/Public_debt" class="mw-redirect" title="Public debt">public debt</a> creation, and European <a href="/wiki/Structural_and_cohesion_funds" class="mw-redirect" title="Structural and cohesion funds">structural and cohesion funds</a> were mismanaged across almost four decades.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">[71]</a></sup></p>
<p>After the <a href="/wiki/Financial_crisis_of_2007%E2%80%9308" class="mw-redirect" title="Financial crisis of 2007‚Äì08">financial crisis of 2007‚Äì08</a>, it was known in 2008‚Äì2009 that two Portuguese banks (<a href="/wiki/Banco_Portugu%C3%AAs_de_Neg%C3%B3cios" title="Banco Portugu√™s de Neg√≥cios">Banco Portugu√™s de Neg√≥cios</a> (BPN) and <a href="/wiki/Banco_Privado_Portugu%C3%AAs" title="Banco Privado Portugu√™s">Banco Privado Portugu√™s</a> (BPP)) had been accumulating losses for years due to bad investments, embezzlement and accounting fraud. The case of BPN was particularly serious because of its size, market share, and the political implications ‚Äì Portugal's then current President, Cavaco Silva, and some of his political allies, maintained personal and business relationships with the bank and its CEO, who was eventually charged and arrested for fraud and other crimes.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">[72]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">[73]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">[74]</a></sup> In the grounds of avoiding a potentially serious financial crisis in the Portuguese economy, the Portuguese government decided to give them a bailout, eventually at a future loss to taxpayers and to the Portuguese people in general.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portugal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Portugal" title="Economy of Portugal">Economy of Portugal</a> and <a href="/wiki/Economic_history_of_Portugal" title="Economic history of Portugal">Economic history of Portugal</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Portugal_Export_Treemap.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Portugal_Export_Treemap.png/200px-Portugal_Export_Treemap.png" width="200" height="156" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Portugal_Export_Treemap.png/300px-Portugal_Export_Treemap.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Portugal_Export_Treemap.png/400px-Portugal_Export_Treemap.png 2x" data-file-width="853" data-file-height="667" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Portugal_Export_Treemap.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A proportional representation of Portugal's exports, as of 2012<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Portugal&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Portugal is a <a href="/wiki/Developed_countries" class="mw-redirect" title="Developed countries">developed</a> and a <a href="/wiki/High_income_countries" class="mw-redirect" title="High income countries">high income country</a>, with its GDP per capita in 2014 being 78% of the EU27 average ‚Äì increasing from 76% in 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">[75]</a></sup> The Portuguese currency is the <a href="/wiki/Euro" title="Euro">euro</a> (‚Ç¨), which replaced the <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Escudo" class="mw-redirect" title="Portuguese Escudo">Portuguese Escudo</a>, and the country was one of the original member states of the <a href="/wiki/Eurozone" title="Eurozone">eurozone</a>. Portugal's central bank is the <i><a href="/wiki/Banco_de_Portugal" title="Banco de Portugal">Banco de Portugal</a></i>, an integral part of the <a href="/wiki/European_System_of_Central_Banks" title="European System of Central Banks">European System of Central Banks</a>. Most industries, businesses and financial institutions are concentrated in the <a href="/wiki/Lisbon_Metropolitan_Area" title="Lisbon Metropolitan Area">Lisbon</a> and <a href="/wiki/Greater_Metropolitan_Area_of_Porto" class="mw-redirect" title="Greater Metropolitan Area of Porto">Porto</a> metropolitan areas‚Äîthe <a href="/wiki/Set%C3%BAbal_District" title="Set√∫bal District">Set√∫bal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aveiro_District" title="Aveiro District">Aveiro</a>, <a href="/wiki/Braga_District" title="Braga District">Braga</a>, <a href="/wiki/Coimbra_District" title="Coimbra District">Coimbra</a> and <a href="/wiki/Leiria_District" title="Leiria District">Leiria</a> districts are the biggest economic centres outside these two main areas. According to World Travel Awards, Portugal is Europe's Leading Golf Destination 2012 and 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">[76]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">[77]</a></sup></p>
<p>Since the <a href="/wiki/Carnation_Revolution" title="Carnation Revolution">Carnation Revolution</a> of 1974, which culminated in the end of one of Portugal's most notable <a href="/wiki/Economic_history_of_Portugal" title="Economic history of Portugal">phases of economic expansion</a> (that started in the 1960s),<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">[78]</a></sup> a significant change has occurred in the nation's annual economic growth.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> After the turmoil of the 1974 revolution and the <a href="/wiki/PREC" class="mw-redirect" title="PREC">PREC</a> period, Portugal tried to adapt to a changing <a href="/wiki/Globalization" title="Globalization">modern global economy</a>, a process that continues in 2013. Since the 1990s, Portugal's <a href="/wiki/Consumption_(economics)" title="Consumption (economics)">public consumption</a>-based <a href="/wiki/Economic_development" title="Economic development">economic development</a> model has been slowly changing to a system that is focused on exports, <a href="/wiki/Investment" title="Investment">private investment</a> and the development of the <a href="/wiki/High-tech" class="mw-redirect" title="High-tech">high-tech</a> sector. Consequently, business services have overtaken more traditional industries such as textiles, clothing, footwear and <a href="/wiki/Cork_(material)" title="Cork (material)">cork</a> (Portugal is the world's leading cork producer),<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">[79]</a></sup> wood products and beverages.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-81">[80]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:November_2011_Austerity_Protest_in_Lisbon,_Portugal.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/November_2011_Austerity_Protest_in_Lisbon%2C_Portugal.JPG/200px-November_2011_Austerity_Protest_in_Lisbon%2C_Portugal.JPG" width="200" height="114" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/November_2011_Austerity_Protest_in_Lisbon%2C_Portugal.JPG/300px-November_2011_Austerity_Protest_in_Lisbon%2C_Portugal.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/November_2011_Austerity_Protest_in_Lisbon%2C_Portugal.JPG/400px-November_2011_Austerity_Protest_in_Lisbon%2C_Portugal.JPG 2x" data-file-width="4592" data-file-height="2615" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:November_2011_Austerity_Protest_in_Lisbon,_Portugal.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
November 2011 protests against austerity measures outside the <a href="/wiki/Assembly_of_the_Republic_(Portugal)" title="Assembly of the Republic (Portugal)">Assembly of the Republic</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In the second decade of the 21st century the Portuguese economy suffered its most severe recession since the 1970s resulting in the country having to be bailed out by the European Commission, European Central Bank and International Monetary Fund. The bailout, agreed to in 2011, required Portugal to enter into a range of austerity measures in exchange for funding support of ‚Ç¨78 billion. In May 2014 the country exited the bailout but reaffirmed its commitment to maintaining its reformist momentum. At the time of exiting the bailout the economy had contracted by 0.7% in the first quarter of 2014, however unemployment, while still high had fallen to 15.3 percent.<sup id="cite_ref-PortugalBailoutEnds_82-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PortugalBailoutEnds-82">[81]</a></sup></p>
<p>The average wage in Portugal is 910 ‚Ç¨ per month (net), excluding self-employed individuals<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">[82]</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Minimum_wage" title="Minimum wage">minimum wage</a>, which is regulated/ref by law, is ‚Ç¨530 per month (paid 14 times per annum).</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Global_Competitiveness_Report" title="Global Competitiveness Report">Global Competitiveness Report</a> for 2014‚Äì2015, published by the <a href="/wiki/World_Economic_Forum" title="World Economic Forum">World Economic Forum</a>, placed Portugal on the 36th position on the economic index. This represents a sharp increase from the 51st position where Portugal appeared in 2013‚Äì2014.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Economist_Intelligence_Unit" title="Economist Intelligence Unit">Economist Intelligence Unit</a>'s quality of life index placed Portugal as the country with the 19th-best quality of life in the world for 2005, ahead of other economically and technologically advanced countries like France, Germany, the United Kingdom and South Korea, but 9 places behind its only neighbour, Spain.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">[83]</a></sup> This is despite the fact that Portugal remains one of the countries with the lowest per capita GDP in Western Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-economia.publico.clix.pt_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-economia.publico.clix.pt-85">[84]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Gold_Reserves.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Gold_Reserves.png/200px-Gold_Reserves.png" width="200" height="91" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Gold_Reserves.png/300px-Gold_Reserves.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Gold_Reserves.png/400px-Gold_Reserves.png 2x" data-file-width="3600" data-file-height="1640" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Gold_Reserves.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Portugal has the 13th largest <a href="/wiki/Gold_reserve" title="Gold reserve">gold reserve</a> in the world</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Major <a href="/wiki/Government-owned_corporation" class="mw-redirect" title="Government-owned corporation">State-owned companies</a> include <a href="/wiki/%C3%81guas_de_Portugal" title="√Åguas de Portugal">√Åguas de Portugal</a> (water), <a href="/wiki/Caixa_Geral_de_Dep%C3%B3sitos" title="Caixa Geral de Dep√≥sitos">Caixa Geral de Dep√≥sitos</a> (banking), <a href="/wiki/Comboios_de_Portugal" title="Comboios de Portugal">Comboios de Portugal</a> (railways), <a href="/wiki/Companhia_das_Lez%C3%ADrias" title="Companhia das Lez√≠rias">Companhia das Lez√≠rias</a> (agriculture) and <a href="/wiki/R%C3%A1dio_e_Televis%C3%A3o_de_Portugal" title="R√°dio e Televis√£o de Portugal">RTP</a> (media). Some former state-owned entities are managed by state-run <a href="/wiki/Holding_company" title="Holding company">holding company</a> <a href="/wiki/Parp%C3%BAblica" title="Parp√∫blica">Parp√∫blica</a>, which is a <a href="/wiki/Shareholder" title="Shareholder">shareholder</a> of several public and private companies.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Among former State owned companies recently privatized are <a href="/wiki/CTT_Correios_de_Portugal,_S.A." title="CTT Correios de Portugal, S.A.">CTT</a> (postal service), <a href="/wiki/TAP_Portugal" title="TAP Portugal">TAP Portugal</a> (airline) and <a href="/wiki/ANA_Aeroportos_de_Portugal" title="ANA Aeroportos de Portugal">ANA</a> (airports).</p>
<p>Companies listed on <a href="/wiki/Euronext_Lisbon" title="Euronext Lisbon">Euronext Lisbon</a> <a href="/wiki/Stock_exchange" title="Stock exchange">stock exchange</a> like <a href="/wiki/Energias_de_Portugal" title="Energias de Portugal">EDP</a>, <a href="/wiki/Galp_Energia" title="Galp Energia">Galp</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jer%C3%B3nimo_Martins" title="Jer√≥nimo Martins">Jer√≥nimo Martins</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mota-Engil" title="Mota-Engil">Mota-Engil</a>, <a href="/wiki/Novabase" title="Novabase">Novabase</a>, <a href="/wiki/Semapa" title="Semapa">Semapa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Portucel_Soporcel" title="Portucel Soporcel">Portucel Soporcel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Portugal_Telecom" title="Portugal Telecom">Portugal Telecom</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sonae" title="Sonae">Sonae</a>, are among the largest corporations of Portugal by number of employees, <a href="/wiki/Net_income" title="Net income">net income</a> or international <a href="/wiki/Market_share" title="Market share">market share</a>. The Euronext Lisbon is the major stock exchange of Portugal and is part of the <a href="/wiki/NYSE_Euronext" title="NYSE Euronext">NYSE Euronext</a>, the first global stock exchange. The <a href="/wiki/PSI-20" title="PSI-20">PSI-20</a> is Portugal's most selective and widely known <a href="/wiki/Stock_index" class="mw-redirect" title="Stock index">stock index</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Primary_sector">Primary sector</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portugal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Primary sector">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Agriculture_in_Portugal" title="Agriculture in Portugal">Agriculture in Portugal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fishing_in_Portugal" title="Fishing in Portugal">Fishing in Portugal</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Mining_in_Portugal" title="Mining in Portugal">Mining in Portugal</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Alentejo_oak_on_wheat_field.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Alentejo_oak_on_wheat_field.jpg/200px-Alentejo_oak_on_wheat_field.jpg" width="200" height="150" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Alentejo_oak_on_wheat_field.jpg/300px-Alentejo_oak_on_wheat_field.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Alentejo_oak_on_wheat_field.jpg/400px-Alentejo_oak_on_wheat_field.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="600" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Alentejo_oak_on_wheat_field.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Alentejo" title="Alentejo">Alentejo</a> is known as the "bread basket of Portugal", being the country's leading region in wheat and cork production.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Agriculture_in_Portugal" title="Agriculture in Portugal">Agriculture in Portugal</a> is based on small to medium-sized family-owned dispersed units. However, the sector also includes larger scale <a href="/wiki/Intensive_farming" title="Intensive farming">intensive farming</a> export-oriented <a href="/wiki/Agrobusiness" class="mw-redirect" title="Agrobusiness">agrobusinesses</a> backed by companies (like <a href="/wiki/Grupo_RAR" title="Grupo RAR">Grupo RAR</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Vitacress" title="Vitacress">Vitacress</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sovena" class="mw-redirect" title="Sovena">Sovena</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lactogal" title="Lactogal">Lactogal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vale_da_Rosa" title="Vale da Rosa">Vale da Rosa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Companhia_das_Lez%C3%ADrias" title="Companhia das Lez√≠rias">Companhia das Lez√≠rias</a> and <a href="/wiki/Valouro" title="Valouro">Valouro</a>). The country produces a wide variety of crops and livestock products, including <a href="/wiki/Tomato" title="Tomato">tomatoes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Citrus" title="Citrus">citrus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Green_vegetables" class="mw-redirect" title="Green vegetables">green vegetables</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rice" title="Rice">rice</a>, <a href="/wiki/Corn" class="mw-redirect" title="Corn">corn</a>, <a href="/wiki/Barley" title="Barley">barley</a>, <a href="/wiki/Olive" title="Olive">olives</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oilseed" class="mw-redirect" title="Oilseed">oilseeds</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nut_(fruit)" title="Nut (fruit)">nuts</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cherry" title="Cherry">cherries</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bilberry" title="Bilberry">bilberry</a>, <a href="/wiki/Table_grapes" class="mw-redirect" title="Table grapes">table grapes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Edible_mushroom" title="Edible mushroom">edible mushrooms</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dairy_products" class="mw-redirect" title="Dairy products">dairy products</a>, <a href="/wiki/Poultry" title="Poultry">poultry</a> and <a href="/wiki/Beef" title="Beef">beef</a>.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Forestry" title="Forestry">Forestry</a> has also played an important economic role among the rural communities and industry (namely <a href="/wiki/Paper_industry" class="mw-redirect" title="Paper industry">paper industry</a> that includes <a href="/wiki/Portucel_Soporcel_Group" class="mw-redirect" title="Portucel Soporcel Group">Portucel Soporcel Group</a>, <a href="/wiki/Engineered_wood" title="Engineered wood">engineered wood</a> that includes <a href="/wiki/Sonae_Ind%C3%BAstria" title="Sonae Ind√∫stria">Sonae Ind√∫stria</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Furniture" title="Furniture">furniture</a> that includes several manufacturing plants in and around <a href="/wiki/Pa%C3%A7os_de_Ferreira" title="Pa√ßos de Ferreira">Pa√ßos de Ferreira</a>, the core of Portugal's major industrial operations of <a href="/wiki/IKEA" title="IKEA">IKEA</a>). In 2001, the gross agricultural product accounted for 4 per cent of the national GDP.</p>
<p>Traditionally a sea-power, Portugal has had a strong tradition in <a href="/wiki/Fishing_in_Portugal" title="Fishing in Portugal">the Portuguese fishing sector</a> and is one of the countries with the highest fish consumption per capita.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">[85]</a></sup> The main landing sites in Portugal (including Azores and Madeira), according to total landings in weight by year, are the harbours of <a href="/wiki/Matosinhos" title="Matosinhos">Matosinhos</a>, <a href="/wiki/Peniche,_Portugal" title="Peniche, Portugal">Peniche</a>, <a href="/wiki/Olh%C3%A3o" title="Olh√£o">Olh√£o</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sesimbra" title="Sesimbra">Sesimbra</a>, <a href="/wiki/Figueira_da_Foz" title="Figueira da Foz">Figueira da Foz</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sines,_Portugal" class="mw-redirect" title="Sines, Portugal">Sines</a>, <a href="/wiki/Portim%C3%A3o" title="Portim√£o">Portim√£o</a> and <a href="/wiki/Madeira" title="Madeira">Madeira</a>. Portuguese processed fish products are exported through several companies, under a number of different brands and registered trademarks, such as <a href="/wiki/Conservas_Ramirez" title="Conservas Ramirez">Ramirez</a>, the world‚Äôs oldest active canned fish producer.</p>
<p>Portugal is a significant European <a href="/wiki/Minerals" class="mw-redirect" title="Minerals">minerals</a> producer and is ranked among Europe's leading <a href="/wiki/Copper" title="Copper">copper</a> producers. The nation is also a notable producer of <a href="/wiki/Tin" title="Tin">tin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tungsten" title="Tungsten">tungsten</a> and <a href="/wiki/Uranium" title="Uranium">uranium</a>. However, the country lacks the potential to conduct <a href="/wiki/Hydrocarbon_exploration" title="Hydrocarbon exploration">hydrocarbon exploration</a> and <a href="/wiki/Aluminium" title="Aluminium">aluminium</a>, a limitation that has hindered the development of Portugal's <a href="/wiki/Mining_in_Portugal" title="Mining in Portugal">mining</a> and <a href="/wiki/Metallurgy" title="Metallurgy">metallurgy</a> sectors. Although the country has vast iron and coal reserves‚Äîmainly in the north‚Äîafter the 1974 revolution and the consequent <a href="/wiki/Economic_globalization" title="Economic globalization">economic globalization</a>, low competitiveness forced a decrease in the extraction activity for these minerals. The <a href="/wiki/Panasqueira" title="Panasqueira">Panasqueira</a> and <a href="/wiki/Neves-Corvo_mine" title="Neves-Corvo mine">Neves-Corvo mines</a> are among the most recognised Portuguese mines that are still in operation.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Secondary_sector">Secondary sector</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portugal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Secondary sector">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:F._Portucel_Soporcel.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/F._Portucel_Soporcel.jpg/200px-F._Portucel_Soporcel.jpg" width="200" height="70" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/F._Portucel_Soporcel.jpg/300px-F._Portucel_Soporcel.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/F._Portucel_Soporcel.jpg/400px-F._Portucel_Soporcel.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="224" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:F._Portucel_Soporcel.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A <a href="/wiki/Portucel_Soporcel" title="Portucel Soporcel">Portucel Soporcel</a> pulp and paper factory in <a href="/wiki/Set%C3%BAbal,_Portugal" class="mw-redirect" title="Set√∫bal, Portugal">Set√∫bal</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Industry is diversified, ranging from <a href="/wiki/Automotive_industry" title="Automotive industry">automotive</a> (<a href="/wiki/Volkswagen_Autoeuropa" class="mw-redirect" title="Volkswagen Autoeuropa">Volkswagen Autoeuropa</a> and <a href="/wiki/Peugeot_Citroen" class="mw-redirect" title="Peugeot Citroen">Peugeot Citroen</a>), <a href="/wiki/Aerospace_industry" class="mw-redirect" title="Aerospace industry">aerospace</a> (<a href="/wiki/Embraer" title="Embraer">Embraer</a> and <a href="/wiki/OGMA" title="OGMA">OGMA</a>), <a href="/wiki/Electronics_industry" title="Electronics industry">electronics</a> and <a href="/wiki/Textile_industry" title="Textile industry">textiles</a>, to <a href="/wiki/Food_industry" title="Food industry">food</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chemical_industry" title="Chemical industry">chemicals</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cement" title="Cement">cement</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wood_pulp" class="mw-redirect" title="Wood pulp">wood pulp</a>. Volkswagen Group's <a href="/wiki/AutoEuropa" title="AutoEuropa">AutoEuropa</a> motor vehicle assembly plant in <a href="/wiki/Palmela" title="Palmela">Palmela</a> is among the largest <a href="/wiki/Foreign_direct_investment" title="Foreign direct investment">foreign direct investment</a> projects in Portugal. Modern non-traditional technology-based industries, such as <a href="/wiki/Aerospace" title="Aerospace">aerospace</a>, <a href="/wiki/Biotechnology" title="Biotechnology">biotechnology</a> and <a href="/wiki/Information_technology" title="Information technology">information technology</a>, have been developed in several locations across the country. <a href="/wiki/Alverca" class="mw-redirect" title="Alverca">Alverca</a>, <a href="/wiki/Covilh%C3%A3" title="Covilh√£">Covilh√£</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">[86]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/%C3%89vora" title="√âvora">√âvora</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">[87]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Ponte_de_Sor" title="Ponte de Sor">Ponte de Sor</a> are the main centres of the Portuguese aerospace industry, which is led by Brazil-based company Embraer and the Portuguese company OGMA. Following the turn of the 21st century, many major biotechnology and information technology industries have been founded, and are concentrated in the metropolitan areas of <a href="/wiki/Lisbon_Metropolitan_Area" title="Lisbon Metropolitan Area">Lisbon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Porto_Metropolitan_Area" class="mw-redirect" title="Porto Metropolitan Area">Porto</a>, <a href="/wiki/Braga" title="Braga">Braga</a>, <a href="/wiki/Coimbra" title="Coimbra">Coimbra</a> and <a href="/wiki/Aveiro,_Portugal" title="Aveiro, Portugal">Aveiro</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tertiary_sector">Tertiary sector</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portugal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Tertiary sector">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_Portugal" title="Tourism in Portugal">Tourism in Portugal</a></div>
<div class="thumb tmulti tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:312px;max-width:312px">
<div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:155px;max-width:155px">

</div>
<div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:153px;max-width:153px">
<div class="thumbimage" style="height:100px;overflow:hidden"><a href="/wiki/File:DSC_3294_(3784718431).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/DSC_3294_%283784718431%29.jpg/151px-DSC_3294_%283784718431%29.jpg" width="151" height="100" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/DSC_3294_%283784718431%29.jpg/227px-DSC_3294_%283784718431%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/DSC_3294_%283784718431%29.jpg/302px-DSC_3294_%283784718431%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1280" data-file-height="849" /></a></div>
