<div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Cristo_Rei,_Lisboa,_Portugal,_2012-05-12,_DD_01.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Cristo_Rei%2C_Lisboa%2C_Portugal%2C_2012-05-12%2C_DD_01.JPG/200px-Cristo_Rei%2C_Lisboa%2C_Portugal%2C_2012-05-12%2C_DD_01.JPG" width="200" height="261" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Cristo_Rei%2C_Lisboa%2C_Portugal%2C_2012-05-12%2C_DD_01.JPG/300px-Cristo_Rei%2C_Lisboa%2C_Portugal%2C_2012-05-12%2C_DD_01.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Cristo_Rei%2C_Lisboa%2C_Portugal%2C_2012-05-12%2C_DD_01.JPG/400px-Cristo_Rei%2C_Lisboa%2C_Portugal%2C_2012-05-12%2C_DD_01.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1794" data-file-height="2339" /></a></div>
</div>
<div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Santu%C3%A1rio_de_F%C3%A1tima_(36)_-_Jul_2008.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Santu%C3%A1rio_de_F%C3%A1tima_%2836%29_-_Jul_2008.jpg/200px-Santu%C3%A1rio_de_F%C3%A1tima_%2836%29_-_Jul_2008.jpg" width="200" height="150" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Santu%C3%A1rio_de_F%C3%A1tima_%2836%29_-_Jul_2008.jpg/300px-Santu%C3%A1rio_de_F%C3%A1tima_%2836%29_-_Jul_2008.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Santu%C3%A1rio_de_F%C3%A1tima_%2836%29_-_Jul_2008.jpg/400px-Santu%C3%A1rio_de_F%C3%A1tima_%2836%29_-_Jul_2008.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2592" data-file-height="1944" /></a></div>
</div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:left;background-color:transparent">The <a href="/wiki/Sanctuary_of_Christ_the_King" class="mw-redirect" title="Sanctuary of Christ the King">Shrine of Christ the King</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Sanctuary_of_F%C3%A1tima" title="Sanctuary of F√°tima">Shrine of Our Lady of F√°tima</a> in Portugal are two of the world's most visited Catholic pilgrimage sites.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>According to the 2011 Census, 88.0% of the Portuguese population are <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholic">Roman Catholic</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">[123]</a></sup> The country has small Protestant, <a href="/wiki/The_Church_of_Jesus_Christ_of_Latter-day_Saints" title="The Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints">Latter-day Saint</a>, <a href="/wiki/Islam_in_Portugal" title="Islam in Portugal">Muslim</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hinduism_in_Portugal" title="Hinduism in Portugal">Hindu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sikh" title="Sikh">Sikh</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Orthodox_Church" title="Eastern Orthodox Church">Eastern Orthodox Church</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jehovah%27s_Witnesses" title="Jehovah's Witnesses">Jehovah's Witnesses</a>, <a href="/wiki/Baha%27i" class="mw-redirect" title="Baha'i">Baha'i</a>, <a href="/wiki/Buddhism" title="Buddhism">Buddhist</a>, <a href="/wiki/Judaism" title="Judaism">Jewish</a> and <a href="/wiki/Spiritism" title="Spiritism">Spiritist</a> communities. Influences from <a href="/wiki/African_Traditional_Religion" class="mw-redirect" title="African Traditional Religion">African Traditional Religion</a> and Chinese Traditional Religion are also felt among many people, particularly in fields related with Traditional Chinese Medicine and African Witch Doctors. Some 6.8% of the population declared themselves to be non-religious, and 8.3% did not give any answer about their religion.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">[124]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2012, a study conducted by the Catholic University revealed 79.5% of the Portuguese considered themselves Catholics, and that 18% <a href="/wiki/Church_attendance" title="Church attendance">attended Mass</a> regularly. These figures represent a drop from 86.9% of Catholics in 2001, while during the same period the number of people stating that they had no religion rose from 8.2% to 14.2%.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">[125]</a></sup></p>
<p>Many Portuguese holidays, festivals and traditions have a Christian origin or connotation. Although relations between the Portuguese state and the Roman Catholic Church were generally amiable and stable since the earliest years of the Portuguese nation, their relative power fluctuated. In the <a href="/wiki/History_of_Portugal_(1279-1415)" class="mw-redirect" title="History of Portugal (1279-1415)">13th and 14th centuries</a>, the church enjoyed both riches and power stemming from its role in the <a href="/wiki/Reconquista" title="Reconquista">reconquest</a>, its close identification with early Portuguese nationalism and the foundation of the Portuguese educational system, including the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Coimbra" title="University of Coimbra">first university</a>.</p>
<p>The growth of the <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Empire" title="Portuguese Empire">Portuguese overseas empire</a> made its <a href="/wiki/Mission_(Christian)" class="mw-redirect" title="Mission (Christian)">missionaries</a> important agents of <a href="/wiki/Colonisation" class="mw-redirect" title="Colonisation">colonization</a>, with important roles in the <a href="/wiki/Teaching" class="mw-redirect" title="Teaching">education</a> and <a href="/wiki/Evangelization" class="mw-redirect" title="Evangelization">evangelization</a> of people from all the inhabited continents. The growth of <a href="/wiki/Liberal_Revolution_of_1820" title="Liberal Revolution of 1820">liberal</a> and nascent <a href="/wiki/Republicanism" title="Republicanism">republican</a> movements during the eras leading to the formation of the <a href="/wiki/First_Portuguese_Republic" title="First Portuguese Republic">First Portuguese Republic</a> (1910‚Äì26) changed the role and importance of organized religion.</p>
<p>Portugal is a <a href="/wiki/Secular_state" title="Secular state">secular state</a>: <a href="/wiki/Separation_of_church_and_state" title="Separation of church and state">church and state were formally separated</a> during the Portuguese First Republic, and later reiterated in the 1976 <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Constitution" class="mw-redirect" title="Portuguese Constitution">Portuguese Constitution</a>. Other than the Constitution, the two most important documents relating to <a href="/wiki/Religious_freedom" class="mw-redirect" title="Religious freedom">religious freedom</a> in Portugal are the 1940 Concordata (later amended in 1971) between Portugal and the <a href="/wiki/Holy_See" title="Holy See">Holy See</a> and the 2001 Religious Freedom Act.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portugal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Languages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Portugal" title="Languages of Portugal">Languages of Portugal</a> and <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">Portuguese language</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Gen%C3%ADsio04.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Gen%C3%ADsio04.jpg/200px-Gen%C3%ADsio04.jpg" width="200" height="110" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Gen%C3%ADsio04.jpg/300px-Gen%C3%ADsio04.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Gen%C3%ADsio04.jpg/400px-Gen%C3%ADsio04.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="880" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Gen%C3%ADsio04.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A sign in <a href="/wiki/Mirandese_language" title="Mirandese language">Mirandese</a> in <a href="/wiki/Miranda_do_Douro" title="Miranda do Douro">Miranda do Douro</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tr%C3%A1s-os-Montes_e_Alto_Douro_Province" title="Tr√°s-os-Montes e Alto Douro Province">Tr√°s-os-Montes</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Map_of_the_portuguese_language_in_the_world.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Map_of_the_portuguese_language_in_the_world.svg/200px-Map_of_the_portuguese_language_in_the_world.svg.png" width="200" height="88" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Map_of_the_portuguese_language_in_the_world.svg/300px-Map_of_the_portuguese_language_in_the_world.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Map_of_the_portuguese_language_in_the_world.svg/400px-Map_of_the_portuguese_language_in_the_world.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1498" data-file-height="660" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Map_of_the_portuguese_language_in_the_world.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">Portuguese</a> is the world's 6th most spoken language, with approx. 260 million speakers.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Portuguese is the official language of Portugal. Portuguese is a <a href="/wiki/Romance_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Romance language">Romance language</a> that originated in what is now <a href="/wiki/Galicia_(Spain)" title="Galicia (Spain)">Galicia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Northern_Portugal" class="mw-redirect" title="Northern Portugal">Northern Portugal</a>, originating from <a href="/wiki/Galician-Portuguese" title="Galician-Portuguese">Galician-Portuguese</a>, which was the common language of the Galician and Portuguese people until the formation of Portugal. Particularly in the North of Portugal, there are still many similarities between the Galician culture and the Portuguese culture. Galicia is a consultative observer of the <a href="/wiki/Community_of_Portuguese_Language_Countries" title="Community of Portuguese Language Countries">Community of Portuguese Language Countries</a>. According to the Ethnologue of Languages, Portuguese and Spanish have a lexical similarity of 89% ‚Äì educated speakers of each language can communicate with one another.</p>
<p>The Portuguese language is derived from the <a href="/wiki/Latin_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Latin language">Latin</a> spoken by the <a href="/wiki/Romanization_(cultural)" title="Romanization (cultural)">romanized</a> <a href="/wiki/Pre-Roman_peoples_of_the_Iberian_Peninsula" title="Pre-Roman peoples of the Iberian Peninsula">Pre-Roman peoples of the Iberian Peninsula</a> around 2000 years ago‚Äîparticularly the <a href="/wiki/Celts" title="Celts">Celts</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tartessians" class="mw-redirect" title="Tartessians">Tartessians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lusitanians" title="Lusitanians">Lusitanians</a> and <a href="/wiki/Iberians" title="Iberians">Iberians</a>. In the 15th and 16th centuries, the language spread worldwide as Portugal established a colonial and commercial empire between 1415 and 1999.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">[126]</a></sup> Portuguese is now spoken as a native language in five different continents, with Brazil accounting for the largest number of native Portuguese speakers of any country (200 million speakers in 2012).<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">[127]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2013 the Portuguese language is the official language spoken in Brazil, Angola, Mozambique, Cape Verde, S√£o Tom√© and Pr√≠ncipe, Guinea-Bissau, Equatorial Guinea, and <a href="/wiki/East_Timor" title="East Timor">East Timor</a>. These countries, plus <a href="/wiki/Macau" title="Macau">Macau</a> Special Administrative Region (People's Republic of China) where Portuguese is co-official with Cantonese, make up the <a href="/wiki/Lusosphere" class="mw-redirect" title="Lusosphere">Lusosphere</a>, a term derived from the ancient <a href="/wiki/Roman_province" title="Roman province">Roman province</a> of "<a href="/wiki/Lusitania" title="Lusitania">Lusitania</a>", which currently matches the Portuguese territory south of the <a href="/wiki/Douro" title="Douro">Douro</a> river.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">[128]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Mirandese_language" title="Mirandese language">Mirandese</a> is also recognized as a co-official regional language in some municipalities of North-Eastern Portugal. An estimate of between 6,000 and 7,000 Mirandese speakers has been documented for Portugal.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">[129]</a></sup></p>
<p>According to <a href="/wiki/EF_English_Proficiency_Index" title="EF English Proficiency Index">International English Proficiency Index</a>, Portugal has a high proficiency level in <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English</a>, higher than in neighbouring countries like <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italy</a>, <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a> or <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">[130]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portugal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Portugal" title="Education in Portugal">Education in Portugal</a></div>
<div class="thumb tmulti tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:204px;max-width:204px">
<div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Coimbra_University.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Coimbra_University.jpg/200px-Coimbra_University.jpg" width="200" height="133" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Coimbra_University.jpg/300px-Coimbra_University.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Coimbra_University.jpg/400px-Coimbra_University.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4288" data-file-height="2848" /></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">Founded in 1290, the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Coimbra" title="University of Coimbra">University of Coimbra</a> is Portugal's oldest.</div>
</div>
<div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Up_reitoria.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Up_reitoria.jpg/200px-Up_reitoria.jpg" width="200" height="126" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Up_reitoria.jpg/300px-Up_reitoria.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Up_reitoria.jpg/400px-Up_reitoria.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="631" /></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">The <a href="/wiki/University_of_Porto" title="University of Porto">University of Porto</a> is Portugal's second largest and its leading research university.</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The educational system is divided into preschool (for those under age 6), basic education (9 years, in three stages, compulsory), secondary education (3 years, compulsory since 2010), and higher education (subdivided in university and <a href="/wiki/Polytechnic_(Portugal)" title="Polytechnic (Portugal)">polytechnic</a> education). Universities are usually organized into <a href="/wiki/Faculty_(division)" title="Faculty (division)">faculties</a>. Institutes and schools are also common designations for autonomous subdivisions of <a href="/wiki/List_of_colleges_and_universities_in_Portugal" class="mw-redirect" title="List of colleges and universities in Portugal">Portuguese higher education institutions</a>.</p>
<p>The total adult literacy rate is 99 percent. Portuguese primary school enrollments are close to 100 percent.</p>
<p>According to the <a href="/wiki/Programme_for_International_Student_Assessment" title="Programme for International Student Assessment">Programme for International Student Assessment</a> (PISA) 2015, the average Portuguese 15-year-old student, when rated in terms of reading literacy, mathematics and science knowledge, is placed significantly above the <a href="/wiki/OECD" class="mw-redirect" title="OECD">OECD</a>'s average, at a similar level as those students from Norway, Poland, Denmark and Belgium, with 501 points (493 is the average). The PISA results of the Portuguese students have been continuously improving, overcoming a number of other highly developed western countries like the USA, Austria, France and Sweden.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">[131]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">[132]</a></sup></p>
<p>Over 35% of college-age citizens (20 years old) attend one of Portugal's higher education institutions<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">[133]</a></sup> (compared with 50% in the United States and 35% in the OECD countries). In addition to being a destination for <a href="/wiki/International_student" title="International student">international students</a>, Portugal is also among the top places of origin for international students. All higher education students, both domestic and international, totaled 380,937 in 2005.</p>
<p>Portuguese universities have existed since 1290. The <a href="/wiki/University_of_Coimbra" title="University of Coimbra">oldest Portuguese university</a> was first established in Lisbon before moving to <a href="/wiki/Coimbra" title="Coimbra">Coimbra</a>. Historically, within the scope of the Portuguese Empire, the Portuguese founded the oldest engineering school of the <a href="/wiki/Americas" title="Americas">Americas</a> (the <i><a href="/wiki/Real_Academia_de_Artilharia,_Fortifica%C3%A7%C3%A3o_e_Desenho" class="mw-redirect" title="Real Academia de Artilharia, Fortifica√ß√£o e Desenho">Real Academia de Artilharia, Fortifica√ß√£o e Desenho</a></i> of <a href="/wiki/Rio_de_Janeiro" title="Rio de Janeiro">Rio de Janeiro</a>) in 1792, as well as the oldest medical college in Asia (the <i><a href="/wiki/Escola_M%C3%A9dico-Cir%C3%BArgica_de_Goa" class="mw-redirect" title="Escola M√©dico-Cir√∫rgica de Goa">Escola M√©dico-Cir√∫rgica</a></i> of <a href="/wiki/Goa" title="Goa">Goa</a>) in 1842. Presently, the largest university in Portugal is the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Lisbon" title="University of Lisbon">University of Lisbon</a>.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Bologna_process" class="mw-redirect" title="Bologna process">Bologna process</a> has been adopted, since 2006, by Portuguese universities and poly-technical institutes. Higher education in state-run educational establishments is provided on a competitive basis, a system of <i><a href="/wiki/Numerus_clausus" title="Numerus clausus">numerus clausus</a></i> is enforced through a national database on student admissions. However, every higher education institution offers also a number of additional vacant places through other extraordinary admission processes for sportsmen, mature applicants (over 23 years old), <a href="/wiki/International_students" class="mw-redirect" title="International students">international students</a>, foreign students from the <a href="/wiki/Lusosphere" class="mw-redirect" title="Lusosphere">Lusosphere</a>, degree owners from other institutions, students from other institutions (<a href="/wiki/Transfer_admissions_in_the_United_States" title="Transfer admissions in the United States">academic transfer</a>), former students (readmission), and course change, which are subject to specific standards and regulations set by each institution or course department.</p>
<p>Most student costs are supported with public money. However, with the increasing tuition fees a student has to pay to attend a Portuguese state-run higher education institution and the attraction of new types of students (many as part-time students or in evening classes) like employees, businessmen, parents, and pensioners, many departments make a substantial profit from every additional student enrolled in courses, with benefits for the college or university's gross tuition revenue and without loss of educational quality (teacher per student, computer per student, classroom size per student, etc.).</p>
<p>Portugal has entered into <a href="/wiki/Higher_education_in_Portugal#International_partnership_agreements" title="Higher education in Portugal">cooperation agreements with the Massachusetts Institute of Technology and other US institutions</a> to further develop and increase the effectiveness of Portuguese higher education and research.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Health">Health</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portugal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Health">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Health_in_Portugal" title="Health in Portugal">Health in Portugal</a></div>
<div class="thumb tmulti tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:204px;max-width:204px">
<div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Hospital_Geral_de_Santo_Ant%C3%B3nio_(14027237313).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Hospital_Geral_de_Santo_Ant%C3%B3nio_%2814027237313%29.jpg/200px-Hospital_Geral_de_Santo_Ant%C3%B3nio_%2814027237313%29.jpg" width="200" height="150" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Hospital_Geral_de_Santo_Ant%C3%B3nio_%2814027237313%29.jpg/300px-Hospital_Geral_de_Santo_Ant%C3%B3nio_%2814027237313%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Hospital_Geral_de_Santo_Ant%C3%B3nio_%2814027237313%29.jpg/400px-Hospital_Geral_de_Santo_Ant%C3%B3nio_%2814027237313%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4000" data-file-height="3000" /></a></div>
</div>
<div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Hospital_de_Santa_Maria.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Hospital_de_Santa_Maria.jpg/200px-Hospital_de_Santa_Maria.jpg" width="200" height="150" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Hospital_de_Santa_Maria.jpg/300px-Hospital_de_Santa_Maria.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Hospital_de_Santa_Maria.jpg/400px-Hospital_de_Santa_Maria.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3072" data-file-height="2304" /></a></div>
</div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:left;background-color:transparent">Santo Ant√≥nio Hospital, in <a href="/wiki/Porto" title="Porto">Porto</a> (above), and Santa Maria Hospital, in <a href="/wiki/Lisbon" title="Lisbon">Lisbon</a> (bottom).</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>According to the latest <a href="/wiki/Human_Development_Report" title="Human Development Report">Human Development Report</a>, the average <a href="/wiki/Life_expectancy" title="Life expectancy">life expectancy</a> in 2015 was 81.0 years.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">[134]</a></sup></p>
<p>Portugal ranks 12th in the best public health systems in the world, ahead of high developed countries like the United Kingdom, Germany or Sweden.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">[135]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Portuguese health system is characterized by three coexisting systems: the National Health Service (<i>Servi√ßo Nacional de Sa√∫de'</i>, SNS), special social health insurance schemes for certain professions (health subsystems) and voluntary private health insurance. The SNS provides universal coverage. In addition, about 25% of the population is covered by the health subsystems, 10% by private insurance schemes and another 7% by mutual funds.</p>
<p>The Ministry of Health is responsible for developing health policy as well as managing the SNS. Five regional health administrations are in charge of implementing the national health policy objectives, developing guidelines and protocols and supervising health care delivery. Decentralization efforts have aimed at shifting financial and management responsibility to the regional level. In practice, however, the autonomy of regional health administrations over budget setting and spending has been limited to primary care.</p>
<p>The SNS is predominantly funded through general taxation. Employer (including the state) and employee contributions represent the main funding sources of the health subsystems. In addition, direct payments by the patient and voluntary health insurance premiums account for a large proportion of funding.</p>
<p>Similar to the other Eur-A countries, most Portuguese die from <a href="/wiki/Noncommunicable_diseases" class="mw-redirect" title="Noncommunicable diseases">noncommunicable diseases</a>. Mortality from <a href="/wiki/Cardiovascular_diseases" class="mw-redirect" title="Cardiovascular diseases">cardiovascular diseases</a> (CVD) is higher than in the <a href="/wiki/Eurozone" title="Eurozone">eurozone</a>, but its two main components, ischaemic heart disease and cerebrovascular disease, display inverse trends compared with the Eur-A, with <a href="/wiki/Cerebrovascular_disease" title="Cerebrovascular disease">cerebrovascular disease</a> being the single biggest killer in Portugal (17%). Portuguese people die 12% less often from cancer than in the Eur-A, but mortality is not declining as rapidly as in the Eur-A. Cancer is more frequent among children as well as among women younger than 44 years. Although lung cancer (slowly increasing among women) and breast cancer (decreasing rapidly) are scarcer, cancer of the cervix and the prostate are more frequent. Portugal has the highest mortality rate for diabetes in the Eur-A, with a sharp increase since the 1980s.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:FCM-UNL.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/FCM-UNL.JPG/200px-FCM-UNL.JPG" width="200" height="150" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/FCM-UNL.JPG/300px-FCM-UNL.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/FCM-UNL.JPG/400px-FCM-UNL.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:FCM-UNL.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Medical Department of the <a href="/wiki/Universidade_Nova_de_Lisboa" title="Universidade Nova de Lisboa">Universidade Nova de Lisboa</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Portugal's <a href="/wiki/Infant_mortality_rate" class="mw-redirect" title="Infant mortality rate">infant mortality rate</a> has dropped sharply since the late 1970s, when 24 of 1000 newborns died in the first year of life. It is now around 2 deaths per a 1000 newborns. This improvement was mainly due to the decrease in neonatal mortality, from 15.5 to 2.4 per 1000 live births.</p>
<p>People are usually well informed about their health status, the positive and negative effects of their behaviour on their health and their use of health care services. Yet their perceptions of their health can differ from what administrative and examination-based data show about levels of illness within populations. Thus, survey results based on self-reporting at the household level complement other data on health status and the use of services.</p>
<p>Only one third of adults rated their health as good or very good in Portugal (Kasmel et al., 2004). This is the lowest of the Eur-A countries reporting and reflects the relatively adverse situation of the country in terms of mortality and selected morbidity.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">[136]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portugal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Portugal" title="Culture of Portugal">Culture of Portugal</a></div>
<div class="thumb tmulti tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:204px;max-width:204px">
<div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Jer%C3%B3nimos_April_2009-4.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Jer%C3%B3nimos_April_2009-4.jpg/200px-Jer%C3%B3nimos_April_2009-4.jpg" width="200" height="128" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Jer%C3%B3nimos_April_2009-4.jpg/300px-Jer%C3%B3nimos_April_2009-4.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Jer%C3%B3nimos_April_2009-4.jpg/400px-Jer%C3%B3nimos_April_2009-4.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2861" data-file-height="1827" /></a></div>
</div>
<div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Torre_Bel%C3%A9m_April_2009-4a.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Torre_Bel%C3%A9m_April_2009-4a.jpg/200px-Torre_Bel%C3%A9m_April_2009-4a.jpg" width="200" height="191" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Torre_Bel%C3%A9m_April_2009-4a.jpg/300px-Torre_Bel%C3%A9m_April_2009-4a.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Torre_Bel%C3%A9m_April_2009-4a.jpg/400px-Torre_Bel%C3%A9m_April_2009-4a.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5035" data-file-height="4805" /></a></div>
</div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:left;background-color:transparent"><a href="/wiki/Jer%C3%B3nimos_Monastery" title="Jer√≥nimos Monastery">Jer√≥nimos Monastery</a> (top) and <a href="/wiki/Bel%C3%A9m_Tower" title="Bel√©m Tower">Bel√©m Tower</a> (bottom) are <a href="/wiki/Great_Work" title="Great Work">magna opera</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Manueline_style" class="mw-redirect" title="Manueline style">Manueline style</a> and symbols of Portuguese nationhood.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Portugal has developed a specific culture while being influenced by various civilizations that have crossed the Mediterranean and the European continent, or were introduced when it played an active role during the <a href="/wiki/Portugal_in_the_Age_of_Discovery" class="mw-redirect" title="Portugal in the Age of Discovery">Age of Discovery</a>. In the 1990s and 2000s (decade), Portugal modernized its public cultural facilities, in addition to the <a href="/wiki/Calouste_Gulbenkian_Foundation" title="Calouste Gulbenkian Foundation">Calouste Gulbenkian Foundation</a> established in 1956 in Lisbon.</p>
<p>These include the <a href="/wiki/Bel%C3%A9m_Cultural_Centre" class="mw-redirect" title="Bel√©m Cultural Centre">Bel√©m Cultural Centre</a> in Lisbon, <a href="/wiki/Serralves_Foundation" class="mw-redirect" title="Serralves Foundation">Serralves Foundation</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Casa_da_M%C3%BAsica" title="Casa da M√∫sica">Casa da M√∫sica</a>, both in <a href="/wiki/Porto" title="Porto">Porto</a>, as well as new public cultural facilities like municipal libraries and concert halls that were built or renovated in many municipalities across the country. Portugal is home to <a href="/wiki/List_of_World_Heritage_Sites_in_Portugal" title="List of World Heritage Sites in Portugal">fifteen</a> UNESCO <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" title="World Heritage Site">World Heritage Sites</a>, ranking it <a href="/wiki/Table_of_World_Heritage_Sites_by_country" title="Table of World Heritage Sites by country">8th in Europe and 17th in the world.</a></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Architecture">Architecture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portugal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: Architecture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Architecture_of_Portugal" title="Architecture of Portugal">Architecture of Portugal</a></div>
<p>Traditional architecture is distinctive and include the <a href="/wiki/Manueline" title="Manueline">Manueline</a>, also known as Portuguese late Gothic, a sumptuous, composite Portuguese style of architectural ornamentation of the first decades of the 16th century. A 20th-century interpretation of traditional architecture, <a href="/wiki/Soft_Portuguese_style" title="Soft Portuguese style">Soft Portuguese style</a>, appears extensively in major cities, especially Lisbon. Modern Portugal has given the world renowned architects like <a href="/wiki/Eduardo_Souto_de_Moura" title="Eduardo Souto de Moura">Eduardo Souto de Moura</a>, <a href="/wiki/%C3%81lvaro_Siza_Vieira" title="√Ålvaro Siza Vieira">√Ålvaro Siza Vieira</a> (both <a href="/wiki/Pritzker_Prize" class="mw-redirect" title="Pritzker Prize">Pritzker Prize</a> winners) and <a href="/wiki/Gon%C3%A7alo_Byrne" title="Gon√ßalo Byrne">Gon√ßalo Byrne</a>. In Portugal <a href="/wiki/Tom%C3%A1s_Taveira" title="Tom√°s Taveira">Tom√°s Taveira</a> is also noteworthy, particularly for stadium design.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">[137]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">[138]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">[139]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cinema">Cinema</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portugal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: Cinema">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Cinema_of_Portugal" title="Cinema of Portugal">Cinema of Portugal</a></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Cinema_of_Portugal" title="Cinema of Portugal">Portuguese cinema</a> has a long tradition, reaching back to the birth of the medium in the late 19th century. Portuguese film directors such as <a href="/wiki/Arthur_Duarte" title="Arthur Duarte">Arthur Duarte</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ant%C3%B3nio_Lopes_Ribeiro" title="Ant√≥nio Lopes Ribeiro">Ant√≥nio Lopes Ribeiro</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ant%C3%B3nio_Reis" title="Ant√≥nio Reis">Ant√≥nio Reis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pedro_Costa" title="Pedro Costa">Pedro Costa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Manoel_de_Oliveira" title="Manoel de Oliveira">Manoel de Oliveira</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jo%C3%A3o_C%C3%A9sar_Monteiro" title="Jo√£o C√©sar Monteiro">Jo√£o C√©sar Monteiro</a>, <a href="/wiki/Edgar_P%C3%AAra" title="Edgar P√™ra">Edgar P√™ra</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ant%C3%B3nio-Pedro_Vasconcelos" title="Ant√≥nio-Pedro Vasconcelos">Ant√≥nio-Pedro Vasconcelos</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fernando_Lopes_(filmmaker)" title="Fernando Lopes (filmmaker)">Fernando Lopes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jo%C3%A3o_Botelho" title="Jo√£o Botelho">Jo√£o Botelho</a> and <a href="/wiki/Leonel_Vieira" title="Leonel Vieira">Leonel Vieira</a>, are among those that gained notability. Noted Portuguese film actors include <a href="/wiki/Joaquim_de_Almeida" title="Joaquim de Almeida">Joaquim de Almeida</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nuno_Lopes" title="Nuno Lopes">Nuno Lopes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Daniela_Ruah" title="Daniela Ruah">Daniela Ruah</a>, <a href="/wiki/Maria_de_Medeiros" title="Maria de Medeiros">Maria de Medeiros</a>, <a href="/wiki/Diogo_Infante" title="Diogo Infante">Diogo Infante</a>, <a href="/wiki/Soraia_Chaves" title="Soraia Chaves">Soraia Chaves</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ribeirinho" title="Ribeirinho">Ribeirinho</a>, <a href="/wiki/L%C3%BAcia_Moniz" title="L√∫cia Moniz">L√∫cia Moniz</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Diogo_Morgado" title="Diogo Morgado">Diogo Morgado</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Literature">Literature</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portugal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=46" title="Edit section: Literature">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_literature" title="Portuguese literature">Portuguese literature</a></div>
<div class="thumb tmulti tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:312px;max-width:312px">
<div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:154px;max-width:154px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Lu%C3%ADs_de_Cam%C3%B5es_por_Fran%C3%A7ois_G%C3%A9rard.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Lu%C3%ADs_de_Cam%C3%B5es_por_Fran%C3%A7ois_G%C3%A9rard.jpg/152px-Lu%C3%ADs_de_Cam%C3%B5es_por_Fran%C3%A7ois_G%C3%A9rard.jpg" width="152" height="206" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Lu%C3%ADs_de_Cam%C3%B5es_por_Fran%C3%A7ois_G%C3%A9rard.jpg/228px-Lu%C3%ADs_de_Cam%C3%B5es_por_Fran%C3%A7ois_G%C3%A9rard.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Lu%C3%ADs_de_Cam%C3%B5es_por_Fran%C3%A7ois_G%C3%A9rard.jpg/304px-Lu%C3%ADs_de_Cam%C3%B5es_por_Fran%C3%A7ois_G%C3%A9rard.jpg 2x" data-file-width="309" data-file-height="419" /></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left"><a href="/wiki/Lu%C3%ADs_Vaz_de_Cam%C3%B5es" class="mw-redirect" title="Lu√≠s Vaz de Cam√µes">Lu√≠s Vaz de Cam√µes</a>, legendary poet of the <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Renaissance" title="Portuguese Renaissance">Portuguese Renaissance</a></div>
</div>
<div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:154px;max-width:154px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Pessoabaixa.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Pessoabaixa.jpg/152px-Pessoabaixa.jpg" width="152" height="202" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Pessoabaixa.jpg/228px-Pessoabaixa.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Pessoabaixa.jpg/304px-Pessoabaixa.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1775" data-file-height="2362" /></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left"><a href="/wiki/Fernando_Pessoa" title="Fernando Pessoa">Fernando Pessoa</a>, prolific writer in 20th century <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">Portuguese</a> literature</div>
</div>
<div style="clear:left"></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Portuguese literature, one of the earliest Western literatures, developed through text as well as song. Until 1350, the <a href="/wiki/Portuguese-Galician" class="mw-redirect" title="Portuguese-Galician">Portuguese-Galician</a> <a href="/wiki/Troubadour" title="Troubadour">troubadours</a> spread their literary influence to most of the Iberian Peninsula.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">[140]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Gil_Vicente" title="Gil Vicente">Gil Vicente</a> (c. 1465‚Äìc. 1536), was one of the founders of Portuguese dramatic traditions.</p>
<p>Adventurer and poet <a href="/wiki/Lu%C3%ADs_de_Cam%C3%B5es" title="Lu√≠s de Cam√µes">Lu√≠s de Cam√µes</a> (c. 1524‚Äì1580) wrote the epic poem <i>"Os Lus√≠adas"</i> (<a href="/wiki/The_Lusiads" class="mw-redirect" title="The Lusiads">The Lusiads</a>), with <a href="/wiki/Virgil" title="Virgil">Virgil</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Aeneid" title="Aeneid">Aeneid</a> as his main influence.<sup id="cite_ref-WDL_142-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WDL-142">[141]</a></sup> Modern Portuguese poetry is rooted in neoclassic and contemporary styles, as exemplified by <a href="/wiki/Fernando_Pessoa" title="Fernando Pessoa">Fernando Pessoa</a> (1888‚Äì1935). Modern Portuguese literature is represented by authors such as <a href="/wiki/Almeida_Garrett" title="Almeida Garrett">Almeida Garrett</a>, <a href="/wiki/Camilo_Castelo_Branco" title="Camilo Castelo Branco">Camilo Castelo Branco</a>, <a href="/wiki/E%C3%A7a_de_Queiroz" class="mw-redirect" title="E√ßa de Queiroz">E√ßa de Queiroz</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fernando_Pessoa" title="Fernando Pessoa">Fernando Pessoa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sophia_de_Mello_Breyner_Andresen" title="Sophia de Mello Breyner Andresen">Sophia de Mello Breyner Andresen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ant%C3%B3nio_Lobo_Antunes" title="Ant√≥nio Lobo Antunes">Ant√≥nio Lobo Antunes</a> and <a href="/wiki/Miguel_Torga" title="Miguel Torga">Miguel Torga</a>. Particularly popular and distinguished is <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Saramago" title="Jos√© Saramago">Jos√© Saramago</a>, recipient of the 1998 <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize_in_Literature" title="Nobel Prize in Literature">Nobel Prize in Literature</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">Cuisine</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portugal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=47" title="Edit section: Cuisine">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_cuisine" title="Portuguese cuisine">Portuguese cuisine</a> and <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_wine" title="Portuguese wine">Portuguese wine</a></div>
<p>Portuguese cuisine is diverse. The Portuguese consume a lot of dry <a href="/wiki/Cod" title="Cod">cod</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/Bacalhau" title="Bacalhau">bacalhau</a></i> in Portuguese), for which there are hundreds of <a href="/wiki/Bacalhau#Bacalhau_dishes" title="Bacalhau">recipes</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">[142]</a></sup> There are more than enough <i><a href="/wiki/Bacalhau" title="Bacalhau">bacalhau</a></i> dishes for each day of the year. Two other popular fish recipes are grilled <a href="/wiki/Sardines" class="mw-redirect" title="Sardines">sardines</a> and <a href="/wiki/Caldeirada" title="Caldeirada">caldeirada</a>, a potato-based <a href="/wiki/Stew" title="Stew">stew</a> that can be made from several types of fish. Typical Portuguese meat recipes made out of beef, pork, lamb, or chicken include <i><a href="/wiki/Cozido_%C3%A0_portuguesa" class="mw-redirect" title="Cozido √† portuguesa">cozido √† portuguesa</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Feijoada" title="Feijoada">feijoada</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Frango_de_churrasco" class="mw-redirect" title="Frango de churrasco">frango de churrasco</a></i>, <i>leit√£o</i> (roast <a href="/wiki/Suckling_pig" title="Suckling pig">suckling pig</a>) and <i><a href="/wiki/Carne_de_porco_%C3%A0_alentejana" title="Carne de porco √† alentejana">carne de porco √† alentejana</a></i>. A very popular northern dish is the arroz de sarrabulho (rice stewed in pigs blood) or the arroz de cabidela (rice and chickens meat stewed in chickens blood).</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Rabelo_Douro_en%E2%80%93Porto.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Rabelo_Douro_en%E2%80%93Porto.jpg/200px-Rabelo_Douro_en%E2%80%93Porto.jpg" width="200" height="133" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Rabelo_Douro_en%E2%80%93Porto.jpg/300px-Rabelo_Douro_en%E2%80%93Porto.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Rabelo_Douro_en%E2%80%93Porto.jpg/400px-Rabelo_Douro_en%E2%80%93Porto.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="530" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Rabelo_Douro_en%E2%80%93Porto.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Portuguese_wine" title="Portuguese wine">Portuguese wine</a>, such as <a href="/wiki/Port_wine" title="Port wine">Port wine</a> (being transported here into <a href="/wiki/Porto" title="Porto">Porto</a>), is world-famous.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Typical fast food dishes include the <a href="/wiki/Francesinha" title="Francesinha">Francesinha</a> (Frenchie) from Porto, and <i>bifanas</i> (grilled pork) or <i>prego</i> (grilled beef) <a href="/wiki/Sandwich" title="Sandwich">sandwiches</a>, which are well known around the country. The Portuguese art of <a href="/wiki/Pastry" title="Pastry">pastry</a> has its origins in the many <a href="/wiki/Medieval" class="mw-redirect" title="Medieval">medieval</a> Catholic monasteries spread widely across the country. These monasteries, using very few ingredients (mostly almonds, flour, eggs and some liquor), managed to create a spectacular wide range of different pastries, of which <a href="/wiki/Past%C3%A9is_de_Bel%C3%A9m" class="mw-redirect" title="Past√©is de Bel√©m">past√©is de Bel√©m</a> (or <i>past√©is de nata</i>) originally from Lisbon, and <i><a href="/wiki/Ovos_moles" class="mw-redirect" title="Ovos moles">ovos moles</a></i> from Aveiro are examples. Portuguese cuisine is very diverse, with different regions having their own traditional dishes. The Portuguese have a culture of good food, and throughout the country there are myriads of good restaurants and typical small <i>tasquinhas</i>.</p>
<p>Portuguese wines have enjoyed international recognition since the times of the Romans, who associated Portugal with their god <a href="/wiki/Dionysus" title="Dionysus">Bacchus</a>. Today, the country is known by wine lovers and its wines have won several international prizes. Some of the best Portuguese wines are <a href="/wiki/Vinho_Verde" title="Vinho Verde">Vinho Verde</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vinho_Alvarinho" class="mw-redirect" title="Vinho Alvarinho">Vinho Alvarinho</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vinho_do_Douro" class="mw-redirect" title="Vinho do Douro">Vinho do Douro</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vinho_do_Alentejo" class="mw-redirect" title="Vinho do Alentejo">Vinho do Alentejo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vinho_do_D%C3%A3o" class="mw-redirect" title="Vinho do D√£o">Vinho do D√£o</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vinho_da_Bairrada" class="mw-redirect" title="Vinho da Bairrada">Vinho da Bairrada</a> and the sweet <a href="/wiki/Port_Wine" class="mw-redirect" title="Port Wine">Port Wine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Madeira_Wine" class="mw-redirect" title="Madeira Wine">Madeira Wine</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Moscatel" class="mw-redirect" title="Moscatel">Moscatel</a> from <a href="/wiki/Set%C3%BAbal" title="Set√∫bal">Set√∫bal</a> and <a href="/wiki/Favaios" title="Favaios">Favaios</a>. Port and Madeira are particularly appreciated in a wide range of places around the world.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music">Music</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portugal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=48" title="Edit section: Music">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Portugal" title="Music of Portugal">Music of Portugal</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Jose_malhoa_fado.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Jose_malhoa_fado.jpg/200px-Jose_malhoa_fado.jpg" width="200" height="171" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Jose_malhoa_fado.jpg/300px-Jose_malhoa_fado.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Jose_malhoa_fado.jpg/400px-Jose_malhoa_fado.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1116" data-file-height="952" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Jose_malhoa_fado.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Fado" title="Fado">Fado</a>, famously depicted in this painting by <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Malhoa" title="Jos√© Malhoa">Jos√© Malhoa</a>, is Portugal's national song.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Music_of_Portugal" title="Music of Portugal">Portuguese music</a> encompasses a wide variety of genres. The most renowned is <a href="/wiki/Fado" title="Fado">Fado</a>, a melancholy urban music originated in <a href="/wiki/Lisbon" title="Lisbon">Lisbon</a>, usually associated with the <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_guitar" title="Portuguese guitar">Portuguese guitar</a> and <i>saudade</i>, or longing. <a href="/wiki/Coimbra_fado" class="mw-redirect" title="Coimbra fado">Coimbra fado</a>, a unique type of "<a href="/wiki/Troubadour" title="Troubadour">troubadour</a> serenading" fado, is also noteworthy. Internationally notable performers include <a href="/wiki/Am%C3%A1lia_Rodrigues" title="Am√°lia Rodrigues">Am√°lia Rodrigues</a>, <a href="/wiki/Carlos_Paredes" title="Carlos Paredes">Carlos Paredes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Afonso" class="mw-redirect" title="Jos√© Afonso">Jos√© Afonso</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mariza" title="Mariza">Mariza</a>, <a href="/wiki/Carlos_do_Carmo" title="Carlos do Carmo">Carlos do Carmo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ant%C3%B3nio_Chainho" title="Ant√≥nio Chainho">Ant√≥nio Chainho</a>, <a href="/wiki/M%C3%ADsia" title="M√≠sia">M√≠sia</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Madredeus" title="Madredeus">Madredeus</a>.</p>
<p>In addition to <a href="/wiki/Fado" title="Fado">Fado</a> and <a href="/wiki/Folk_music" title="Folk music">Folk</a>, the Portuguese listen to pop and other types of modern music, particularly from North America and the United Kingdom, as well as a wide range of Portuguese, Caribbean and Brazilian artists and bands. Artists with international recognition include <a href="/wiki/Dulce_Pontes" title="Dulce Pontes">Dulce Pontes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Moonspell" title="Moonspell">Moonspell</a>, <a href="/wiki/Buraka_Som_Sistema" title="Buraka Som Sistema">Buraka Som Sistema</a>, <a href="/wiki/Blasted_Mechanism" title="Blasted Mechanism">Blasted Mechanism</a> and <a href="/wiki/The_Gift_(band)" title="The Gift (band)">The Gift</a>, with the two latter being nominees for a <a href="/wiki/MTV_Europe_Music_Award" class="mw-redirect" title="MTV Europe Music Award">MTV Europe Music Award</a>.</p>
<p>Portugal has several summer music festivals, such as <i><a href="/wiki/Festival_Sudoeste" title="Festival Sudoeste">Festival Sudoeste</a></i> in <a href="/wiki/Zambujeira_do_Mar" title="Zambujeira do Mar">Zambujeira do Mar</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/Festival_de_Paredes_de_Coura" class="mw-redirect" title="Festival de Paredes de Coura">Festival de Paredes de Coura</a></i> in <a href="/wiki/Paredes_de_Coura" title="Paredes de Coura">Paredes de Coura</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/Festival_Vilar_de_Mouros" class="mw-redirect" title="Festival Vilar de Mouros">Festival Vilar de Mouros</a></i> near <a href="/wiki/Caminha" title="Caminha">Caminha</a>, <a href="/wiki/Boom_Festival" title="Boom Festival">Boom Festival</a> in <a href="/wiki/Idanha-a-Nova_Municipality" class="mw-redirect" title="Idanha-a-Nova Municipality">Idanha-a-Nova Municipality</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/NOS_Alive" title="NOS Alive">NOS Alive</a></i>, <i>Sumol Summer Fest</i> in <a href="/wiki/Ericeira" title="Ericeira">Ericeira</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/Rock_in_Rio#Lisboa.2C_Portugal.2C_and_Madrid.2C_Spain" title="Rock in Rio">Rock in Rio Lisboa</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Super_Bock_Super_Rock" title="Super Bock Super Rock">Super Bock Super Rock</a></i> in <a href="/wiki/Greater_Lisbon" class="mw-redirect" title="Greater Lisbon">Greater Lisbon</a>. Out of the summer season, Portugal has a large number of festivals, designed more to an urban audience, like Flowfest or Hip Hop Porto. Furthermore, one of the largest international <a href="/wiki/Goa_trance" title="Goa trance">Goa trance</a> festivals takes place in central Portugal every two years, the <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://boomfestival.org/boom2012/">Boom Festival</a>, that is also the only festival in Portugal to win international awards: European Festival Award 2010 ‚Äì Green'n'Clean Festival of the Year and the Greener Festival Award Outstanding 2008 and 2010. There is also the student festivals of <i><a href="/wiki/Queima_das_Fitas" title="Queima das Fitas">Queima das Fitas</a></i> are major events in a number of cities across Portugal. In 2005, Portugal held the <a href="/wiki/MTV_Europe_Music_Awards" title="MTV Europe Music Awards">MTV Europe Music Awards</a>, in <a href="/wiki/Pavilh%C3%A3o_Atl%C3%A2ntico" class="mw-redirect" title="Pavilh√£o Atl√¢ntico">Pavilh√£o Atl√¢ntico</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lisbon" title="Lisbon">Lisbon</a>.</p>
<p>In the classical music domain, Portugal is represented by names as the pianists <a href="/wiki/Artur_Pizarro" title="Artur Pizarro">Artur Pizarro</a>, <a href="/wiki/Maria_Jo%C3%A3o_Pires" title="Maria Jo√£o Pires">Maria Jo√£o Pires</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sequeira_Costa" title="Sequeira Costa">Sequeira Costa</a>, the violinists Carlos Damas, <a href="/wiki/Gerardo_Ribeiro" title="Gerardo Ribeiro">Gerardo Ribeiro</a> and in the past by the great cellist <a href="/wiki/Guilhermina_Suggia" title="Guilhermina Suggia">Guilhermina Suggia</a>. Notable composers include <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Vianna_da_Motta" title="Jos√© Vianna da Motta">Jos√© Vianna da Motta</a>, <a href="/wiki/Carlos_Seixas" title="Carlos Seixas">Carlos Seixas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jo%C3%A3o_Domingos_Bomtempo" title="Jo√£o Domingos Bomtempo">Jo√£o Domingos Bomtempo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jo%C3%A3o_de_Sousa_Carvalho" title="Jo√£o de Sousa Carvalho">Jo√£o de Sousa Carvalho</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lu%C3%ADs_de_Freitas_Branco" title="Lu√≠s de Freitas Branco">Lu√≠s de Freitas Branco</a> and his student <a href="/wiki/Joly_Braga_Santos" title="Joly Braga Santos">Joly Braga Santos</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fernando_Lopes-Gra%C3%A7a" title="Fernando Lopes-Gra√ßa">Fernando Lopes-Gra√ßa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Emmanuel_Nunes" title="Emmanuel Nunes">Emmanuel Nunes</a> and <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A9rgio_Azevedo" title="S√©rgio Azevedo">S√©rgio Azevedo</a>. Similarly, contemporary composers such as Nuno Malo and Miguel d'Oliveira have achieved some international success writing <a href="/wiki/Film_score" title="Film score">original music for film and television</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Visual_arts">Visual arts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portugal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=49" title="Edit section: Visual arts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:A_Adora%C3%A7%C3%A3o_dos_Magos_(1828)_-_Domingos_Sequeira.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/A_Adora%C3%A7%C3%A3o_dos_Magos_%281828%29_-_Domingos_Sequeira.png/200px-A_Adora%C3%A7%C3%A3o_dos_Magos_%281828%29_-_Domingos_Sequeira.png" width="200" height="145" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/A_Adora%C3%A7%C3%A3o_dos_Magos_%281828%29_-_Domingos_Sequeira.png/300px-A_Adora%C3%A7%C3%A3o_dos_Magos_%281828%29_-_Domingos_Sequeira.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/A_Adora%C3%A7%C3%A3o_dos_Magos_%281828%29_-_Domingos_Sequeira.png/400px-A_Adora%C3%A7%C3%A3o_dos_Magos_%281828%29_-_Domingos_Sequeira.png 2x" data-file-width="2210" data-file-height="1599" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:A_Adora%C3%A7%C3%A3o_dos_Magos_(1828)_-_Domingos_Sequeira.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Domingos_Sequeira" title="Domingos Sequeira">Domingos Sequeira</a> was one the most prolific <a href="/wiki/Neoclassicism" title="Neoclassicism">neoclassical</a> painters. (<i>Adoration of the Magi</i>; 1828).</div>
</div>
</div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_art" title="Portuguese art">Portuguese art</a></div>
<p>Portugal has a <a href="/wiki/List_of_Portuguese_artists" title="List of Portuguese artists">rich history in painting</a>. The first well-known painters date back to the 15th century&#160;‚Äì like <a href="/wiki/Nuno_Gon%C3%A7alves" title="Nuno Gon√ßalves">Nuno Gon√ßalves</a>&#160;‚Äì were part of the Gothic painting period. <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Malhoa" title="Jos√© Malhoa">Jos√© Malhoa</a>, known for his work <i>Fado</i>, and <a href="/wiki/Columbano_Bordalo_Pinheiro" title="Columbano Bordalo Pinheiro">Columbano Bordalo Pinheiro</a> (who painted the portraits of <a href="/wiki/Te%C3%B3filo_Braga" title="Te√≥filo Braga">Te√≥filo Braga</a> and <a href="/wiki/Antero_de_Quental" title="Antero de Quental">Antero de Quental</a>) were both references in <a href="/wiki/Naturalist_school_of_painting" class="mw-redirect" title="Naturalist school of painting">naturalist painting</a>.</p>
<p>The 20th century saw the arrival of <a href="/wiki/Modernism" title="Modernism">Modernism</a>, and along with it came the most prominent Portuguese painters: <a href="/wiki/Amadeo_de_Souza-Cardoso" class="mw-redirect" title="Amadeo de Souza-Cardoso">Amadeo de Souza-Cardoso</a>, who was heavily influenced by French painters, particularly the Delaunays (<a href="/wiki/Robert_Delaunay" title="Robert Delaunay">Robert</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sonia_Delaunay" title="Sonia Delaunay">Sonia</a>). Among his best-known works is <i>Can√ß√£o Popular a Russa e o F√≠garo</i>. Another great modernist painters/writers were <a href="/wiki/Carlos_Botelho" title="Carlos Botelho">Carlos Botelho</a> and <a href="/wiki/Almada_Negreiros" class="mw-redirect" title="Almada Negreiros">Almada Negreiros</a>, friend to the poet <a href="/wiki/Fernando_Pessoa" title="Fernando Pessoa">Fernando Pessoa</a>, who painted his (Pessoa's) portrait. He was deeply influenced by both <a href="/wiki/Cubist" class="mw-redirect" title="Cubist">Cubist</a> and <a href="/wiki/Futurism_(art)" class="mw-redirect" title="Futurism (art)">Futurist</a> trends.</p>
<p>Prominent international figures in visual arts nowadays include painters <a href="/wiki/Vieira_da_Silva" class="mw-redirect" title="Vieira da Silva">Vieira da Silva</a>, <a href="/wiki/J%C3%BAlio_Pomar" title="J√∫lio Pomar">J√∫lio Pomar</a>, Helena Almeida, <a href="/wiki/Joana_Vasconcelos" title="Joana Vasconcelos">Joana Vasconcelos</a>, <a href="/wiki/Juli%C3%A3o_Sarmento" title="Juli√£o Sarmento">Juli√£o Sarmento</a> and <a href="/wiki/Paula_Rego" title="Paula Rego">Paula Rego</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sport">Sport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Portugal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=50" title="Edit section: Sport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sport_in_Portugal" title="Sport in Portugal">Sport in Portugal</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Cristiano_Ronaldo_20120609.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Cristiano_Ronaldo_20120609.jpg/200px-Cristiano_Ronaldo_20120609.jpg" width="200" height="302" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Cristiano_Ronaldo_20120609.jpg/300px-Cristiano_Ronaldo_20120609.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Cristiano_Ronaldo_20120609.jpg/400px-Cristiano_Ronaldo_20120609.jpg 2x" data-file-width="435" data-file-height="656" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Cristiano_Ronaldo_20120609.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Cristiano_Ronaldo" title="Cristiano Ronaldo">Cristiano Ronaldo</a>, from <a href="/wiki/Madeira" title="Madeira">Madeira</a> has been ranked as the best football player in the world.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">Football</a> is the most popular sport in Portugal. There are several football competitions ranging from local amateur to world-class professional level. The legendary <a href="/wiki/Eus%C3%A9bio" title="Eus√©bio">Eus√©bio</a> is still a major symbol of <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_football" class="mw-redirect" title="Portuguese football">Portuguese football</a> history. <a href="/wiki/FIFA_World_Player_of_the_Year" title="FIFA World Player of the Year">FIFA World Player of the Year</a> winners <a href="/wiki/Lu%C3%ADs_Figo" title="Lu√≠s Figo">Lu√≠s Figo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cristiano_Ronaldo" title="Cristiano Ronaldo">Cristiano Ronaldo</a>, who won the <a href="/wiki/FIFA_Ballon_d%27Or" title="FIFA Ballon d'Or">FIFA Ballon d'Or</a>, are two world-class Portuguese football players. Portuguese football managers are also noteworthy, with <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Mourinho" title="Jos√© Mourinho">Jos√© Mourinho</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fernando_Santos_(Portuguese_footballer)" title="Fernando Santos (Portuguese footballer)">Fernando Santos</a> being among the most renowned.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Portugal_national_football_team" title="Portugal national football team">Portugal national football team</a>&#160;‚Äì <i>Sele√ß√£o Nacional</i>&#160;‚Äì have won one <a href="/wiki/UEFA_European_Championship" title="UEFA European Championship">UEFA European Championship</a> title: the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2016" title="UEFA Euro 2016">UEFA Euro 2016</a>, with a 1‚Äì0 victory in the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2016_Final" title="UEFA Euro 2016 Final">final</a> over <a href="/wiki/France_national_football_team" title="France national football team">France</a>, the tournament hosts. In addition, Portugal finished second in the <a href="/wiki/2004_European_Football_Championship" class="mw-redirect" title="2004 European Football Championship">Euro 2004</a> (held in Portugal), third in the <a href="/wiki/1966_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1966 FIFA World Cup">1966 FIFA World Cup</a>, and fourth in the <a href="/wiki/2006_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2006 FIFA World Cup">2006 FIFA World Cup</a>. At youth level, Portugal have won two <a href="/wiki/FIFA_World_Youth_Championship" class="mw-redirect" title="FIFA World Youth Championship">FIFA World Youth Championships</a> (in <a href="/wiki/1989_FIFA_World_Youth_Championship" title="1989 FIFA World Youth Championship">1989</a> and <a href="/wiki/1991_FIFA_World_Youth_Championship" title="1991 FIFA World Youth Championship">1991</a>) and several <a href="/wiki/UEFA" title="UEFA">UEFA</a> European Youth Championships.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/S.L._Benfica" title="S.L. Benfica">S.L. Benfica</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sporting_CP" class="mw-redirect" title="Sporting CP">Sporting CP</a> and <a href="/wiki/FC_Porto" title="FC Porto">FC Porto</a> are the largest <a href="/wiki/Sports_clubs" class="mw-redirect" title="Sports clubs">sports clubs</a> by popularity and by number of trophies won, often known as "<i>os tr√™s grandes</i>" (<a href="/wiki/Big_Three_(Portugal)" title="Big Three (Portugal)">"the big three"</a>). They have won eight titles in the European <a href="/wiki/UEFA" title="UEFA">UEFA</a> club competitions, were present in many finals and have been regular contenders in the last stages almost every season. Other than football, many Portuguese sports clubs, including the "big three", compete in several other sports events with a varying level of success and popularity, these may include <a href="/wiki/Roller_hockey_(quad)" title="Roller hockey (quad)">roller hockey</a>, <a href="/wiki/Basketball" title="Basketball">basketball</a>, <a href="/wiki/Futsal" title="Futsal">futsal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Team_handball" class="mw-redirect" title="Team handball">handball</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Volleyball" title="Volleyball">volleyball</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Football_Federation" title="Portuguese Football Federation">Portuguese Football Federation</a> (FPF) &#160;‚Äì <i>Federa√ß√£o Portuguesa de Futebol</i>&#160;‚Äì annually hosts the <a href="/wiki/Algarve_Cup" title="Algarve Cup">Algarve Cup</a>, a prestigious <a href="/wiki/Women%27s_association_football" title="Women's association football">women`s football</a> tournament that has been celebrated in the Algarvian part of Portugal.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Portugal_national_rugby_union_team" title="Portugal national rugby union team">Portuguese national rugby union team</a> qualified for the <a href="/wiki/2007_Rugby_World_Cup" title="2007 Rugby World Cup">2007 Rugby World Cup</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Portugal_national_rugby_sevens_team" title="Portugal national rugby sevens team">Portuguese national rugby sevens team</a> has played in the <a href="/wiki/World_Rugby_Sevens_Series" title="World Rugby Sevens Series">World Rugby Sevens Series</a>.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:N%C3%A9lson_%C3%89vora_2015.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/N%C3%A9lson_%C3%89vora_2015.jpg/200px-N%C3%A9lson_%C3%89vora_2015.jpg" width="200" height="313" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/N%C3%A9lson_%C3%89vora_2015.jpg/300px-N%C3%A9lson_%C3%89vora_2015.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/N%C3%A9lson_%C3%89vora_2015.jpg/400px-N%C3%A9lson_%C3%89vora_2015.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1360" data-file-height="2128" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:N%C3%A9lson_%C3%89vora_2015.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Nelson_%C3%89vora" title="Nelson √âvora">Nelson √âvora</a> won gold in <a href="/wiki/Athletics_at_the_2008_Summer_Olympics_%E2%80%93_Men%27s_triple_jump" title="Athletics at the 2008 Summer Olympics ‚Äì Men's triple jump">triple jump</a> at the <a href="/wiki/2008_Summer_Olympics" title="2008 Summer Olympics">2008 Beijing Olympics</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/Athletics_(sport)" class="mw-redirect" title="Athletics (sport)">athletics</a>, the Portuguese have won a number of gold, silver and bronze medals in the European, World and Olympic Games competitions. <a href="/wiki/Cycling" title="Cycling">Cycling</a>, with <a href="/wiki/Volta_a_Portugal" title="Volta a Portugal">Volta a Portugal</a> being the most important race, is also a popular sports event and include professional cycling teams such as <a href="/wiki/Sporting_CP" class="mw-redirect" title="Sporting CP">Sporting CP</a>, <a href="/wiki/Boavista_(cycling_team)" class="mw-redirect" title="Boavista (cycling team)">Boavista</a>, <a href="/wiki/Clube_de_Ciclismo_de_Tavira" class="mw-redirect" title="Clube de Ciclismo de Tavira">Clube de Ciclismo de Tavira</a> and <a href="/wiki/Uni%C3%A3o_Ciclista_da_Maia" title="Uni√£o Ciclista da Maia">Uni√£o Ciclista da Maia</a>.</p>
<p>The country has also achieved notable performances in sports like <a href="/wiki/Fencing" title="Fencing">fencing</a>, <a href="/wiki/Judo" title="Judo">judo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kitesurf" class="mw-redirect" title="Kitesurf">kitesurf</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rowing_(sport)" title="Rowing (sport)">rowing</a>, sailing, <a href="/wiki/Surfing" title="Surfing">surfing</a>, shooting, <a href="/wiki/Triathlon" title="Triathlon">triathlon</a> and <a href="/wiki/Windsurf" class="mw-redirect" title="Windsurf">windsurf</a>, owning several European and world titles. The <a href="/wiki/Paralympic" class="mw-redirect" title="Paralympic">paralympic</a> athletes have also conquered many medals in sports like swimming, <a href="/wiki/Boccia" title="Boccia">boccia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wrestling" title="Wrestling">wrestling</a>.</p>
<p>In motorsport, Portugal is internationally noted for the <a href="/wiki/Rally_of_Portugal" class="mw-redirect" title="Rally of Portugal">Rally of Portugal</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Estoril_Circuit" class="mw-redirect" title="Estoril Circuit">Estoril</a>, <a href="/wiki/Algarve_Circuit" class="mw-redirect" title="Algarve Circuit">Algarve Circuits</a> and the revived <a href="/wiki/Porto_Street_Circuit" class="mw-redirect" title="Porto Street Circuit">Porto Street Circuit</a> which holds a stage of the WTCC every two years, as well as for a number of internationally noted pilots in varied <a href="/wiki/Motorsports" class="mw-redirect" title="Motorsports">motorsports</a>.</p>
<p>In equestrian sports, Portugal won the only Horseball-Pato World Championship (in 2006), achieved the third position in the First <a href="/wiki/Horseball" title="Horseball">Horseball</a> World Cup (organized in Ponte de Lima, Portugal, in 2008), and has achieved several victories in the European <a href="/wiki/Working_Equitation" class="mw-redirect" title="Working Equitation">Working Equitation</a> Championship.</p>
<p>In water sports, Portugal has two major sports: <a href="/wiki/Swimming_(sport)" title="Swimming (sport)">swimming</a> and <a href="/wiki/Water_polo" title="Water polo">water polo</a>. Northern Portugal has its own original <a href="/wiki/Martial_art" class="mw-redirect" title="Martial art">martial art</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/Jogo_do_Pau" class="mw-redirect" title="Jogo do Pau">Jogo do Pau</a></i>, in which the fighters use staffs to confront one or several opponents. Other popular sport-related recreational outdoor activities with thousands of enthusiasts nationwide include <a href="/wiki/Airsoft" title="Airsoft">airsoft</a>, fishing, <a href="/wiki/Golf" title="Golf">golf</a>, hiking, hunting and <a href="/wiki/Orienteering" title="Orienteering">orienteering</a>.</p>
<p>Portugal is one of the world's best <a href="/wiki/Golf" title="Golf">golf</a> destinations.<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">[143]</a></sup> It has received several awards by the World Golf Awards.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">[144]</a></sup> Its weather allows play all year round.</p>

<li id="cite_note-10"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-10">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Brian Jenkins, Spyros A. <blockquote class="templatequote">
<p><span class="reference-text">The first thing there is to understand is that in a good measure, the Courts of C√°diz created a new state, the Spanish state.[...]there had never been a proclamation of a Kingdom of Spain, so that difficulties always arose upon the legal value of the very frequent references to 'Spain' in the legal texts of the sixteenth, seventeenth and eighteenth centuries. The Spanish sovereigns had always refused the advice [...] in the sense of establishing a United Kingdom of Spain, preferring to see themselves as vertices of converging scattered kingdoms, at least in theory. Even the Napoleonic Bayonne Constitution of 1808 did not proclaim a kingdom of Spain, but a 'Crown of Spain and the Indies'. On the other hand, 'Spain' was merely a geographical name, a simple romance version of 'Hispania',whereby its use, in principle, should not have to go beyond the designations ‚ÄòGalia‚Äô,‚ÄòGermania‚Äô[...]</span></p>
